The Seven Demands: A Beautiful Feature
Editor highlights Sanusi's elegant editing of the seven demands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate how Sanusi's elegant editing of the seven demands (al-matalib al-sab'a) stands out as a beauty of Sharh al-Wusta.

Core Idea
The seven demands are a hallmark of elegance in Sanusi's creed.

The editor notes that one unique feature of Sharh al-Wusta is Sanusi's graceful treatment of the 'seven demands' (al-matalib al-sab'a). These are key theological inquiries. Sanusi himself remarked that this is one of the beauties of his creed. Let's explore what this means.

Guided Path
1
Locate the mention of seven demands
Find the line in the passage where the editor mentions 'تحريره للمطالب السبعة بطريقة رشيقة'. Read it in Arabic.
2
Understand Sanusi's pride
Notice that Sanusi reportedly said about this feature: 'That is among its beauties, and how many beauties it has!' This shows his own appreciation.
3
Reflect on the style
The phrase 'بطريقة رشيقة' (in an elegant manner) suggests clarity and conciseness. Think about why such editing would be valuable in a theological text.

Source Text

What is in (Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta)? The attention of Imam al-Sanusi was directed to explaining al-Aqida al-Wusta without stopping at every sentence or word, and this commentary was unique in elaborating on issues that the Imam presented briefly elsewhere, even if this presentation was in (Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra), and in presenting issues not found elsewhere. Among that: - Renewed emphasis on the issue of taqlid, with an explanation of the danger of accepting it and attaching it to the rank of hypocrisy; as he narrated from Imam Ibn Dahhaq that hypocrisy is of two types: the muqallid and the second is in the fundamentals of religion, except that he slightly changed what he had gone to in Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra; as he made the school of the majority of theologians on the opinion of some of them the statement of the disbelief of the muqallid, and likewise his criticism of those who wanted to downplay the importance of this issue among his contemporaries like al-Allama Ibn Zakari, and those before him like al-Allama al-Sharif al-Idrisi, and his assertion that whoever knows but does not know how he knows... then he does not know; he only imagines himself knowledgeable, and his rank is conjecture, and his evidence is taqlid. In short: the Imam did not retract in Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta from his opinion concerning the muqallid, his defense of the science of kalam, and his statement that the Companions and those after them from the Salaf were at the highest degree of knowledge and the farthest people from taqlid, and his refutation against the Hashwiyya who are heedless of this reality. That is in description. - His editing of the seven demands in an elegant manner, and he said about this creed of his: 'That is among its beauties, and how many beauties it has!' - The suspension of judgment on the abstract substance, following the Imam al-Muqtarih. - His affirmation of the doctrine of states, following al-Qadi and Imam al-Haramayn. - His inclination to the doctrine of delegation in issues of attributes beyond the seven or eight, following one of the two opinions of Shaykh Abi al-Hasan and Imam al-Haramayn eventually. - His great attention to quoting from two eminent scholars in this field: Imam Ibn Dahhaq, as he frequently quoted from his book 'Nukat al-Irshad', and Imam al-Sa'd.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is an editorial list of distinctive features of Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta. The editor begins by noting that Sanusi's aim was to explain the creed without being overly wordy, and that this commentary uniquely elaborates on issues he treated briefly elsewhere, even in his own Sharh al-Kubra, and includes issues not found elsewhere. Then the editor lists six features: (1) Renewed emphasis on taqlid. Sanusi here intensifies his warning against taqlid, linking it to hypocrisy, and narrates from Ibn Dahhaq that hypocrisy has two types: the muqallid (blind follower) and the second type (actual hypocrisy in fundamentals). He slightly changes his earlier position in Sharh al-Kubra, now attributing to the majority of theologians the view that the muqallid is a disbeliever, and criticizes contemporaries who downplay this issue. He insists that one who knows but does not know how he knows is not truly knowledgeable, and that his rank is only conjecture based on taqlid. The editor notes that Sanusi did not retract his stance on the muqallid. (2) Elegant editing of the seven demands (al-matalib al-sab'a), and Sanusi's own remark that this is one of the beauties of his creed. (3) Suspension of judgment regarding the abstract substance (jawhar mujarrad), following al-Muqtarih. (4) Affirmation of the doctrine of states (ahwal), following al-Qadi and Imam al-Haramayn. (5) Inclination to tafwid (delegation of meaning) regarding attributes beyond the seven or eight, following one of the two opinions of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Imam al-Haramayn in his later view. (6) Extensive reliance on two great scholars: Ibn Dahhaq (especially his book Nukat al-Irshad) and al-Sa'd. Each point shows a unique aspect of this commentary.

Key Terms
مطالب سبعة
رشيقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Sanusi say about his editing of the seven demands?
A) It is too brief.
B) It is one of the beauties of his creed.
C) It is copied from another work.
D) It is controversial.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi considered his elegant treatment of the seven demands a notable beauty of his creed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi called his elegant treatment of the seven demands a 'beauty' of his creed. Do you view the theological truths of Islam as beautiful, or merely as a set of beliefs to affirm? What would change in your heart if you approached every theological question with a sense of awe and admiration for the divine wisdom behind them?
?
The editor highlights that Sanusi took pride in the elegance of his work. When you study or share Islamic knowledge, do you strive for beauty and precision as an act of worship, or do you settle for carelessness? Will you commit to polishing one aspect of your understanding of Aqeedah this week as a sign of reverence?

Suspending Judgment on the Abstract Substance
Sanusi's suspension on the abstract substance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Sanusi suspended judgment regarding the abstract substance (al-jawhar al-mujarrad), following the position of Imam al-Muqtarih.

Core Idea
Sanusi refrains from ruling on the abstract substance, a sign of scholarly caution.

A unique theological stance in Sharh al-Wusta is Sanusi's suspension of judgment (tawaqquf) concerning the 'abstract substance' (al-jawhar al-mujarrad). This refers to a metaphysical entity that is not composed of matter. Sanusi follows Imam al-Muqtarih in not committing to a definitive judgment. Let's examine this point.

Guided Path
1
Read the line about jawhar mujarrad
Find the Arabic line: 'التوقف في الحكم على الجوهر المجرد، تبعاً للعلامة الإمام المقترح'.
2
Understand the concept
The abstract substance is a notion in kalam about a non-material entity. Sanusi's suspension means he neither affirms nor denies certain properties of it.
3
Consider the implication
This shows Sanusi's careful methodology: he adopts a position of caution when evidence is insufficient, following a respected scholar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Affirmation of the Doctrine of States
Sanusi's affirmation of the doctrine of states

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Sanusi affirmed the doctrine of states (ahwal) in Sharh al-Wusta, following al-Qadi and Imam al-Haramayn.

Core Idea
Sanusi adopts the controversial doctrine of states, a distinctive Ash'ari position.

Another unique feature of Sharh al-Wusta is Sanusi's affirmation of the doctrine of states (ahwal). This doctrine posits that attributes (like knowledge, power) are states that are neither existent nor non-existent. Sanusi follows the views of al-Qadi (Abu Bakr al-Baqillani) and Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni). Let's see what this means.

Guided Path
1
Read the line on ahwal
Find the Arabic: 'إثباته القول بالأحوال، تبعاً للقاضي وإمام الحرمين'.
2
Understand the doctrine of ahwal
The term 'ahwal' (states) refers to an intermediate ontological category used to explain divine attributes. It was championed by al-Baqillani and al-Juwayni.
3
Note the significance
By affirming this, Sanusi aligns with a specific Ash'ari school that seeks to balance transcendence with attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Inclination to Tafwid in Attributes
Sanusi's inclination to tafwid for extra attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's inclination to tafwid (delegation of meaning) regarding divine attributes beyond the seven or eight, following Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Imam al-Haramayn.

Core Idea
Sanusi leans toward tafwid for attributes beyond the core seven or eight.

In Sharh al-Wusta, Sanusi shows a tendency towards tafwid (consigning the meaning to Allah) for those divine attributes that go beyond the seven or eight core attributes. He follows one of the two opinions of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Imam al-Haramayn in his later view. This reflects a cautious approach to anthropomorphic interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Read the tafwid passage
Find the line: 'ميله إلى القول بالتفويض في مسائل الصفات الزائدة على السبعة أو الثمانية'
2
Understand tafwid
Tafwid means to delegate the true meaning of certain attributes to Allah, avoiding interpretation. It is a method of dealing with ambiguous verses.
3
Note the scope
Sanusi only applies this to attributes beyond the seven or eight core attributes (like life, knowledge, power). The core attributes are affirmed with interpretation.
4
Identify his authorities
He follows one of two opinions from Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Imam al-Haramayn's later position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ماذا في ( شرح العقيدة الوسطى ) ؟ كانت عناية الإمام السنوسي منصرفةً إلى شرح « العقيدة الوسطى » دون الوقوف على كل جملة من جملها أو كلمة من كلماتها ، وقد انفرد هذا الشرح بإشباع مسائل عرض لها الإمام في غيره إيجازاً ولو كان هذا العرض في ( شرح العقيدة الكبرى ) ، وبإيراد مسائل لا تجدها في غيره ؛ فمن ذلك : - تجديد تشديده في مسألة التقليد ، مع بيان خطورة الأخذ وإلحاقه برتبة النفاق ؛ إذ نقل عن الإمام ابن دهاق بأنَّ النفاق نفاقان ، المقلّد والثاني هو في أصول الدين ، إلا أنَّه غيَّر يسيراً عما ذهب إليه في شرح العقيدة الكبرى » ؛ إذ جعل مذهب جمهور المتكلمين على رأي بعضهم هو القول بكفر المقلد ، وكذا تعييبُهُ على مَنْ أراد أن يهوّنَ شأن هذه المسألة من معاصريه كالعلامة ابن زكري ، ومن سبقه كالعلامة الشريف الإدريسي ، وتأكيده أنَّ مَنْ عَلِمَ ولم يعلم كيف عَلِمَ . . فلم يعلم ؛ إِنَّما توهّم نفسَهُ عالمةً ، ورتبتها الظن ، ودليلها التقليد ، وباختصار : لم يرجع الإمام في شرح العقيدة الوسطى » عن رأيه في مسألة المقلد دفاعه عن علم الكلام ، وبيان أن الصحابة ومن جاء بعدهم من السلف كانوا في أرفع درجة المعرفة ، وأبعد الناس عن التقليد ، وردُّه على الحشوية الذاهلين عن هذه الحقيقة . ذلك في وصف - تحريره للمطالب السبعة بطريقة رشيقة ، وقال عن عقيدته هذه : ( وذلكَ مِنْ محاسنِها ، وكم فيها مِنْ محاسنَ ! ) . - التوقف في الحكم على الجوهر المجرد ، تبعاً للعلامة الإمام المقترح - إثباته القول بالأحوال ، تبعاً للقاضي وإمام الحرمين . - ميله إلى القول بالتفويض في مسائل الصفات الزائدة على السبعة أو الثمانية ، تبعاً لأحد قولي الشيخ أبي الحسن وإمام الحرمين بأخرة . - عنايته البالغةُ بالنقل عن علمين جبلين في هذا العلم ؛ الإمام ابن دهاق ، فقد أكثر النقل عن كتابه « نكت الإرشاد » ، والإمام السعد
What is in (Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta)? The attention of Imam al-Sanusi was directed to explaining al-Aqida al-Wusta without stopping at every sentence or word, and this commentary was unique in elaborating on issues that the Imam presented briefly elsewhere, even if this presentation was in (Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra), and in presenting issues not found elsewhere. Among that: - Renewed emphasis on the issue of taqlid, with an explanation of the danger of accepting it and attaching it to the rank of hypocrisy; as he narrated from Imam Ibn Dahhaq that hypocrisy is of two types: the muqallid and the second is in the fundamentals of religion, except that he slightly changed what he had gone to in Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra; as he made the school of the majority of theologians on the opinion of some of them the statement of the disbelief of the muqallid, and likewise his criticism of those who wanted to downplay the importance of this issue among his contemporaries like al-Allama Ibn Zakari, and those before him like al-Allama al-Sharif al-Idrisi, and his assertion that whoever knows but does not know how he knows... then he does not know; he only imagines himself knowledgeable, and his rank is conjecture, and his evidence is taqlid. In short: the Imam did not retract in Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta from his opinion concerning the muqallid, his defense of the science of kalam, and his statement that the Companions and those after them from the Salaf were at the highest degree of knowledge and the farthest people from taqlid, and his refutation against the Hashwiyya who are heedless of this reality. That is in description. - His editing of the seven demands in an elegant manner, and he said about this creed of his: 'That is among its beauties, and how many beauties it has!' - The suspension of judgment on the abstract substance, following the Imam al-Muqtarih. - His affirmation of the doctrine of states, following al-Qadi and Imam al-Haramayn. - His inclination to the doctrine of delegation in issues of attributes beyond the seven or eight, following one of the two opinions of Shaykh Abi al-Hasan and Imam al-Haramayn eventually. - His great attention to quoting from two eminent scholars in this field: Imam Ibn Dahhaq, as he frequently quoted from his book 'Nukat al-Irshad', and Imam al-Sa'd.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is an editorial list of distinctive features of Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta. The editor begins by noting that Sanusi's aim was to explain the creed without being overly wordy, and that this commentary uniquely elaborates on issues he treated briefly elsewhere, even in his own Sharh al-Kubra, and includes issues not found elsewhere. Then the editor lists six features: (1) Renewed emphasis on taqlid. Sanusi here intensifies his warning against taqlid, linking it to hypocrisy, and narrates from Ibn Dahhaq that hypocrisy has two types: the muqallid (blind follower) and the second type (actual hypocrisy in fundamentals). He slightly changes his earlier position in Sharh al-Kubra, now attributing to the majority of theologians the view that the muqallid is a disbeliever, and criticizes contemporaries who downplay this issue. He insists that one who knows but does not know how he knows is not truly knowledgeable, and that his rank is only conjecture based on taqlid. The editor notes that Sanusi did not retract his stance on the muqallid. (2) Elegant editing of the seven demands (al-matalib al-sab'a), and Sanusi's own remark that this is one of the beauties of his creed. (3) Suspension of judgment regarding the abstract substance (jawhar mujarrad), following al-Muqtarih. (4) Affirmation of the doctrine of states (ahwal), following al-Qadi and Imam al-Haramayn. (5) Inclination to tafwid (delegation of meaning) regarding attributes beyond the seven or eight, following one of the two opinions of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Imam al-Haramayn in his later view. (6) Extensive reliance on two great scholars: Ibn Dahhaq (especially his book Nukat al-Irshad) and al-Sa'd. Each point shows a unique aspect of this commentary.

Key Terms
تفويض
صفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Sanusi applies tafwid to all attributes.
Correction: He applies tafwid only to attributes beyond the core seven or eight, showing a nuanced position.

Checkpoint
To which attributes does Sanusi apply tafwid in Sharh al-Wusta?
A) All divine attributes.
B) Only the seven core attributes.
C) Attributes beyond the seven or eight.
D) Only the attribute of istiwa'.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi adopts tafwid for extra attributes, following Ash'ari and al-Juwayni's later view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter an attribute of Allah that you cannot fully comprehend, do you feel content to simply affirm it and delegate its reality to Allah, or do you feel an inner pressure to explain it? What does that reveal about your trust in Allah's knowledge over your own?
?
Sanusi adopted tafwid for extra attributes after studying the later view of scholars. Is there a theological or practical belief you hold that you are afraid to question or refine because it feels safer? How might God be calling you to intellectual humility?
?
The source says Sanusi followed 'one of the two opinions' of earlier scholars. In your own life, when you face two valid opinions, do you choose based on what is easier or what requires more submission? Which choice would bring you closer to Allah?

Reliance on Ibn Dahhaq and al-Sa'd
Sanusi's reliance on Ibn Dahhaq and al-Sa'd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate Sanusi's extensive quotation from two major scholars: Ibn Dahhaq (Nukat al-Irshad) and al-Sa'd, as a distinctive feature of Sharh al-Wusta.

Core Idea
Sanusi heavily relies on Ibn Dahhaq and al-Sa'd as his primary sources.

A final unique feature highlighted by the editor is Sanusi's great attention to quoting from two eminent scholars: Imam Ibn Dahhaq, especially from his book Nukat al-Irshad, and Imam al-Sa'd. This shows the commentary's scholarly foundation. Let's explore this aspect.

Guided Path
1
Read the relevant line
Find the Arabic: 'عنايته البالغةُ بالنقل عن علمين جبلين في هذا العلم؛ الإمام ابن دهاق... والإمام السعد'
2
Identify the two scholars
Ibn Dahhaq is the author of Nukat al-Irshad, and al-Sa'd is another major scholar. Both are described as 'two mountains' (علمين جبلين) in this science.
3
Understand the method
Sanusi frequently quotes from their works, indicating his reliance on their authority and the influence they had on his commentary.

The Imam's Creedal Choices
Lists the Imam's four creedal positions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific doctrinal positions adopted by the Imam in his creed, including his editing of the seven demands, suspension on the abstract substance, affirmation of states, and inclination toward tafwid in attributes.

Core Idea
The Imam's creed is a refined Ash'ari synthesis carefully selected from earlier authorities.

In this passage, the commentator lists several of the Imam's distinctive creedal choices. These include his graceful editing of the seven demands, his suspension of judgment on the abstract substance, his affirmation of the doctrine of states (ahwal), and his inclination toward tafwid (consignment) regarding attributes beyond the essential seven or eight. Each position reflects his adherence to the Ash'ari tradition and his careful selection from earlier scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text first, then the translation, to get the overall list of positions.
Notice the structure: each position is introduced with a dash.
2
Identify each position
Count how many distinct positions are mentioned. There are four. Name each one.
3
Understand the authorities cited
For each position, note which earlier scholar(s) the Imam follows. This shows his reliance on tradition.
The authorities are: al-Muqtarah, al-Qadi, Imam al-Haramayn, Shaykh Abu al-Hasan.
4
Reflect on the method
Ask yourself why the Imam chooses these specific positions. They are not innovations but careful selections.
This connects to the Ash'ari school's internal diversity.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك في وصف - تحريره للمطالب السبعة بطريقة رشيقة ، وقال عن عقيدته هذه : ( وذلكَ مِنْ محاسنِها ، وكم فيها مِنْ محاسنَ ! ) . - التوقف في الحكم على الجوهر المجرد ، تبعاً للعلامة الإمام المقترح · - إثباته القول بالأحوال ، تبعاً للقاضي وإمام الحرمين . - ميله إلى القول بالتفويض في مسائل الصفات الزائدة على السبعة أو الثمانية ، تبعاً لأحد قولي الشيخ أبي الحسن وإمام الحرمين بأخرة . - عنايته البالغةُ بالنقل عن علمين جبلين في هذا العلم ؛ الإمام ابن دهاق ، فقد أكثر النقل عن كتابه « نكت الإرشاد » ، والإمام السعد التفتازاني ، وأكثر النقل بإسهاب ، وبإحالة وغير إحالة ؛ عن كتابه شرح المقاصد » ، ولا سيما الأبحاث الأخيرة .
That is in description: his editing of the seven demands in a graceful manner, and he said about this creed of his: 'That is among its merits, and how many merits it has!' - his suspension of judgment on the abstract substance (al-jawhar al-mujarrad), following al-Allama al-Imam al-Muqtarah. - his affirmation of the doctrine of states (al-ahwal), following al-Qadi and Imam al-Haramayn. - his inclination toward the doctrine of tafwid (consignment) in matters of attributes beyond seven or eight, following one of the two sayings of Shaykh Abu al-Hasan and Imam al-Haramayn in the latter period. - his great attention to quoting from two monumental scholars in this science: Imam Ibn Dahaq, as he frequently quoted from his book Nukat al-Irshad, and Imam Saad al-Taftazani, and he frequently quoted at length, with and without referral, from his book Sharh al-Maqasid, especially the later investigations.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage describes several of the Imam's creedal positions and his scholarly methodology. First, he edited the al-matalib al-sab'a (the seven demands) in a graceful way, and he praised his own creed (likely his al-Aqida al-Wusta) as having many merits. Second, he suspended judgment on the abstract substance (al-jawhar al-mujarrad), following al-Imam al-Muqtarah. Third, he affirmed the Ash'ari doctrine of ahwal (states), following al-Qadi (al-Baqillani) and Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni). Fourth, he inclined towards tafwid (consignment of meaning to God) in attributes beyond the seven or eight essential attributes, following one of the two opinions of Shaykh Abu al-Hasan (al-Ash'ari) and Imam al-Haramayn in his later period. Fifth, he heavily relied on two great authorities: Ibn Dahaq (author of Nukat al-Irshad) and al-Taftazani (author of Sharh al-Maqasid), citing them extensively and at length, especially in later discussions. This shows the Imam's adherence to the Ash'ari tradition and his method of using authoritative texts.

Key Terms
المطالب السبعة
الجوهر المجرد
الأحوال
التفويض
الصفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Imam's positions were arbitrary or innovative.
Correction: Each position is carefully chosen from established Ash'ari authorities, showing his adherence to tradition.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following positions did the Imam adopt?
A) Affirmation of the abstract substance without suspension.
B) Denial of the doctrine of states (ahwal).
C) Inclination towards tafwid in attributes beyond seven or eight.
D) Rejection of all Ash'ari positions.

Key Takeaway
The Imam's creedal positions are a deliberate selection from the Ash'ari tradition, reflecting his method of adhering to authoritative predecessors.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How do you approach complex theological matters? Do you rely on careful study and tradition, or do you form opinions hastily? This lesson shows the Imam's deliberate selection from authorities. What areas of your faith have you investigated with the same seriousness? Are there aspects where you simply accept what is common without deep reflection? Write one commitment to study a creedal issue with more diligence.
?
The Imam praised his own creed, saying 'That is among its merits.' Do you have confidence in your understanding of Islamic creed based on solid evidence, or are you uncertain about foundational beliefs? What steps can you take this week to solidify your conviction on one attribute of Allah?
?
Notice how the Imam followed respected scholars like al-Qadi and al-Juwayni. Are you actively seeking knowledge from reliable sources, or are you relying on social media or weak opinions? How can you align yourself more closely with the tradition of the Salaf in your learning?

The Imam's Reliance on Ibn Dahaq and al-Taftazani
Describes the Imam's reliance on Ibn Dahaq and al-Taftazani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Imam's heavy reliance on two key scholars, Ibn Dahaq and al-Taftazani, and how he used their works in his creedal writing.

Core Idea
The Imam's scholarship was deeply grounded in the works of Ibn Dahaq and al-Taftazani.

The passage concludes by noting the Imam's extensive citation of two major authorities: Imam Ibn Dahaq, from whose book Nukat al-Irshad he frequently quoted, and Imam Saad al-Taftazani, from whose Sharh al-Maqasid he quoted at length, both with and without explicit referral, especially in later investigations. This shows his method of relying on established commentaries.

Guided Path
1
Read the relevant part of the passage
Focus on the section that mentions the two scholars. Read the Arabic and translation.
2
Identify the two scholars and their works
Name the scholars and the books cited. Note the full titles.
Ibn Dahaq wrote Nukat al-Irshad; al-Taftazani wrote Sharh al-Maqasid.
3
Understand the manner of quoting
The passage says he quoted frequently, at length, with and without referral. What does 'with and without referral' mean?
Referral means citing the source explicitly; without referral means using the material without naming it.
4
Note the emphasis on later investigations
The passage says 'especially the later investigations'. This indicates where the Imam relied most on these authorities.
This shows the structure of his work: he built upon earlier commentators in later parts.

ذلك في وصف - تحريره للمطالب السبعة بطريقة رشيقة ، وقال عن عقيدته هذه : ( وذلكَ مِنْ محاسنِها ، وكم فيها مِنْ محاسنَ ! ) . - التوقف في الحكم على الجوهر المجرد ، تبعاً للعلامة الإمام المقترح · - إثباته القول بالأحوال ، تبعاً للقاضي وإمام الحرمين . - ميله إلى القول بالتفويض في مسائل الصفات الزائدة على السبعة أو الثمانية ، تبعاً لأحد قولي الشيخ أبي الحسن وإمام الحرمين بأخرة . - عنايته البالغةُ بالنقل عن علمين جبلين في هذا العلم ؛ الإمام ابن دهاق ، فقد أكثر النقل عن كتابه « نكت الإرشاد » ، والإمام السعد التفتازاني ، وأكثر النقل بإسهاب ، وبإحالة وغير إحالة ؛ عن كتابه شرح المقاصد » ، ولا سيما الأبحاث الأخيرة .
That is in description: his editing of the seven demands in a graceful manner, and he said about this creed of his: 'That is among its merits, and how many merits it has!' - his suspension of judgment on the abstract substance (al-jawhar al-mujarrad), following al-Allama al-Imam al-Muqtarah. - his affirmation of the doctrine of states (al-ahwal), following al-Qadi and Imam al-Haramayn. - his inclination toward the doctrine of tafwid (consignment) in matters of attributes beyond seven or eight, following one of the two sayings of Shaykh Abu al-Hasan and Imam al-Haramayn in the latter period. - his great attention to quoting from two monumental scholars in this science: Imam Ibn Dahaq, as he frequently quoted from his book Nukat al-Irshad, and Imam Saad al-Taftazani, and he frequently quoted at length, with and without referral, from his book Sharh al-Maqasid, especially the later investigations.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage describes several of the Imam's creedal positions and his scholarly methodology. First, he edited the al-matalib al-sab'a (the seven demands) in a graceful way, and he praised his own creed (likely his al-Aqida al-Wusta) as having many merits. Second, he suspended judgment on the abstract substance (al-jawhar al-mujarrad), following al-Imam al-Muqtarah. Third, he affirmed the Ash'ari doctrine of ahwal (states), following al-Qadi (al-Baqillani) and Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni). Fourth, he inclined towards tafwid (consignment of meaning to God) in attributes beyond the seven or eight essential attributes, following one of the two opinions of Shaykh Abu al-Hasan (al-Ash'ari) and Imam al-Haramayn in his later period. Fifth, he heavily relied on two great authorities: Ibn Dahaq (author of Nukat al-Irshad) and al-Taftazani (author of Sharh al-Maqasid), citing them extensively and at length, especially in later discussions. This shows the Imam's adherence to the Ash'ari tradition and his method of using authoritative texts.

Key Terms
نكت الإرشاد
شرح المقاصد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Imam's creed was based solely on his own reasoning.
Correction: The passage shows he heavily relied on two major scholars and their works.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, from which book did the Imam frequently quote Ibn Dahaq?
A) Sharh al-Maqasid
B) Nukat al-Irshad
C) al-Matalib al-Sab'a
D) al-Aqida al-Wusta

Key Takeaway
The Imam's creed is heavily informed by the works of Ibn Dahaq and al-Taftazani, especially in later discussions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Imam quoted from Ibn Dahaq and al-Taftazani with such mastery that he sometimes cited them and sometimes did not. In what area of your Islamic knowledge have you reached a point where you no longer need to constantly refer back to sources because you have truly internalized them? Where are you still relying on crutches?
?
Notice that the Imam's deepest reliance on these scholars came in his 'later investigations'. As you grow older in faith, do your studies become deeper and more rooted in primary texts, or do you remain content with surface-level understanding? What would it take for you to engage with a work like Sharh al-Maqasid directly, and what is holding you back?

How a Critical Edition Is Made
Editor describes the editorial methodology for the critical edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meticulous editorial methodology used in preparing a critical edition of a classical Islamic theological text, as exemplified by the editor of Sanusi's Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta.

Core Idea
A critical edition is a scholarly reconstruction, not a simple copy.

The preface of a critical edition often reveals the painstaking work behind the text. Here, the editor of Sanusi's Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta explains his method: collating many manuscripts, adding vocalization and numbering, attributing citations, sourcing reports, adding annotations, and recording variants. This lesson unpacks that methodology, showing how scholars ensure the text is reliable and accessible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of the editor's approach. Then read the English translation to clarify unfamiliar terms.
Notice the sequence of editorial tasks mentioned.
2
Identify the key editorial tasks
List each task the editor performed: using many manuscripts, collating, vocalizing, numbering, attributing citations, sourcing reports, adding annotations, noting variants, and preparing front matter.
There are about eight distinct actions.
3
Reflect on why each task matters
For each task, ask yourself: why is this important for a reliable edition? For example, vocalization prevents misreading, attribution shows respect for sources, and variants alert readers to textual ambiguities.
Think about the Quranic concept of i'rab—proper vocalization preserves meaning.
4
Consider the role of annotations and variants
The editor added annotations from al-Saffaqisi's commentary and recorded variant readings. Why? To provide additional insight and to acknowledge that even the editor may have missed something during work.
Variant readings are rare but show intellectual honesty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منهج العمال في الكتاب
نُسَخُ شرح العقيدة الوسطى ( ملأت دورَ المخطوطات بحمد الله وفضله ، غير أنها كما ظهر بعد تطويل النظر شبه متكافئة ، لا تفضل إحداهن أختها إلا بسبقِ زمان ، أو جزيِ قلم بتعليق وفائدة لبعض أهل العرفان ، ولذا فقد أعذرنا حينما أكثرنا من الأصول الخطية له ؛ عسى أن تنفع واحدة منها نفعاً لا يُرى في أخرى .
وقد قوبلت نسخه الخطيَّة الرئيسة ، وحُرِّرَ نصُّهُ على أوفق الوجوه ، وكان لبعض النسخ دور رئيس في إثراء وتوضيح مقاطعه
وجُمله
•
وكان من جملة العنايات العامة أنْ شُكل شكلاً إعرابياً تاماً ، ورُقّم بمنهج ترقيم مريح ، وعُزيت نقوله إلى مصادرها الأم ، ولا سيما كلام الإمام ابن دهاق ، كما خُرِّجَت آثارُهُ وأخباره من دواوين السنة والآثار وكتب التاريخ ، وأضيفت له بعض التعليقات من حاشية العلامة الصفاقسي عليه ؛ زيادةً في النفع ، وأثبتَتْ على ندرة بعضُ المغايرات التي قد تشي بفهم غاب ساعة العمل ، إضافة إلى إعداد المقدمات المألوفة ؛ من ترجمة للمؤلّف وتعريف بالكتاب ، وفهرسة
لمحتواه
Methodology of the work in the book. Copies of 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta' filled the libraries of manuscripts, praise be to Allah and His grace. However, they were, as appeared after prolonged examination, nearly equivalent, none surpassing its sister except by precedence of time or a pen's jotting with a comment and benefit from some people of gnosis. Therefore we excused ourselves when we used many of its manuscript sources, hoping that one of them may provide benefit not seen in another. And the main manuscript copies were collated, and its text was edited in the most appropriate manner, and some copies had a major role in enriching and clarifying its sections and sentences. And among the general attentions was that it was fully vocalized with i'rab, and numbered with a convenient numbering scheme, and its citations were attributed to their original sources, especially the words of Imam Ibn Dahaq. Also, its reports and narrations were sourced from the compilations of Sunnah, reports, and books of history. And some annotations from the commentary of al-Saffaqisi were added for increased benefit. And on rare occasions, some variant readings were recorded that may indicate an understanding that was absent at the time of editing. In addition to preparing the customary introductions: a biography of the author, a description of the book, and a table of contents.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is the editor's description of the editorial methodology. It explains that numerous manuscripts of Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta exist, but they are roughly equivalent, differing mainly in age or occasional marginalia. The editor used many manuscripts, hoping each contributes unique value. The main copies were collated and the text edited optimally. Special care was given to full vocalization, clear numbering, and proper citation attribution, particularly for statements of Imam Ibn Dahaq. Reports were traced back to original hadith and history works. Annotations from al-Saffaqisi's commentary were added. Variant readings were recorded when they might indicate a lost understanding. Finally, standard front matter was added: author biography, book description, and index.

Key Terms
مخطوطة (manuscript)
تحرير (editing)
ترقيم (numbering)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Having many manuscripts automatically yields a superior text.
Correction: The editor notes that the manuscripts are 'nearly equivalent,' and careful collation and additional scholarly work (vocalization, annotation, attribution) are necessary to produce a reliable edition.

Checkpoint
What did the editor add from the commentary of al-Saffaqisi?
A) New chapters
B) Annotations
C) A complete translation
D) A biography of the author

Key Takeaway
A reliable critical edition requires collation, vocalization, numbering, attribution, sourcing, annotation, and recording of variants, not just reliance on many manuscripts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The editor used many manuscripts, hoping each offers something the other lacks. In your own learning about Allah, do you rely on a single teacher or book, or do you seek diverse sources to enrich your understanding? What might you be missing by limiting your sources?
?
The editor recorded variant readings that 'may indicate an understanding that was absent at the time of editing.' When you encounter a different interpretation of a core aqeedah issue, is your first instinct to reject it because it contradicts what you know, or to consider it as a possible insight you had missed? Will you humble yourself to learn?
?
The editor carefully vocalized and numbered the text for clarity. When you read a sacred text, do you take the time to understand it properly, or do you rush through it superficially? How much care do you give to the words of Allah and His Messenger, knowing that scholars labored to present them accurately?

The Purpose of Sanusi's Concise Statements
Sanusi states the purpose of his concise summaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's stated goal for his treatise: to transition the responsible believer from disputed imitation to universally accepted correct reasoning.

Core Idea
Sanusi writes to replace imitation with reasoned conviction.

Sanusi opens his work with a clear declaration of intent. He does not begin with theological arguments but with a methodological statement: this book is a tool for leaving behind the uncertainty of blind following and entering the certainty of rational inquiry. As we read, notice how he presents this not as a mere suggestion but as a structured path.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the formal opening (basmalah, praise, prayer) and then the key phrase 'wa ba‘d' that signals the main text.
Pay attention to the author's full name and lineage—it establishes his scholarly authority.
2
Identify the two states: taqlid and nazar
Find where Sanusi contrasts 'taqlid' (imitation) and 'nazar' (reasoning). Understand that taqlid is following without evidence, while nazar is seeking correct reasoning.
Sanusi uses the verbs 'takhruj' (emerges) and 'ilā' (to) to show movement from one state to the other.
3
Note the disagreement and consensus
Sanusi says there is disagreement (mukhtalif fihi) about the faith of one who follows taqlid, but consensus (mujma‘ ‘alayhi) for one who practices correct reasoning. Reflect on why this distinction matters for the mukallaf (responsible person).
This directly links the purpose of the book to a key theological issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم وصلى الله على سيدنا ومولانا محمد على آله وصحبه وسلم تسليما كثيرا
قال الشيخ الإمام العالم المتفنن أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف السنوسي الحسني ، لطف الله به وبكل من انتمى إليه :
الحمد لله رب العالمين ، والصلاة والسلام على سيدنا ومولانا محمد خاتم النبيين وإمام المرسلين ، ورضي الله تعالى عن أصحاب رسول الله أجمعين ، ومن تبعهم بإحسان إلى يوم الدين .
وبعد :
فهذه جمل مختصرة تخرج المكلف بفهمها إن شاء الله تعالى من التقليد المختلف في إيمان صاحبه .. إلى النظر الصحيح المجمع على إيمان صاحبه
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. And may Allah bless our master Muhammad and his family and companions and grant abundant peace. The chief, the imam, the scholar, the versatile, Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Sanusi al-Hasani – may Allah be kind to him and to everyone who belongs to him – said: Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and prayer and peace be upon our master Muhammad, the seal of the prophets and the imam of the messengers, and may Allah be pleased with all the companions of the Messenger of Allah and those who follow them with excellence until the Day of Judgment. And after: These are concise statements; by understanding them, the responsible person (mukallaf) will – if Allah wills – leave the imitation (taqlid) concerning which there is disagreement about the faith of its adherent… to correct reasoning (nazar) concerning which there is consensus about the faith of its adherent.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the book. It begins with the basmalah and a prayer for the Prophet, followed by the author's self-introduction with his full name and lineage: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Sanusi al-Hasani, asking Allah's kindness for himself and all who follow him. Then he praises Allah and sends salaams upon the Prophet and his companions. The phrase 'wa ba‘d' (and after) signals the main text. Here Sanusi states the purpose of his work: it consists of concise statements ('jumal mukhtasarah') that, when understood, will bring the mukallaf (the legally responsible person) out of taqlid (imitation) – which is disputed regarding the validity of the iman (faith) of its adherent – into nazar sahih (correct reasoning), which is agreed upon. This clearly establishes the work as a tool for achieving certain knowledge in theology through rational inquiry, moving from blind following to reasoned conviction.

Key Terms
المكلف
التقليد
النظر
إيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that taqlid (imitation) is always acceptable in matters of belief and that one can remain in blind following without consequence.
Correction: Sanusi indicates that taqlid is a state to be left behind because there is disagreement about the faith of its adherent, whereas correct reasoning brings consensus. This implies that true faith requires reasoned conviction.

Checkpoint
What is the stated purpose of the concise statements in this book according to Sanusi?
A) To teach rhetoric and debate
B) To bring the mukallaf from taqlid to correct reasoning
C) To summarize the biographies of scholars
D) To refute heretical sects

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's concise statements are designed to bring the believer out of imitation and into sound reasoning, which is the only path to certain faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a core belief you hold about Allah or the Prophet. Have you ever personally examined the rational evidence for it, or do you simply trust what you were taught? Are you prepared to do the work of nazar to turn that belief into certain conviction?
?
Sanusi says that faith based on imitation is a matter of disagreement among scholars. Does this unsettle you? Will you seek to understand the proofs behind your own faith so that you are not relying on something disputed?
?
What is stopping you from moving from taqlid to nazar? Fear of doubt? Lack of time? Comfort in tradition? Identify one belief you will investigate with the intention of confirming it through reason, starting today.

Purpose of the Book: From Taqlid to Nazar
Sanusi states the purpose of his book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's stated aim for writing his book and the significance of moving from taqlid to nazar in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Sanusi's book is a concise guide to transform imitation into reasoned faith.

Sanusi opens his work with a clear statement of intent. He explains that these 'concise sentences' are designed to bring the believer out of the disputed state of taqlid and into the agreed-upon certainty of nazar. This sets the stage for the entire theological method he will employ.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the traditional opening: basmala, praise, author's name, and transition 'wa ba'd'.
Pay attention to the formulaic structure that signals a new work.
2
Identify the purpose statement
Locate the sentence that begins with 'فهذهِ جُمَلٌ مختصرةٌ' (These are concise sentences). This is the core purpose.
The purpose is to bring the mukallaf from taqlid to nazar.
3
Understand key terms: taqlid and nazar
Taqlid is imitation without evidence; nazar is reasoned reflection. Note their statuses: taqlid is disputed in terms of faith, nazar is unanimously accepted.
Sanusi aims to achieve consensus by guiding to nazar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الله الرحمن الرحيم
وصلی اللہ علی سیدنا و مولانا محمد على آله وصحبه وسلم تسليما كثيرا
قالَ الشيخ الإمامُ العالمُ المتفنِّنُ ؛ أبو عبدِ اللهِ محمدُ بنُ يوسف السنوسي الحسني ، لطف الله بهِ وبكلِّ مَنِ انتمى إليه :
الحمدُ للهِ ربِّ العالمينَ ، والصلاة والسلام على سيدنا ومولانا محمد خاتم النبيِّينَ وإمامِ المرسلين ، ورضي الله تعالى عنْ أَصحابِ رسولِ اللهِ أجمعينَ ، ومَنْ تبعهم بإحسانٍ إلى يومِ الدِّينِ .
وبعد :
فهذهِ جُمَلٌ مختصرةٌ تُخْرِجُ المكلَّفَ بفهمها إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ تعالى مِنَ التقليدِ المُختلفِ في إيمان صاحبه .. إلى النظرِ الصحيحِ المُجمعِ على إيمانِ صاحبِهِ
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. And may Allah bless our master and patron Muhammad and his family and companions and grant them abundant peace. The learned, accomplished Imam, Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Sanusi al-Hasani – may Allah be kind to him and to all who are attached to him – said: Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and blessings and peace be upon our master and patron Muhammad, the seal of the prophets and the imam of the messengers, and may Allah be pleased with all the companions of the Messenger of Allah and those who followed them in excellence until the Day of Judgment. To proceed: These are concise sentences which, by understanding them – Allah willing – bring the mukallaf (legally responsible person) out of taqlid (imitation) concerning which there is dispute about the faith of its practitioner, to correct nazar (research/reflection) concerning which there is consensus on the faith of its practitioner.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is an introduction and statement of purpose. Sanusi begins with the basmala and praise of the Prophet, then gives his full name and lineage. He then praises Allah and sends blessings on the Prophet and his companions. After this, he says 'To proceed' (wa ba'd), a standard transition. He then declares the purpose of his book: these concise sentences (jumal mukhtasara) are intended, by Allah's will, to bring the mukallaf – the person legally responsible for observing religious duties – out of taqlid (imitation) and into nazar (correct research). The key point is that taqlid is disputed: scholars disagree whether the faith of a person who merely imitates is valid. But nazar leads to certain faith upon which there is consensus. Thus Sanusi's aim is to provide a brief yet sufficient guide to reasoned theological reflection that secures agreed-upon faith.

Key Terms
تقليد
نظر
مكلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all forms of taqlid are invalid.
Correction: Sanusi specifically refers to 'disputed taqlid', implying some forms of taqlid may be considered valid; he aims to move to nazar, which is universally accepted.

Checkpoint
What is the stated purpose of Sanusi's book?
A) To present arguments against the existence of God
B) To lead the mukallaf from disputed taqlid to agreed-upon nazar
C) To refute all philosophers
D) To provide a comprehensive history of kalam

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's book aims to lead the mukallaf from the disputed imitation of taqlid to the certain faith of correct nazar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely on imitation (taqlid) for any of your core beliefs? Which belief would you be most afraid to examine critically, and why?
?
Sanusi claims that understanding this concise book can move you from disputed to agreed-upon faith. What is stopping you from engaging deeply with it today?
?
If the validity of your faith is at stake in the choice between taqlid and nazar, what concrete step will you take this week to begin the journey of reflection (nazar)?

Sanusi's Preface: The Difficulty of the Age
Sanusi explains the purpose of his work and the challenges of his era.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's motivation for writing and the spiritual challenges of his time that hinder the study of creed.

Core Idea
The chief obstacle to knowledge today is a heart clouded by love of the world.

Sanusi wrote his creed and commentary, but not everyone could benefit. In this preface, he reflects on the spiritual decay of his era and identifies the rarest and most difficult combination: intelligence with good intention, yet still prone to worldly distraction. This lesson explores his diagnosis and its implications for seeking knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage aloud
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Let the author's own voice set the tone before analyzing.
Notice the emotive language: 'calamity', 'darkness of trials', 'rust of sins'.
2
Identify the key problem
Sanusi describes two groups: those who found the creed difficult and those who found the commentary lengthy. He then explains the underlying cause: hearts corrupted by trials and sins.
This is the context for his diagnosis.
3
Examine the strangest phenomenon
The strangest challenge is the combination of intelligence with good intention, yet worldly attachment. Sanusi says such a person cannot benefit from higher sciences.
Reflect on why worldly love undermines knowledge.

وبعد : فلمَّا مَنَّ الله سبحانه وتعالى عليَّ بوضع العقيدة المسماة بـ « عقيدة أهل التوحيدِ (۱) ، ووضع شرحها المسمى بـ « عمدة أهل التوفيق والتسديد » . . استصعب العقيدةَ أُناسٌ ، واستطال الشرحَ آخرونَ ، والكلُّ في هذا الزمان الذي قلَّ خيرُهُ واستعسر ، وكثُرَ شره واستيسر . . مُصدَّقون فيما يدَّعونَ ؛ إذ المصيبة في زماننا هذا قد تمكَّنَتْ مِنَ القلوب حتى امتنعَتْ مِنْ حُسْنِ الاستماع ، فضلاً عن الفهم والانتفاع لِمَا تراكم عليها مِنْ ظلماتِ الفتنِ ورانِ الذنوب ، فإِنَّا للهِ وإِنَّا إِلَيهِ راجعون . وأغرب شيءٍ في هذا الزمانِ وأصعبُهُ : اجتماع ذكاء فهم معَ حَسْنِ نيَّة ، وسَعْيِ فيما يعني وهجرٍ للعوائد التي قادَتْ إلى كلٌّ بليَّةٍ ، وإِنَّما الذكي اليوم مبتلى في الغالبِ بحب الدنيا والسعي لها ، وعدم الاهتبال بالآخرة (۲) ، ومثلُ هذا ليسَ أهلاً لأن يفيد أو يُفادَ شيئاً مِنْ نفائس العلوم الفاخرة ؛ لأنَّهُ على تقدير أن يحصل له شيءٌ منها إِنَّما يَتَّخِذُهُ (۱) وهي أول عقائده وضعاً ، وقد اشتهرت من قبل المصنف وغيره بـ « العقيدة الكبرى » ، وقد ذكرها المصنف كما ستراه ( ص ٢١٢ ) ، وأما الزيادة المشهورة : « المخرجة بعون الله من ظلمات الجهل والتقليد ، المرغمة بفضل الله تعالى أنف كل مبتدع عنيد » فهي أوصاف لإظهار عظم شأنها ، نبَّهَ على ذلك كلّهِ العلامة إسماعيل الحامدي في ) حواشيه » عليها ( ص ٥٠٧ ) . (۲) الاهتبال : الاغتنام ، والاعتناء بالشيء
And after: When God, glorified and exalted, bestowed upon me the composition of the creed named 'The Creed of the People of Tawhid' (1), and the composition of its commentary named 'The Support of the People of Success and Guidance'... some people found the creed difficult, and others found the commentary lengthy, and all of them in this time, whose good has become scarce and hard, and whose evil has become abundant and easy, are believed in what they claim, for the calamity in our time has taken hold of hearts to the point that they have refrained from good listening, let alone understanding and benefiting, due to what has accumulated upon them of the darkness of trials and the rust of sins. Indeed, we belong to God and to Him we return. And the strangest thing in this time and the most difficult is the combination of intelligent understanding with good intention, and striving in what matters, and abandoning habits that have led to every calamity. Indeed, the intelligent person today is mostly afflicted with love of the world and striving for it, and lack of concern for the Hereafter (2). And such a person is not fit to benefit or be benefited with any of the precious lofty sciences, because even if he were to attain something of them, he would only take it (for worldly purposes). (1) It is his first creed composition, and it became well-known before the author and others as 'The Greater Creed', and the author mentioned it as you will see (p. 212). As for the famous addition: 'The one extracted with the help of God from the darkness of ignorance and imitation, the one that humiliates, by God's grace, the nose of every stubborn innovator' – these are descriptions to show its great status. All of that was noted by the scholar Ismail al-Hamidi in his footnotes on it (p. 507). (2) al-ightibāl: to take advantage, to care for something.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface explaining the context of his work. Sanusi states that after writing his creed 'Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid' and its commentary 'Umdat Ahl al-Tawfiq wa al-Tasdid', some found the creed difficult and others found the commentary lengthy. He sympathizes with them, attributing this to the spiritual decline of the age: hearts have become corrupt due to trials and sins, unable to listen well. Then he identifies the strangest and most difficult phenomenon: the combination of intelligence with good intention and sincere effort, and abandonment of harmful habits. He notes that most intelligent people are preoccupied with worldly love and neglect the Hereafter, and such people are not worthy of benefiting from precious sciences because they would misuse them. The footnotes clarify that 'Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid' is his first creed, known as 'al-Aqida al-Kubra', and provide an additional description of it.

Key Terms
العقيدة
النيَّة
الاهتبال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sanusi is criticizing all intelligent people.
Correction: Sanusi specifies that he is referring to those whose intelligence is coupled with love of the world and lack of concern for the Hereafter, not all intelligent people.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the strangest and most difficult thing in his time?
A) The lack of intelligence among people
B) The combination of intelligence with good intention and effort
C) The length of his commentary
D) The abundance of worldly goods

Key Takeaway
Sanusi teaches that intellectual ability alone is insufficient; it must be paired with sincere intention and detachment from worldly desires to benefit from sacred knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi says that 'the intelligent person today is mostly afflicted with love of the world and striving for it, and lack of concern for the Hereafter.' Look at your own life right now: what is the one worldly ambition that quietly consumes most of your thoughts and energy? Are you willing to abandon it for the sake of the Hereafter, or does the thought of letting it go terrify you? What is one concrete step you can take today to shift your concern toward the Hereafter?
?
He also mentions that hearts have accumulated 'darkness of trials and rust of sins' to the point that they cannot even listen properly. When was the last time you truly listened to a Quran recitation or a religious lesson with a heart free from distractions? What specific sin or attachment in your life is creating that rust, and how can you begin to polish your heart today through repentance and turning away from it?
?
Sanusi validates the complaint that his creed is difficult, but attributes it to the spiritual state of the age, not to the text itself. When you encounter difficulty in learning your faith, do you tend to blame the teacher, the book, or your own heart? How can you take responsibility for softening your heart so that knowledge can enter?

Lamenting the Corrupt Time and Advising Seclusion
Sanusi laments the rarity of the pious in his time and advises seclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the severity of the corrupt time as described by Sanusi and the rationale behind his advice to isolate after acquiring necessary knowledge.

Core Idea
In corrupt times, salvation lies in isolation after knowledge.

Sanusi paints a grim picture of his own era near the end of the ninth century, where righteous people are scarce and evils are rampant. He reflects on how earlier imams would react if they saw this time, and then prescribes a radical solution: complete withdrawal from society for those who have already acquired necessary knowledge. This passage serves as both a historical lament and a practical spiritual counsel.

Guided Path
1
Read the lament and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp Sanusi's description of the scarcity of the pious and the evils of the time.
Notice his reference to earlier scholars and the hadith that refutes despair.
2
Identify the key advice
Find where Sanusi states the obligation to isolate and the conditions he attaches (after acquiring knowledge).
The phrase 'الواجب قطعاً' is important; it indicates a definitive duty.
3
Examine the supporting poetry
Read the lines from Ka'b and Ibn Mas'ud that describe an age of rejection of truth.
This underscores the severity of the time.
4
Reflect on the purpose of isolation
Consider why isolation is recommended: to preserve one's self and religion amidst trials until death.
The metaphor 'حِلْسَ بيته' emphasizes staying put.
5
Check your understanding
Take the checkpoint quiz to ensure you've grasped the main obligation.
This passage is a methodological warning.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأيسَ الإنسانُ في هذا الزمانِ مِنْ أنْ يجد أحداً منهم ، ولكن الحديث يردُّ هذا الإياس - أو كما قال - ، لكنهم في القلة بحيث لا يُعرفونَ ، فطوبى لمن عرف واحداً منهم أو رآه بعين التعظيم ، فهم القومُ الذينَ لا يشقى بهم جليسهم ، نسألُ اللهَ تعالى ألا يَحرِمَنا بركاتِهم بمنّه ) انتهى (1) هذا ما قاله هؤلاء الأئمَّةُ الأعلام في أزمنتهم الفاضلة الزاهرة بوجودهم ووجود أمثالهم مِنْ سادات وعلماء كرام ، فكيف لو رأوا زماننا هذا أواخر القرن التاسع ؟! والله سبحانه المستعان وما عسى أن يصف الواصفُ مِنْ شرورِ هذا الوقتِ وشرورِ أهلِهِ ؟! وقد أغنى فيه عن الخبر العِيانُ ، والواجب فيهِ قطعاً لِمَنْ أَرادَ النجاة بعد تحصيل ما يلزمُهُ مِنَ العلم : أن يعتزلَ الناس جملة ، ويكونَ حِلْسَ بيته ويبكي على نفسِهِ ، ويدعو دعاءَ الغريق ؛ لعلَّ الله سبحانَهُ يَخرِقُ لهُ العادة بحفظه بينَ هذه الفتنِ المتراكمة في نفسِهِ ودينه إلى أنْ يرتحل عن هذه الدنيا بموته هَذَا الزَّمَانُ الَّذِي كُنَّا نُحَاذِرُهُ فِي قَوْلِ كَعْبٍ وَفِي قَوْلِ أَبْنِ مَسْعُودِ دَهُرٌ بِهِ الْحَقُّ مَرْدُودٌ بِأَجْمَعِهِ وَالظُّلْمُ وَالْبَغْيُ فِيهِ غَيْرُ مَرْدُودِ إنْ دامَ هَذَا وَلَمْ يُحْدَتْ لَهُ غِيَرٌ لَمْ يُبْكَ مَيْتٌ وَلَمْ يُفْرَحْ بِمَوْلُودِ
A person in this time has no hope of finding any of them, but the hadith refutes this despair - or as he said - but they are in such scarcity that they are not known. So blessed is he who knows one of them or sees him with an eye of reverence, for they are the people whose companion is never miserable. We ask Allah the Exalted not to deprive us of their blessings by His grace. End. (1) This is what these eminent imams said in their virtuous, flourishing times due to their existence and the existence of their likes from noble masters and scholars. So how would they have seen our time at the end of the ninth century?! Allah the Exalted is the one sought for help. And what can a describer describe of the evils of this time and the evils of its people?! Sight has sufficed over news. And the absolute obligation for one who desires salvation after acquiring the necessary knowledge is to entirely isolate from people, and to become a doormat of his house, and weep over himself, and supplicate like one drowning; perhaps Allah the Exalted will break the norm for him by preserving him amidst these accumulated trials in his self and his religion until he departs from this world by his death. This is the time we used to be cautious of in the saying of Ka'b and in the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: an age in which the truth is entirely rejected, and oppression and transgression are not rejected in it. If this continues and no change occurs, no dead will be wept over and no newborn will be rejoiced at.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a lament by the author about the scarcity of righteous people in his own time, and his advice for those seeking salvation to isolate themselves. The author begins by stating that one despairs of finding any of those pious people, but then notes that a hadith rejects this despair, implying that they still exist but are very few. He then cites the hadith that says blessed is he who knows or sees one of them with reverence, for their companionship brings no misery. The author then reflects on how the great imams of earlier times would react if they saw the end of the ninth century, with its overwhelming evils. He says that the state of affairs is so evident that seeing suffices over reports. For one who wants salvation after obtaining necessary knowledge, the duty is to withdraw from people completely, stay fixed in his home like a doormat (a metaphor for never leaving), weep over his own state, and pray earnestly like a drowning person, hoping that Allah may grant him a miracle of preservation amidst the accumulating trials until death. The passage concludes with a poetic quotation from Ka'b and Ibn Mas'ud describing an age where truth is rejected and oppression is not opposed, and if it persists, no one will mourn the dead or rejoice at birth. The author uses this to emphasize the severity of the times.

الحِلْس
العِيان
الفتن
الإياس
الطائفة
أواخر القرن التاسع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that isolation (العزلة) is recommended for everyone regardless of their state.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly conditions isolation on having already acquired the necessary knowledge (بعد تحصيل ما يلزمه من العلم).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the absolute obligation (الواجب قطعاً) for one who desires salvation after acquiring necessary knowledge?
A) To seek out the remaining righteous people and accompany them.
B) To isolate entirely from people and stay in his house weeping and supplicating.
C) To engage in jihad against the oppressors.
D) To migrate to another land.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi advises that in a corrupt age, after acquiring essential knowledge, one must completely withdraw from people, stay home, weep and supplicate, hoping for Allah's preservation until death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that complete isolation from people could save your faith, would you be willing to leave your community, job, and relationships? What holds you back?
?
Sanusi describes weeping over oneself like a drowning person. When was the last time you felt such desperation about your own spiritual state? What would it take for you to weep like that?
?
The righteous are described as so rare that they are virtually unknown. Are you among the few striving for that level, or are you content with the majority's state? What specific change will you make today to pursue your own salvation?

Author's Intention to Write a Commentary on His Creed
Sanusi announces his plan to write a commentary on his shorter creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's purpose and motivation for writing a commentary on his creed, and why he emphasizes the unique value of his concise creed despite its brevity.

Core Idea
Brevity combined with depth: a concise creed containing verified proofs and rare details.

In this passage, Sanusi expresses gratitude for composing a concise creed and explains his motivation to write a commentary. He highlights that despite its brevity, this creed contains thorough proofs and unique details that even lengthy works often lack. The passage sets the stage for the commentary to come, emphasizing the need for divine assistance and effort to grasp its deep meanings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the English translation carefully.
Notice the author's grateful tone and the structure: first praising the creed, then stating the plan for commentary.
2
Identify the two key qualities of the creed
Sanusi mentions that his creed is both concise (أخصر) and yet contains thorough verification (تحقيق البراهين) and attention to subtle details (جزئيات). Identify these qualities in the text.
This shows that brevity does not mean lack of depth.
3
Note the author's motivation for writing the commentary
Sanusi says he wants to make the sweet sources (عذب مواردها) easier to drink from and to clarify the 'brides of its meanings' (عرائس معانيها). Understand why a commentary is needed.
The commentary is meant to facilitate access, not to replace the original.
4
Reflect on the role of divine success and effort
Sanusi states that even an intelligent person cannot attain verification except through special success (توفيق خاص) and great effort. Consider why this is emphasized.
This highlights that understanding creed is both a gift and a struggle.

وقد مَنَّ الله سبحانه وتعالى عليَّ في هذه الأيام الغريبة بوضعِ عقيدة يظهرُ أنَّها أخصرُ مِنَ الأُولى وأقربُ ، ثم معَ اختصارِها ففيها مِنْ تحقيق البراهين ما يجلو عنِ النفوسِ المُيسرة لفهم الحقِّ وقبولِهِ مِنْ أَهْلِهِ كل الكربِ ، وفيها مِنَ التنبيه على جزئيَّاتِ مِنَ العقائدِ ممَّا لا يُوجَدُ في كثيرِ مِنَ المطوَّلات فضلاً عن المختصراتِ ، بل ولا يَتوصَّلُ اللبيب إلى تحقيقه إلا بتوفيق خاص وعظيمِ تعب ، فأردتُ أنْ أشفعَ ذلك بوضع مختصر يُجَسِّرُ على الشرب مِنْ عذب مواردها ، ويُسهل ما عسى أن يتعوَّصَ مِنْ عرائس معانيها على خاطبها ومُكابدها ، وعزمتُ أنْ
And Allah the Exalted has granted me favor in these strange days by composing a creed that appears to be more concise than the first and closer, then despite its brevity, it contains such verification of proofs as removes from souls that are facilitated to understand the truth and accept it from its people all distress, and it contains attention to particulars of creed that are not found in many lengthy works, let alone abridged ones; rather, the intelligent person does not attain its verification except through special success and great effort. So I wanted to follow that with a commentary that strengthens drinking from the sweet sources, and eases whatever might become difficult from the brides of its meanings upon its recipient and its striver, and I resolved to
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is the author's announcement of his intention to write a commentary (مختصر) on a creed (عقيدة) that he had previously composed. He begins by thanking Allah for enabling him to write a creed that is even more concise and accessible than an earlier one ('الأولى'). He emphasizes that despite its brevity, this creed contains a level of verification of proofs (تحقيق البراهين) that clears all distress from souls that are prepared to understand and accept the truth. Additionally, it includes attention to particular details of creedal matters that are not found in many lengthy works, let alone abridged ones. He notes that even a clever person cannot attain verification of these details except through a special divine granting of success (توفيق خاص) and immense effort. To facilitate access to these deep meanings, the author resolves to write a commentary that will strengthen the reader's ability to drink from the sweet sources (مواردها) and ease whatever may be difficult from the 'brides of its meanings' (عرائس معانيها) for the one who receives it and strivers. The sentence ends abruptly with 'وعزمتُ أنْ' (and I resolved to...), indicating that the continuation is on the next page.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that brevity implies lack of depth.
Correction: The author asserts that this concise creed contains verified proofs and unique details not found in many lengthy works, demonstrating that brevity can coexist with depth.

Checkpoint
What does the author claim about the creed he composed?
A) It is longer and more detailed than his earlier creed.
B) It is concise yet contains verified proofs and unique details not found in many long works.
C) It is intended only for advanced scholars.
D) It requires no commentary because it is so clear.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi composed a concise creed rich in verified proofs and unique details, and he writes a commentary to make its deep meanings accessible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you come across a concise statement of creed, do you assume it is simple or do you humbly recognize that it may require deep reflection and guidance? How often have you skimmed over profound truths because you underestimated their depth?
?
The author thanks Allah for enabling him to write a creed that clears distress from the soul. In what areas of your faith do you still carry distress or doubt? Have you sought out the kind of verified proofs that can truly clear that distress, or have you been content with superficial answers?
?
Sanusi resolved to write a commentary to ease the difficulty of understanding. When you find a matter of aqeedah challenging, do you have the patience and discipline to seek out a teacher, a book, or a commentary to help you? What is holding you back from 'drinking from the sweet sources' of knowledge?

Author's Motivation and Method in Writing a Concise Creed
Author quotes poetry about the age and states his plan to write a concise creed with proofs and a commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's motivation for writing a concise creed and his pedagogical method of combining conciseness with proofs.

Core Idea
Sanusi writes a concise creed with proofs to guide believers in a time of widespread injustice and confusion.

This passage opens Sanusi's commentary with a vivid portrayal of a troubled era, citing poetry from Ka‘b and Ibn Mas‘ūd. The author expresses gratitude that Allah has enabled him to produce a creed that is both concise and rich in proofs, addressing detailed matters of faith. He then announces his plan to write a summary (mukhtaṣar) to make the creed accessible, focusing on wording for brevity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage with translation
Read the Arabic text and its translation together to get a sense of the author's flow and style. Note the poetic quotation at the beginning.
The poetry sets a somber tone for the author's project.
2
Identify the two main parts
The passage has two clear parts: (1) a description of the corrupt age using poetry, and (2) the author's response of composing a creed and then a summary. Locate each part in the text.
The transition occurs at 'وقد من الله سبحانه وتعالى علي'.
3
Analyze the author's methodology
Notice how the author emphasizes conciseness (اختصار) and verification of proofs (تحقيق البراهين). He also stresses that the creed covers particulars not found in longer works.
This shows his goal of making deep theology accessible.
4
Understand the plan for the summary
The author intends to accompany the creed with a summary (مختصر) that focuses only on wording (ما يتعلق باللفظ) to maintain conciseness and ease understanding.
The summary is meant to help students drink from the 'sweet waters' of the creed.
5
Address a common misunderstanding
Some might think the author is criticizing his earlier creed, but he praises it and aims for an even more concise version. The passage shows gratitude, not criticism.
Read the lines about 'أخصر من الأولى' carefully.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا الزمان الذي كنا نحاذره في قول كعب وفي قول ابن مسعود دهر به الحق مردود بأجمعه والظلم والبغي فيه غير مردود إن دام هذا ولم يحدث له غير لم يبك ميت ولم يفرح بمولود وقد من الله سبحانه وتعالى علي في هذه الأيام الغريبة بوضع عقيدة يظهر أنها أخصر من الأولى وأقرب ثم مع اختصارها ففيها من تحقيق البراهين ما يجلو عن النفوس الميسرة لفهم الحق وقبوله من أهله كل الكرب وفيها من التنبيه على جزئيات من العقائد مما لا يوجد في كثير من المطولات فضلا عن المختصرات بل ولا يتوصل اللبيب إلى تحقيقه إلا بتوفيق خاص وعظيم تعب فأردت أن أشفع ذلك بوضع مختصر يجسر على الشرب من عذب مواردها ويسهل ما عسى أن يتعوص من عرائس معانيها على خاطبها ومكابدها وعزمت أن أقتصر فيه على ما يتعلق باللفظ دون زيادة حرصا مني على سوق النفس بالاختصار إلى الاستفادة
This is the time we used to beware of in the saying of Ka‘b and in the saying of Ibn Mas‘ūd: a time in which the truth is rejected entirely, and injustice and transgression are not repelled. If this continues and no change occurs, no dead will be mourned and no newborn will be rejoiced. And Allah, Exalted is He, has favored me in these strange days by composing a creed (ʿaqīda) that appears to be more concise than the first one and easier. Then along with its conciseness, it contains such verification of proofs (barāhīn) that it clears the hearts (which are disposed to understand and accept the truth from its people) of all distress, and it contains warnings about particular matters of beliefs (ʿaqāʾid) that are not found in many lengthy works, let alone summaries. Rather, the intelligent person cannot attain verification of them except by special divine grace and great effort. So I wanted to accompany that by composing a summary (mukhtaṣar) that facilitates drinking from the sweet waters of its sources, and eases what might become difficult to grasp of the brides of its meanings for the one who requests and strives to acquire them. And I resolved to restrict myself in it to what pertains to wording without addition, out of my eagerness to drive the soul to benefit through conciseness.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is an introduction where the author sets the context. He begins by quoting poetry that describes a corrupt age where truth is rejected and injustice prevails. Then he expresses gratitude to Allah for enabling him to write a new creed (ʿaqīda) that is even more concise than a previous one, yet contains strong proofs (barāhīn) and covers detailed matters of belief (ʿaqāʾid) not found in longer works. He emphasizes that understanding these details requires divine grace and effort. He then announces his plan to write a summary (mukhtaṣar) that will facilitate understanding the creed, focusing on wording for brevity. The author's goal is to make the creed accessible and beneficial through conciseness.

Key Terms
عقيدة
براهين
مختصر
اختصار
تقليد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the author is criticizing his first creed or that conciseness implies lack of depth.
Correction: The author praises the first creed and aims for an even more concise version, while emphasizing that this new creed contains strong proofs and detailed matters not found in longer works. Conciseness does not sacrifice depth.

Checkpoint
What does the author plan to write after composing the concise creed?
A) A lengthy commentary on the Qur'an
B) A summary (mukhtaṣar) that focuses on wording
C) A refutation of the first creed
D) A poetry collection

Key Takeaway
Sanusi’s project is to provide a concise yet proof-rich creed, accompanied by a summary focused on wording, to guide believers in troubled times.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In this description of a time where truth is rejected and injustice prevails, do you see your own era? What concrete steps are you taking to ensure you are not complicit in that rejection, and how are you actively seeking the truth that the author labored to present concisely?
?
The author says that understanding these details requires 'special divine grace and great effort.' Have you ever earnestly sought that grace through sincere supplication and intense effort in learning your creed? If not, what holds you back?
?
Sanusi resolved to restrict himself to wording for conciseness, aiming to drive the soul to benefit. Are you the kind of reader who takes such conciseness as a gift, or do you brush over it? How will you approach this text to truly benefit?
