The Legitimacy of Kalam and Its Definition
The author defends kalam and defines its method with a Quranic example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that kalam is a legitimate discipline rooted in the Quran and Sunnah, and you will learn its definition as a method of argumentation using rational and scriptural proofs.

Core Idea
Kalam is not an innovation; it is the Quranic method of argumentation.

The author opens with a powerful poetic defense: just as the sun’s light is unaffected by the blind, kalam is unharmed by its critics. He then asserts that disparaging the science of tawheed is tantamount to denying the Quran and Sunnah, because its proofs are drawn from them. This sets the stage for a clear definition of the kalam method and a rebuttal of the false claim that it originated from outside Islamic sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the poetic defense
Read the opening couplet and reflect on its meaning: criticism does not harm truth. Then read the translation.
2
Understand the gravity of disparaging tawheed
The author quotes a scholar saying that criticizing tawheed is rejecting Quran and Sunnah. Notice the strong link between kalam and revelation.
3
Learn the definition of kalam method
The author provides a formal definition: 'presenting a proof for a claim in the manner of the mutakallimun.' The example from Quran 21:22 shows that the Quran itself uses this method.
This refutes the claim that kalam is foreign to Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عَابَ الكَلامَ أُناس لا خَلاقَ لَهُمْ وَمَا عَلَيْهِ إِذَا عَابُوهُ مِنْ ضَرَرِ مَا ضَرَّ شَمْسَ الضُّحَى فِي الأُفْقِ طَالِعَةً أَلَّا يَرَى ضَوْءَهَا مَنْ لَيْسَ ذَا بَصَرِ

قالَ بعض العلماءِ : مَنْ قدحَ في علم التوحيد فقد أنكر القرآن والسنة ؛ إذ أدلته مأخوذة منهما .

وقد ذكر أهلُ البيان حقيقة المذهب الكلامي فقالوا : هو إيرادُ حُجَّةٍ للمطلوب على طريقة أهل الكلام ، ومثلوا ذلك بقولِهِ تعالى : ( لَوْ كَانَ فيهِمَا ءَالِمَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَنَا) [الأنبياء : ٢٢]

قالوا : وأَوَّلُ مَنْ أنكرَ المذهب الكلامي الجاحظُ مِنَ المعتزلة . قال الشيخ ابن عرفة : ( وكذبَ الجاحظ ؛ إذْ أَكثرُ حُجَجِ أَهلِ الكلام مستنبطةٌ مِنَ القرآن العظيم ) .

وما يَستنِدُ إِليهِ بعضُ مَنْ أعمى الله بصيرتهُ في ادعائِهِ تحريم النظرِ في علم التوحيدِ ؛ مِنْ أنَّ الشافعي رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه رأى في أهل علم الكلام أنْ يُضربوا بالجريد . . نقولُ بمُوجَبِهِ في أولئك الذينَ كانوا يُسمَّونَ أهلَ علمِ الكلام في زمانِهِ ؛ وهم عمرُو بنُ عُبَيدٍ مِنَ المعتزلة في زمانه وحفصُ القردِ مِنَ القدرية وأضرابهم ، ولذلك لمَّا مرض الشافعي رضي الله تعالى عنه دخل عليهِ حفص القردِ ، فقالَ : مَنْ ؟ فقالَ : حفصُ القردِ ، فقالَ : لا حفظَكَ اللهُ ولا رعاك حتى تتوبَ عمَّا أنتَ فيه .

وهذا التلقيبُ بأهلِ علم الكلام في ذلك الزمانِ خاص بأولئك ، ولا شك أنَّ أولئكَ إنَّما كان كلامهم بالبدع ، وإلقاء الشُّبَهِ ، وهدْمِ ما دلّ عليه العقل والنقلُ ، وهم أهل لأنْ يُضربوا بالحديدِ عوضاً عن الضرب بالجريد . وأما أهلُ علم الكلام في اصطلاحِنا اليوم : فهم شيخُ أهل السنَّةِ أبو الحسن الأشعري رضي الله تعالى عنه ، وأصحابه ؛ كالأستاذ أبي إسحاق الإسفرايني ، وسيفِ السنَّةِ القاضي أبي بكر الباقلاني ، وإمام الحرمين ، وأتباعهم ، ولا شكّ أنَّ هؤلاء الأئمَّةَ رضيَ الله تعالى عنهم ونفع بهم همُ القائمونَ بحُجَّةِ اللهِ تعالى ورسولِهِ ، والناصرون لدينِهِ بعد الصحابة رضي الله تعالى عنهم ، وهم الذينَ ضَربوا بأعظم مِنَ الحديد مَنْ أمرَ الشافعي رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه أَنْ يُضربوا بالجريد ؛ إذ هم قد ضربوهم بقواطع الأدلة التي هي في التأثير أمضى مِنَ السيوف والأسنَّةِ ، وكشفوا فضائحهم على ممر الدهور ، وردُّوا كيدهم للدين في نحورهم ، وأبانوا خِسَّةَ عقولهم في غاية ؛ حتى لا يغتر بمقالتِهم مسلمٌ . ولا شكّ أنَّهم رضي الله تعالى عنهم هم الذين قاموا بجهادِ تمييز الحقِّ عن الباطل لمَّا اختلطا ، وجَلَوُا الحق حقاً على مِنَصَّةِ الظُهورِ
Some people without virtue have criticized kalam, but it suffers no harm from their criticism, just as the morning sun in the horizon is not harmed by the fact that those without sight do not see its light. Some scholars said: Whoever disparages the science of tawheed (monotheism) has denied the Quran and the Sunnah, because its proofs are taken from them. The experts in expression (ahl al-bayan) have mentioned the true nature of the kalam method and said: It is presenting an argument for the desired conclusion in the manner of the people of kalam. And they gave as an example His statement, the Exalted: 'If there were in them gods besides Allah, they would surely have corrupted' [Quran 21:22]. They said: The first to deny the kalam method was al-Jahiz from the Mu'tazila. Shaykh Ibn Arafa said: 'Al-Jahiz lied, for most of the proofs of the people of kalam are derived from the Great Quran.' What some people whose insight Allah has blinded rely on in their claim that reflection in the science of tawheed is forbidden, from the report that al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, held that the practitioners of kalam should be beaten with palm branches... we say: this applies to those who were called 'people of kalam' in his time, namely Amr ibn Ubayd from the Mu'tazila of his time, and Hafs al-Qard from the Qadariyya, and their ilk. For this reason, when al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, fell ill, Hafs al-Qard entered upon him. He said, 'Who is it?' He said, 'Hafs al-Qard.' He said, 'May Allah not preserve you nor protect you until you repent from what you are upon.' And this appellation of 'people of the science of kalam' in that time was specific to those people. There is no doubt that those people's discourse consisted of innovations, casting doubts, and demolishing what reason and revelation indicated. They deserved to be beaten with iron instead of being beaten with palm branches. As for the people of the science of kalam in our present terminology, they are: the Shaykh of Ahl al-Sunnah, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, and his companions, such as the master Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini, the Sword of the Sunnah, the Judge Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, Imam al-Haramayn [al-Juwayni], and their followers. There is no doubt that these imams, may Allah be pleased with them and benefit [us] through them, are the ones who uphold the proof of Allah and His Messenger, and the supporters of His religion after the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. They are the ones who struck with something greater than iron those whom al-Shafi'i ordered to be beaten with palm branches; for they struck them with decisive proofs which are more effective in their impact than swords and spears. They exposed their scandals throughout the ages, repelled their plots against religion, and revealed the baseness of their intellects to the utmost, so that no Muslim would be deceived by their sayings. There is no doubt that they, may Allah be pleased with them, are the ones who undertook the jihad of distinguishing truth from falsehood when they became mixed, and they made truth manifestly clear.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a defense of kalam (theological reasoning) against its critics. It begins with a poetic line stating that criticizing kalam does not harm it. Then it asserts that disparaging the science of tawhid (theology) is tantamount to denying the Quran and Sunnah because its proofs are derived from them. It defines the kalam method as presenting a proof for a theological claim in the manner of the mutakallimun, citing the Quranic verse on the impossibility of multiple gods as an example. It then addresses the claim that kalam is forbidden by clarifying that the condemnation of kalam by early scholars like al-Shafi'i was directed at specific heretics such as Amr ibn Ubayd (a Mu'tazili) and Hafs al-Fard (a Qadari), not at the orthodox mutakallimun. It recounts the anecdote of al-Shafi'i rebuking Hafs al-Fard. The author then distinguishes the early heretical 'people of kalam' from the later orthodox school, naming Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, al-Isfara'ini, al-Baqillani, al-Juwayni, and others, praising them as defenders of the proof of Allah and His Messenger. The passage concludes that these orthodox scholars refuted the heretics with decisive arguments, exposing their falsehood and protecting the faith.

Key Terms
كلام
علم التوحيد
المذهب الكلامي
أهل البيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author cite as an example of the kalam method in the Quran?
A) The verse about the sun and moon
B) The verse on the impossibility of multiple gods (21:22)
C) The verse on the creation of humans
D) The verse on the Night of Power

Key Takeaway
Kalam is a legitimate method rooted in the Quran, as shown by its definition and scriptural example.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that the Quran itself uses argumentation. When you read the Quran, do you actively seek out its logical proofs, or do you treat it only as a source of spiritual comfort? Will you commit to studying the Quranic arguments for tawheed as a means of strengthening your faith?
?
The opening couplet compares critics of kalam to the blind who cannot see the sun. Have you ever dismissed a branch of Islamic knowledge without examining its foundations? What disciplines have you judged unfairly, and will you investigate them with an open heart?
?
Al-Jahiz denied the kalam method despite being a knowledgeable scholar. This warns against arrogance. Is there a area of religious knowledge where you rely on your own opinion rather than the consensus of scholars? What step will you take to humble yourself and learn from those who are more knowledgable?

Al-Shafi'i's Condemnation: Clarifying the Target
The author clarifies that al-Shafi'i's condemnation targeted heretics, not orthodox kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-Shafi'i's criticism of kalam was directed at heretical innovators, not at orthodox theological reasoning.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i condemned heretics, not the discipline of kalam itself.

Some critics of kalam cite al-Shafi'i's reported order to beat 'people of kalam' with palm branches as evidence that kalam is forbidden. The author addresses this by specifying that al-Shafi'i was referring to specific heretics like Amr ibn Ubayd and Hafs al-Fard, who used kalam to spread innovations and doubts. The anecdote of al-Shafi'i's harsh rebuke of Hafs al-Fard illustrates this point.

Guided Path
1
Read the claim and its refutation
Read the passage where the author describes how some people misuse al-Shafi'i's statement. Notice how the author immediately restricts its application.
2
Identify the heretics named
The author names Amr ibn Ubayd (Mu'tazili) and Hafs al-Fard (Qadari). Understand that these were known heretical figures.
3
Reflect on the anecdote
The story of al-Shafi'i's illness and his prayer against Hafs al-Fard shows his personal condemnation of such individuals, not of kalam itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عَابَ الكَلامَ أُناس لا خَلاقَ لَهُمْ وَمَا عَلَيْهِ إِذَا عَابُوهُ مِنْ ضَرَرِ مَا ضَرَّ شَمْسَ الضُّحَى فِي الأُفْقِ طَالِعَةً أَلَّا يَرَى ضَوْءَهَا مَنْ لَيْسَ ذَا بَصَرِ

قالَ بعض العلماءِ : مَنْ قدحَ في علم التوحيد فقد أنكر القرآن والسنة ؛ إذ أدلته مأخوذة منهما .

وقد ذكر أهلُ البيان حقيقة المذهب الكلامي فقالوا : هو إيرادُ حُجَّةٍ للمطلوب على طريقة أهل الكلام ، ومثلوا ذلك بقولِهِ تعالى : ( لَوْ كَانَ فيهِمَا ءَالِمَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَنَا) [الأنبياء : ٢٢]

قالوا : وأَوَّلُ مَنْ أنكرَ المذهب الكلامي الجاحظُ مِنَ المعتزلة . قال الشيخ ابن عرفة : ( وكذبَ الجاحظ ؛ إذْ أَكثرُ حُجَجِ أَهلِ الكلام مستنبطةٌ مِنَ القرآن العظيم ) .

وما يَستنِدُ إِليهِ بعضُ مَنْ أعمى الله بصيرتهُ في ادعائِهِ تحريم النظرِ في علم التوحيدِ ؛ مِنْ أنَّ الشافعي رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه رأى في أهل علم الكلام أنْ يُضربوا بالجريد . . نقولُ بمُوجَبِهِ في أولئك الذينَ كانوا يُسمَّونَ أهلَ علمِ الكلام في زمانِهِ ؛ وهم عمرُو بنُ عُبَيدٍ مِنَ المعتزلة في زمانه وحفصُ القردِ مِنَ القدرية وأضرابهم ، ولذلك لمَّا مرض الشافعي رضي الله تعالى عنه دخل عليهِ حفص القردِ ، فقالَ : مَنْ ؟ فقالَ : حفصُ القردِ ، فقالَ : لا حفظَكَ اللهُ ولا رعاك حتى تتوبَ عمَّا أنتَ فيه .

وهذا التلقيبُ بأهلِ علم الكلام في ذلك الزمانِ خاص بأولئك ، ولا شك أنَّ أولئكَ إنَّما كان كلامهم بالبدع ، وإلقاء الشُّبَهِ ، وهدْمِ ما دلّ عليه العقل والنقلُ ، وهم أهل لأنْ يُضربوا بالحديدِ عوضاً عن الضرب بالجريد . وأما أهلُ علم الكلام في اصطلاحِنا اليوم : فهم شيخُ أهل السنَّةِ أبو الحسن الأشعري رضي الله تعالى عنه ، وأصحابه ؛ كالأستاذ أبي إسحاق الإسفرايني ، وسيفِ السنَّةِ القاضي أبي بكر الباقلاني ، وإمام الحرمين ، وأتباعهم ، ولا شكّ أنَّ هؤلاء الأئمَّةَ رضيَ الله تعالى عنهم ونفع بهم همُ القائمونَ بحُجَّةِ اللهِ تعالى ورسولِهِ ، والناصرون لدينِهِ بعد الصحابة رضي الله تعالى عنهم ، وهم الذينَ ضَربوا بأعظم مِنَ الحديد مَنْ أمرَ الشافعي رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه أَنْ يُضربوا بالجريد ؛ إذ هم قد ضربوهم بقواطع الأدلة التي هي في التأثير أمضى مِنَ السيوف والأسنَّةِ ، وكشفوا فضائحهم على ممر الدهور ، وردُّوا كيدهم للدين في نحورهم ، وأبانوا خِسَّةَ عقولهم في غاية ؛ حتى لا يغتر بمقالتِهم مسلمٌ . ولا شكّ أنَّهم رضي الله تعالى عنهم هم الذين قاموا بجهادِ تمييز الحقِّ عن الباطل لمَّا اختلطا ، وجَلَوُا الحق حقاً على مِنَصَّةِ الظُهورِ
Some people without virtue have criticized kalam, but it suffers no harm from their criticism, just as the morning sun in the horizon is not harmed by the fact that those without sight do not see its light. Some scholars said: Whoever disparages the science of tawheed (monotheism) has denied the Quran and the Sunnah, because its proofs are taken from them. The experts in expression (ahl al-bayan) have mentioned the true nature of the kalam method and said: It is presenting an argument for the desired conclusion in the manner of the people of kalam. And they gave as an example His statement, the Exalted: 'If there were in them gods besides Allah, they would surely have corrupted' [Quran 21:22]. They said: The first to deny the kalam method was al-Jahiz from the Mu'tazila. Shaykh Ibn Arafa said: 'Al-Jahiz lied, for most of the proofs of the people of kalam are derived from the Great Quran.' What some people whose insight Allah has blinded rely on in their claim that reflection in the science of tawheed is forbidden, from the report that al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, held that the practitioners of kalam should be beaten with palm branches... we say: this applies to those who were called 'people of kalam' in his time, namely Amr ibn Ubayd from the Mu'tazila of his time, and Hafs al-Qard from the Qadariyya, and their ilk. For this reason, when al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, fell ill, Hafs al-Qard entered upon him. He said, 'Who is it?' He said, 'Hafs al-Qard.' He said, 'May Allah not preserve you nor protect you until you repent from what you are upon.' And this appellation of 'people of the science of kalam' in that time was specific to those people. There is no doubt that those people's discourse consisted of innovations, casting doubts, and demolishing what reason and revelation indicated. They deserved to be beaten with iron instead of being beaten with palm branches. As for the people of the science of kalam in our present terminology, they are: the Shaykh of Ahl al-Sunnah, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, and his companions, such as the master Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini, the Sword of the Sunnah, the Judge Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, Imam al-Haramayn [al-Juwayni], and their followers. There is no doubt that these imams, may Allah be pleased with them and benefit [us] through them, are the ones who uphold the proof of Allah and His Messenger, and the supporters of His religion after the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. They are the ones who struck with something greater than iron those whom al-Shafi'i ordered to be beaten with palm branches; for they struck them with decisive proofs which are more effective in their impact than swords and spears. They exposed their scandals throughout the ages, repelled their plots against religion, and revealed the baseness of their intellects to the utmost, so that no Muslim would be deceived by their sayings. There is no doubt that they, may Allah be pleased with them, are the ones who undertook the jihad of distinguishing truth from falsehood when they became mixed, and they made truth manifestly clear.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a defense of kalam (theological reasoning) against its critics. It begins with a poetic line stating that criticizing kalam does not harm it. Then it asserts that disparaging the science of tawhid (theology) is tantamount to denying the Quran and Sunnah because its proofs are derived from them. It defines the kalam method as presenting a proof for a theological claim in the manner of the mutakallimun, citing the Quranic verse on the impossibility of multiple gods as an example. It then addresses the claim that kalam is forbidden by clarifying that the condemnation of kalam by early scholars like al-Shafi'i was directed at specific heretics such as Amr ibn Ubayd (a Mu'tazili) and Hafs al-Fard (a Qadari), not at the orthodox mutakallimun. It recounts the anecdote of al-Shafi'i rebuking Hafs al-Fard. The author then distinguishes the early heretical 'people of kalam' from the later orthodox school, naming Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, al-Isfara'ini, al-Baqillani, al-Juwayni, and others, praising them as defenders of the proof of Allah and His Messenger. The passage concludes that these orthodox scholars refuted the heretics with decisive arguments, exposing their falsehood and protecting the faith.

Key Terms
الشافعي
أهل علم الكلام
الجريد
عمر بن عبيد
حفص القرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Shafi'i condemned all kalam and its practitioners.
Correction: Al-Shafi'i's order was specific to heretical innovators like Amr ibn Ubayd and Hafs al-Fard, who used kalam to spread doubts and innovations.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who were the actual targets of al-Shafi'i's order to beat 'people of kalam'?
A) All practitioners of kalam without exception.
B) Specific heretics like Amr ibn Ubayd and Hafs al-Fard.
C) The Ash'ari school.
D) The companions of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Al-Shafi'i's criticism was directed at heretical innovators, not at the legitimate discipline of kalam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever quoted a scholar's statement as a blanket judgment on a group without asking who exactly they were referring to? This lesson shows that even the greatest imams spoke with precision. When will you start investigating the specific context and target of every scholarly condemnation you use?
?
Al-Shafi'i's harsh prayer against Hafs al-Qard was not random anger—it was rooted in the danger of Hafs's specific heresy. Do you take the time to understand what someone actually believes before you dismiss or condemn them? Or do you label people based on general categories without examining their individual content?
?
The heretics of that time demolished 'what reason and revelation indicated.' Are there any ideas or influences in your own life that subtly undermine the harmony of reason and revelation? This passage calls you to protect your faith from both blind rejection and blind acceptance. What step will you take today to ensure your beliefs are built on solid ground, not on the doubts of innovators?

The Orthodox Ash'ari School: Defenders of the Faith
The author praises the Ash'ari school as the orthodox defenders of the faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will recognize the key figures of the orthodox Ash'ari school and appreciate their role in refuting heretics and upholding the faith.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari scholars are the true inheritors of prophetic defense against heresy.

Having distinguished the heretical mutakallimun, the author now identifies the orthodox school: the Ash'ariyya. He names its founding figure, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and key followers like al-Isfara'ini, al-Baqillani, and al-Juwayni. He praises them as the ones who uphold Allah's proof and support His religion after the Companions. The passage concludes with a vivid description of how they refuted heretics with decisive proofs, more effective than swords.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of orthodox scholars
Read the names: al-Ash'ari, al-Isfara'ini, al-Baqillani, al-Juwayni. Notice the titles such as 'Sword of the Sunnah' for al-Baqillani.
2
Understand their role
The author describes them as those who uphold the proof of Allah and support His religion after the Companions. This highlights their importance.
3
Contrast with the heretics
They struck heretics with proofs that are more effective than iron. Reflect on how intellectual refutation is a form of jihad.

Some people without virtue have criticized kalam, but it suffers no harm from their criticism, just as the morning sun in the horizon is not harmed by the fact that those without sight do not see its light. Who are included in the orthodox 'people of kalam' according to the author?
A) Amr ibn Ubayd and Hafs al-Fard.
B) Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and his companions.
C) Al-Jahiz and the Mu'tazila.
D) All those who engage in kalam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When the passage says the Ash'ari scholars 'struck with decisive proofs,' ask yourself: Is your faith supported by intellectual conviction, or do you rely on blind imitation? What would it take for you to build such conviction?
?
The scholars are praised for making truth 'manifestly clear so that no Muslim would be deceived.' Are you actively seeking clarity in areas where truth and falsehood have become mixed in your own life? Identify one issue and commit to investigating it today.
?
If you were to undertake the 'jihad of distinguishing truth from falsehood' in your own heart, what comfortable falsehood would you have to confront? What step will you take this week to expose it with proof?

The Just Carriers of Knowledge
Author cites hadith on carriers of knowledge and praises scholars who defend the faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith about the carriers of knowledge and how it supports the role of scholars in defending the faith from distortion, false claims, and misinterpretation.

Core Idea
Scholars are the just carriers who guard the faith from corruption.

The author begins with a metaphor comparing the scholars' clarity to the sun. He then cites a key hadith that defines the mission of scholars across generations: to protect the religion from three types of corruption. The rest of the passage uses conditional statements to elevate the status of these scholars and explain why earlier generations did not need them as much.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its translation
Read the Arabic passage of the hadith and its English translation carefully. Note the key phrases: 'carriers of knowledge,' 'just ones,' and the three things they repel.
The hadith is the central proof of the lesson.
2
Understand the three types of corruption
Focus on the explanation of tahrīf al-ghālīn, intihāl al-mubṭilīn, and ta’wīl al-jāhilīn. Use the commentary from al-Qari to grasp each term.
These terms are technical and essential for understanding the scholar's role.
3
Reflect on the conditional statements about the Salaf
Consider the two 'if' scenarios: what the Salaf would have done if they had seen these scholars, and what they would have done if they had faced the same trials. Why did they not need to act?
These conditionals emphasize the necessity of scholars in times of innovation.
4
Grasp the necessity of scholars in times of trial
The author concludes that the purity of earlier times made such defense unnecessary, but later times require scholars to protect the faith. Understand how this justifies the science of kalam.
This connects the hadith to the broader purpose of Islamic theology.

Like the sun, and they showed falsehood as falsehood until its darkness appeared more severe than the darkness of early dawn. And the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, informed about these masters and their followers, among those who followed their path and helped them in their noble purpose, may God Almighty be pleased with them, in his saying: 'The just ones of every generation will carry this knowledge, repelling from it the distortion of the extremists, the false claims of the falsifiers, and the misinterpretation of the ignorant.' (1) God. (1) Narrated by al-Bazzar in his Musnad (9423), and al-Tabarani in Musnad al-Shamiyyin (599) from the hadith of our master Abu Hurayra, may God be pleased with him, and al-‘Ala’i in Itharat al-Fawa’id (11) from the hadith of our master Usama ibn Zayd, may God be pleased with them both, and he said: a good strange hadith. See Irshad al-Sari (4/1). Al-‘Allama al-Qari said in Mirqat al-Mafatih (1/322) in explanation of 'distortion of the extremists': 'i.e., the innovators who exceed the limits of the Book of God and the Sunnah of His Messenger from the intended meaning, deviating from its direction; from ghala yaghlū, when he exceeds the limit, such as the sayings of the Qadariyya, the Jabriyya, and the Mushabbiha'; and 'false claim' is claiming something falsely, so these people show adherence to the Sunnah and following the prophetic guidance while they are not upon that. Then if the Companions or those after them from the pious predecessors, may God Almighty be pleased with them, had seen these masters upon whom God Almighty bestowed the greatest favor upon the Muslims, they would have magnified them with the utmost magnification, praised them with the greatest praise, and commanded the general Muslims—due to the generality of trials—to resort to them for correcting the principles of their religion and fortifying them against the devils of humans and jinn with the strong, impenetrable fortresses of their insights. And if the predecessors and Companions, may God Almighty be pleased with them, had experienced the trials that these masters experienced, they could not have done anything except the like of their action or greater. But they remained silent about that because of the purity of their minds and their times from every doubt, and the correctness of the beliefs of all of them by the necessary proofs that were made clear to them from the Qur'an and the Lawgiver, may God bless him and grant him peace, until their great and small, their males and females, their free and their slaves knew that. So they had no need for that, due to the non-appearance of the darkness of innovations in the suns of their noble times.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage combines a proof (the hadith) with a rhetorical commendation of scholars. The author begins with a metaphor: the scholars have made falsehood clear like the sun. Then he cites the well-known hadith about the 'just carriers of knowledge' who protect the faith from three types of corruption: distortion by extremists (tahrīf al-ghālīn), false claims by falsifiers (intihāl al-mubṭilīn), and misinterpretation by the ignorant (ta’wīl al-jāhilīn). The footnote provides the hadith's chain and explains the terms: tahrīf refers to innovators who exceed limits, mentioning sectarian examples (Qadariyya, Jabriyya, Mushabbiha); intihāl is claiming something falsely, pretending to follow the Sunnah while not. After the hadith, the author uses conditional statements to show the high status of these scholars: if the Salaf had seen them, they would have exalted them and directed Muslims to them for correcting their beliefs. Then another conditional: if the Salaf had faced the same trials, they would have done the same as these scholars—but they were free from need because their times were pure from innovation. This establishes the legitimacy and necessity of the scholars' role in defending doctrine.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the hadith only applies to hadith transmitters and not to theologians or defenders of creed.
Correction: The author applies the hadith to scholars who defend the faith from distortion, false claims, and misinterpretation, which is exactly the task of theologians (mutakallimūn) in later times.

Checkpoint

B) Innovations, sins, and disbelief
C) Doubts, desires, and misguidance
D) Corruption, division, and weakness

Key Takeaway
The hadith establishes that scholars who defend the faith from distortion, false claims, and misinterpretation are the true inheritors of prophetic knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

When you last learned something about your religion, did you verify that it came from such a carrier? What will you do today to ensure you are not unknowingly accepting a distorted teaching?
?
The author says the Salaf did not need these scholars because their minds and times were pure from doubt. But you live in an age of widespread innovation and confusion. What specific steps will you take to seek out and rely on the true scholars who defend the faith?
?
The hadith mentions three threats: extremism, hypocrisy in claiming to follow the Sunnah, and ignorant interpretation. Which of these do you see most in yourself or your community? Commit to one concrete action this week to guard against it.

The Obligation of Teaching 'Aqidah to the Common People
Author refutes the claim that 'aqidah should not be taught to common people and proves its obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why teaching proof-based 'aqidah to the common people is obligatory, and how the author refutes the objection that it should not be taught.

Core Idea
Every Muslim, including the common person, is required to know 'aqidah through proof.

Some have argued that 'aqidah should not be taught to common people with proofs, fearing confusion. In this passage, the author, Imam Sanusi, refutes this claim head-on. He argues that since knowledge of God is obligatory for every individual and can only be attained through proof, teaching proofs to the common people is not only permissible but necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument flow before interpreting.
Notice the strong opening refutation: 'It is clearly corrupt.'
2
Identify the opponent's claim and the author's refutation
Find the opponent's view that 'aqidah should not be taught to the common people. Then see how the author declares it 'clearly corrupt' (wāḍiḥ al-fasād).
The author does not mince words.
3
Understand the two supporting proofs
First proof: knowledge (ma'rifa) is obligatory for every individual and is only attained through proof (burhān). Second proof: reciting Qur'an and hadith without explanation is allowed, even though they can be misunderstood; so teaching beliefs with proofs is even more fitting.
The second proof is an argument from the lesser to the greater.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that teaching 'aqidah with proofs is not only permissible but incumbent (yata'ayyan). Consider why he uses 'more fitting' (aḥrā) and then 'incumbent'.
The obligation (taklīf) applies to all, with no distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان : في أنَّ للعامَّةِ نصيباً مِنَ الأدلة يطيقونَهُ ويُكلَّفون معرفته ] وأما قولُ بعض مَنْ لا بصيرة له ولا تحقيق : إِنَّهُ لا تُعلَّمُ العقائد للعوام ، ولا تُذكَرُ لهم براهينها ، مِنْ غير فرق منه بين واضحها الذي يمكنهم فهمُهُ وبينَ غيرِهِ .. فواضحُ الفسادِ ؛ لأنَّهُ إذا كانَتِ المعرفة واجبة على الأعيان بإجماع على ما ذكرَهُ كَثيرٌ مِنَ الأَئِمَّةِ ، بل هي نفسُ الإيمان أو لازمةٌ له ، وهي لا تحصل إلا بالبرهان .. فكيف لا يتأكَّدُ السعي في تعليمهم ما يُحصِّلُها ؟! وإذا جازَتْ قراءة القرآنِ والأحاديث النبوية بحضرتهم مِنْ غيرِ شرح لهم لمعانيهما ، معَ أنَّ فيهما ظواهر يجب تأويلها بإجماع ، وبسببِ فهمها على ظاهرِها هَلَكَ كثيرٌ مِنَ الخَلْقِ .. فَلَأَنْ يجوز تعليمهم العقائد مشروحة بأدلَّتِها التي تسعُها عقولهم أحرى ، بل يتعيَّنُ في حقهم ذلك ؛ لأنَّ التكليف بمعرفة عقائدِ الإيمان بالنظر الصحيح لا فرق فيهِ
Explanation: That the general public have a share of the proofs that they can bear and are obligated to know. As for the saying of one who has no insight nor verification: that 'aqidah should not be taught to the common people, nor should its proofs be mentioned to them, without distinguishing between its clear ones that they can understand and other than that—it is clearly corrupt. Because if knowledge (ma‘rifa) is obligatory upon individuals by consensus, as many of the imams have mentioned—indeed it is faith itself or necessary for it—and it is not attained except by proof (burhān), then how can striving to teach them what attains it not be emphasized? And if it is permissible to recite the Qur'an and prophetic hadiths in their presence without explaining their meanings to them, even though they contain apparent meanings that must be interpreted by consensus, and due to understanding them according to their apparent meanings many of the creation have perished—then it is more fitting that teaching them the beliefs explained with their proofs, which their intellects can accommodate, be permissible. Rather, it is incumbent upon them, because the obligation of knowing the beliefs of faith through correct consideration (al-naẓar al-ṣaḥīḥ) does not differentiate in that regard.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. The author states his thesis: the common people have a share of proofs that they can bear and are obligated to know. He then quotes an opponent who says that 'aqidah should not be taught to common people nor its proofs mentioned, without distinguishing between clear and unclear proofs. The author declares this view clearly corrupt (wāḍiḥ al-fasād). He provides two proofs: First, knowledge (ma‘rifa) of God is obligatory upon every individual by consensus, and it is either faith itself or necessary for it. This knowledge cannot be attained except through proof (burhān). Therefore, teaching them what attains that knowledge is obligatory. Second, it is permissible to recite the Qur'an and hadith in their presence without explanation, even though these texts contain apparent meanings (ẓawāhir) that must be interpreted (ta’wīl) by consensus, and misunderstanding them has led many astray. So if that is permissible, then teaching them beliefs with explanations and proofs that suit their intellects is even more permissible. Indeed, it is incumbent (yata‘ayyan) upon them, because the obligation of knowing the beliefs of faith through correct consideration (al-naẓar al-ṣaḥīḥ) applies to all, with no difference between the learned and the common. The argument flows logically: the requirement of proof for every individual necessitates teaching proofs to all, including the common people.

Key Terms
العقائد
العوام
البرهان
النظر الصحيح
المعرفة
الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Common people cannot understand proof-based 'aqidah, so it should not be taught to them.
Correction: The author argues that common people can understand clear proofs and are obligated to learn them, as ma'rifa is obligatory for every individual and only attained through proof.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main argument against the claim that 'aqidah should not be taught to common people?
A) Because common people are too weak to understand proofs
B) Because knowledge of 'aqidah is obligatory upon every individual, and it can only be attained through proof, so teaching proofs is necessary
C) Because common people already know 'aqidah instinctively
D) Because the Qur'an and hadith are sufficient without explanation

Key Takeaway
The obligation of knowing 'aqidah through proof applies to all Muslims, including the common people, so teaching them proofs is obligatory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever truly examined your own beliefs with proof, or have you relied on what you were taught without question? What specific step can you take today to build your 'aqidah on clear evidence from the Qur'an and reason?
?
If you are responsible for teaching others, do you shy away from explaining proofs, thinking they are too difficult? Remember the author’s warning: many have perished due to misunderstanding. Will you commit to teaching 'aqidah with proofs, even to those you consider common?
?
The author says knowledge is faith itself or necessary for it. Is your faith strong enough to withstand doubts? What will you do to ensure that your belief in Allah is not just inherited but is your own, based on personal conviction and proof?

Why the Salaf Were Silent on Kalam
Sanusi explains why early Salaf refrained from detailed kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the early Salaf did not engage in detailed kalam reasoning, according to Sanusi.

Core Idea
The Salaf's silence on kalam was due to sufficiency, not prohibition.

Sanusi addresses a key methodological question: why did the early righteous predecessors (Salaf) not engage in elaborate theological argumentation? In this passage, he explains that their silence was not because of inability or a ban, but because their minds and times were free from doubt, and their beliefs were already secure through clear proofs from the Quran and Sunnah. This lesson unpacks that explanation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overanalyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's precise wording.
Notice the terms 'necessary proofs' and 'darkness of innovations'.
2
Identify the two reasons for silence
The passage gives two reasons why the Salaf did not engage in kalam: purity of minds/times from doubt, and soundness of beliefs through necessary proofs from Quran and Sunnah.
Both reasons emphasize sufficiency, not inability.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: does this passage suggest that kalam is forbidden or simply unnecessary for those with pure faith? Sanusi implies the latter.
This connects to common misunderstandings about the Salaf's practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أدركها هؤلاء الساداتُ .. لَمَا وسعَهم أنْ يفعلوا إلا مثل فعلهم أو أعظم ، لكنَّهم سكتوا عن ذلك ؛ لصفاء أذهانهم وأزمانِهم مِنْ كل وهم ، وصحة عقائد جميعهم بالبراهين الضرورية التي اتَّضحَتْ لهم مِنَ القرآنِ وصاحب الشرع صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، حتى عرف ذلكَ كبيرهم وصغيرهم ، وذكرهم وأنثاهم ، وحُرُّهم ورقيقُهم ، فلم يكن لهم مُخوجٌ إلى ذلكَ ؛ لعدم ظهورِ ظُلمةِ البدع في شموس أزمنتهمُ الشريفة .
These noble ones realized that they could not do otherwise than what they did or something greater, but they remained silent about that, due to the purity of their minds and their times from every doubt (wahm), and the soundness of the beliefs of all of them through the necessary proofs (al-barāhin al-ḍarūriyya) that had become clear to them from the Quran and the possessor of the Law (ṣāḥib al-sharʿ), may God bless him and grant him peace, such that their great and small, their male and female, their free and slave all knew that. So they had no need to resort to that, because the darkness of innovations (bidaʿ) did not appear in the suns of their noble times.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage explains why the early Salaf (the righteous predecessors) did not engage in detailed kalam reasoning even though they were capable of it. The author begins by affirming that these noble figures could have performed the same or even greater feats of theological argumentation. However, they chose silence. The reason is twofold: first, the purity of their minds and times from every doubt (wahm) — their intellectual environment was free from confusion. Second, the beliefs of all of them, regardless of status, were already sound through necessary proofs (al-barāhin al-ḍarūriyya) that had become clear from the Quran and the Prophet himself. Thus, they had no need for elaborate kalam because the darkness of innovations had not yet appeared in their bright era. The point is that their silence was due to sufficiency, not prohibition.

Key Terms
السادات
البراهين الضرورية
البدع
وهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Salaf's silence on kalam means kalam is forbidden (haram) in all circumstances.
Correction: Sanusi shows their silence was due to sufficiency (they already had certainty) and the absence of need, not because kalam is inherently prohibited.

Checkpoint
Why did the early Salaf not engage in detailed kalam reasoning according to Sanusi?
A) They were incapable of it.
B) They considered it forbidden.
C) Their minds and times were pure from doubt, and their beliefs were already secure through necessary proofs.
D) They only relied on taqlid (blind following).

Key Takeaway
The early Salaf's silence on kalam was a sign of their strong, doubt-free faith, not a condemnation of theological reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you content with the clarity of your own faith, or do you rely on elaborate arguments to convince yourself? What would it take for your heart to be as pure from doubt as the Salaf's?
?
The Salaf had no need for detailed theology because their beliefs were clear from Quran and Sunnah. In your daily life, do you seek clarity from these primary sources, or do you turn to secondary debates? What change can you make today to prioritize the Quran and Prophetic guidance over theological arguments?
?
If the darkness of innovations had not appeared in their times, why do we today engage in so much theological discussion? Is it because we lack the pure faith they had, or because we face new doubts? Examine yourself: Is your engagement with these topics driven by a sincere desire for truth, or by confusion and the need to defend yourself?

Teaching Creedal Proofs to Commoners is Obligatory
Sanusi refutes the denial of teaching creedal proofs to commoners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi argues that teaching creedal proofs to commoners is obligatory and how he refutes the opposing view, including clarifying the intent of al-Ghazālī's statement.

Core Idea
Creedal knowledge requires proof; commoners must be taught proofs to fulfill their duty.

Sanusi tackles a controversial claim: that commoners should not be taught the proofs of Islamic creed. He systematically dismantles this position with multiple arguments, showing that teaching proofs is not only permissible but actually obligatory. The passage also clarifies a famous quote from al-Ghazālī, often misused to support this claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the English translation. Notice the argumentative structure as Sanusi responds to an objection.
2
Identify the opposing view
Find where Sanusi states the claim he is refuting: that commoners should not be taught creeds or their proofs, without distinction.
3
Trace Sanusi's arguments
List the points Sanusi uses to refute this claim. He uses logical entailments, analogies, and the consensus of scholars.
There are at least six distinct arguments in this passage.
4
Understand the clarification of al-Ghazālī
Sanusi addresses the proof text from al-Ghazālī and explains its true meaning: not to unsettle firm beliefs with doubts, not to withhold teaching.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why this issue matters for Islamic education and the responsibility to teach correct doctrine to all Muslims.

وأما قول بعض مَنْ لا بصيرة له ولا تحقيق : إِنَّهُ لا تُعلَّمُ العقائد للعوام ، ولا تُذكَرُ لهم براهينها ، مِنْ غير فرق منه بين واضحها الذي يمكنهم فهمُهُ وبينَ غيرِهِ .. فواضحُ الفسادِ ؛ لأنَّهُ إذا كانَتِ المعرفة واجبة على الأعيان بإجماع على ما ذكرَهُ كَثيرٌ مِنَ الأَئِمَّةِ ، بل هي نفسُ الإيمان أو لازمةٌ له ، وهي لا تحصل إلا بالبرهان .. فكيف لا يتأكَّدُ السعي في تعليمهم ما يُحصِّلُها ؟! وإذا جازَتْ قراءة القرآنِ والأحاديث النبوية بحضرتهم مِنْ غيرِ شرح لهم لمعانيهما ، معَ أنَّ فيهما ظواهر يجب تأويلها بإجماع ، وبسببِ فهمها على ظاهرِها هَلَكَ كثيرٌ مِنَ الخَلْقِ .. فَلَأَنْ يجوز تعليمهم العقائد مشروحة بأدلَّتِها التي تسعُها عقولهم أحرى ، بل يتعيَّنُ في حقهم ذلك ؛ لأنَّ التكليف بمعرفة عقائدِ الإيمان بالنظر الصحيح لا فرق فيهِ عند المحققينَ بينَ العامِّي وغيرِهِ ، وإذا كانَ يتعيَّنُ تعليمهم ما يَخصُّهم في الفروع ؛ كالصلاة والزكاة ونحوهما.. فكيف لا يتعيَّن تعليمهم ما يخصهم في أصول دينهم، وما يكونون به مؤمنين حقاً ؟! وزعمُهُ أَنَّهُ لا يُحتاجُ إلى ذلكَ في حقهم ؛ لحصول المعرفة لجميعهم .. مكابرةٌ ، وكذبٌ يفضحُهُ مشاهدة التخليط منه ومنهم في كثيرِ مِنَ العقائدِ ، ولم يحصل لهم الحقُّ فيها ولو بالتقليد ، فكيف بالنظر ؟! وليسَتِ المعرفةُ بالعقائدِ ضروريةً حتى يُدعى حصولها لكلِّ أحدٍ بغير نظر ، بلِ الذي يتبادر إلى الوَهْمِ أوَّلاً إِنَّما هو الفسادُ في كثيرٍ مِنَ العقائدِ حتى يفتحَ الله سبحانه وتعالى لمَنْ شاءَ في تطهير القلبِ مِنْ ذلك بالنظر الصحيح . وأما احتجاجه على ذلكَ بقولِ بعض الأئمة : ( لا تُحرَّكُ على العوام عقائدهم (۱) .. فهَوَس وسوء فهم منه ؛ لأنَّ تحريك عقائدِهم إنَّما يصدقُ في إزالتها مِنْ قلوبهم ، وزحزحتها عن تصميمهم بإيراد شُبَه عليهم تُشكّكهم في الحقِّ ، وتُوجِبُ لهم التردُّد فيه ، كما فعلتِ المبتدعةُ بهم في أزمنة استطالتهم على هذه الأمَّةِ ، وأمَّا تعليم العوام العقائد الصحيحة بأدلَّتِها فليس بتحريك عقائدهم بل هو تقرير لها وإثبات . (۱) هو حجة الإسلام الغزالي ، قال ذلك في الاقتصاد في الاعتقاد » ( ص ١٠٦ ) ، وذاك قوله في حق العامة الذين صح اعتقادهم ، واشتغلوا بعد ذلك إما بعبادة أو صناعة : ( فهؤلاء ينبغي أن يتركوا على ما هم عليه ، ولا تُحرَّكَ عقائدهم بالاستحثاث على تعلم هذا العلم )
As for the saying of someone who has no insight and no verification: that the creeds (al-ʿaqāʾid) should not be taught to the common people (al-ʿawāmm), nor should their proofs be mentioned to them, without him distinguishing between that which is clear and they can understand and that which is not — it is clearly corrupt. Because if knowledge (al-maʿrifa) is individually obligatory by consensus, as many of the imams have mentioned — indeed it is faith itself or necessary for it, and it is only attained through proof (burhān) — then how can striving to teach them what attains it not be emphasized? And if the recitation of the Quran and prophetic hadiths in their presence without explanation of their meanings is permissible, even though they contain apparent meanings (ẓawāhir) that must be interpreted (taʾwīl) by consensus, and due to understanding them in their apparent sense many of creation have perished, then how much more likely that teaching them the creeds explained with their proofs that their minds can accommodate is permissible? Rather, it is incumbent upon them, because the obligation to know the creeds of faith by correct reflection (al-naẓar al-ṣaḥīḥ) is, according to the verifiers, no different between the commoner and others. And if it is incumbent to teach them what pertains to them in the branches (al-furūʿ), like prayer, zakāt, and the like, then how is it not incumbent to teach them what pertains to them in the principles of their religion (uṣūl dīnihim), and that by which they are truly believers? And his claim that this is not needed for them because knowledge is attained for all of them is stubbornness and a lie that is exposed by observing the confusion from him and from them in many of the creeds; and the truth has not been attained by them even by taqlīd, so how about by reflection? And the knowledge of creeds is not necessary (ḍarūriyya) such that it can be claimed that everyone attains it without reflection. Rather, what first comes to mind is corruption in many of the creeds, until God, exalted is He, opens for whom He wills the purification of the heart from that by correct reflection. And as for his argument on that by the saying of some imams: 'Do not stir the creeds of the common people from their place' — it is delusion and misunderstanding. For stirring their creeds is only true in the sense of removing them from their hearts and shifting them from their firmness by presenting to them doubts (shubah) that make them doubt the truth and cause them to hesitate in it, as the innovators (al-mubtadiʿa) did to them in times when they gained ascendancy over this community. As for teaching the common people the correct creeds with their proofs, that is not stirring their creeds but rather confirming them and establishing them. (1) He is the Proof of Islam al-Ghazālī, said that in 'al-Iqtiṣād fī al-Iʿtiqād' (p. 106), and that is his statement concerning the common people whose belief is sound and who after that occupy themselves with either worship or craft: 'These should be left as they are, and their creeds should not be stirred by urging them to learn this science.'
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (radd) of the claim that commoners should not be taught creedal proofs. The author, Sanusi, systematically dismantles this position. He begins by identifying the opposing view: that commoners should not be taught creeds or their proofs, regardless of whether the proofs are clear or abstruse. He declares this view 'clearly corrupt.' He then provides multiple arguments. First, knowledge (maʿrifa) is individually obligatory (wājib ʿaynī) by consensus, and it is attained only through proof (burhān). Therefore, teaching the means to it become obligatory. Second, if it is permissible to recite Quran and hadith to commoners without explanation, even though those texts contain verses that require interpretation and have led many astray when taken literally, then it is even more fitting to teach creeds with explanations and proofs tailored to their intellectual capacity. Third, the obligation to know creed through correct reflection applies equally to the commoner and the elite according to the verifiers (al-muḥaqqiqūn). Fourth, since commoners are taught the branches of religion (furūʿ) like prayer and zakāt, they must likewise be taught the principles (uṣūl) of their religion. Fifth, the claim that commoners already possess knowledge is a lie, as seen in their confusion about many creeds; they have not even attained truth by taqlīd, let alone investigation. Sixth, knowledge of creeds is not innate (ḍarūriyya) — the initial inclination is towards corruption, requiring correct reflection to purify the heart. Finally, he addresses the citation of an imam (al-Ghazālī) who said 'Do not stir the creeds of the common people.' Sanusi explains that this refers to unsettling their firm beliefs by casting doubts, not to teaching them correct creeds with proofs, which actually strengthens their faith.

التقليد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that commoners should not be taught any proofs of creed, citing al-Ghazālī's statement 'Do not stir the creeds of the common people.'
Correction: Al-Ghazālī meant not to unsettle their firm beliefs by casting doubts, not to refrain from teaching correct creeds with proofs. Teaching proofs is actually a reinforcement, not a stirring.

Checkpoint
What is Sanusi's main argument for why teaching creedal proofs to commoners is obligatory?
A) Because commoners cannot understand proofs without teaching.
B) Because knowledge of creed is individually obligatory and attained only through proof.
C) Because al-Ghazālī said so.
D) Because commoners are less capable than elites.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi argues that teaching creedal proofs to commoners is not only permissible but obligatory, as it fulfills the duty of knowledge and strengthens faith, contrary to those who misinterpret scholarly warnings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever withheld a creedal proof from someone, assuming they wouldn't understand, thereby failing in your duty to help them attain true faith? What will you change starting today?
?
Are you content to simply follow the beliefs of your family or community without personally reflecting on the proofs of your faith? If so, what is holding you back from seeking that knowledge?
?
When you encounter someone who dismisses the need to teach proofs to 'common people,' do you recognize the harm in that view? How will you respond to such a claim with the clarity of this lesson?

Teaching Common People Correct Beliefs is Obligatory
Sanusi argues for the obligation of teaching common people correct beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation of teaching common people the fundamentals of Islamic creed and why the claim of innate knowledge is false.

Core Idea
Teaching creed is more essential than teaching legal branches.

Sanusi addresses a critical objection: why bother teaching common people complex theological matters? He argues compellingly that if we teach them practical religious duties, we must teach them the foundations of belief. This lesson unpacks his argument and the refutation of the claim that knowledge is innate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the full argument.
Notice the tone of refutation.
2
Identify the a fortiori argument
Identify how Sanusi compares teaching furu' (branches) to teaching usul (foundations). Understand why the latter is more necessary.
This is an argument from stronger to weaker.
3
Examine the refutation of innate knowledge
Sanusi rejects the claim that common people already know the truth. Find his proof from observable reality.
He calls it stubbornness and a lie.
4
Understand the role of reflection (nazar)
Recognize that correct belief requires intellectual effort, not just imitation. Only through proper reflection can the heart be purified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عند المحققين بين العامي وغيره، وإذا كان يتعين تعليمهم ما يخصهم في الفروع؛ كالصلاة والزكاة ونحوهما.. فكيف لا يتعين تعليمهم ما يخصهم في أصول دينهم، وما يكونون به مؤمنين حقاً؟! وزعمه أنه لا يحتاج إلى ذلك في حقهم؛ لحصول المعرفة لجميعهم .. مكابرة، وكذب يفضحه مشاهدة التخليط منه ومنهم في كثير من العقائد، ولم يحصل لهم الحق فيها ولو بالتقليد، فكيف بالنظر؟! وليست المعرفة بالعقائد ضرورية حتى يدعى حصولها لكل أحد بغير نظر، بل الذي يتبادر إلى الوهم أولاً إنما هو الفساد في كثير من العقائد حتى يفتح الله سبحانه وتعالى لمن شاء في تطهير القلب من ذلك بالنظر الصحيح
According to the investigators, between the common person and others: if it is necessary to teach them what concerns them in the branches (furu'), such as prayer and zakat and the like, then how is it not necessary to teach them what concerns them in the foundations of their religion (usul dinihim), and that by which they are truly believers? And his claim that there is no need for that in their case because knowledge is obtained for all of them is stubbornness and a lie that is exposed by the observation of confusion from him and from them in many of the beliefs, and the truth has not been obtained for them even by blind imitation (taqlid), so how by reflection (nazar)?! And knowledge of beliefs is not necessary (daruriyya) such that it is claimed that it is obtained for everyone without reflection; rather, what first comes to mind is corruption in many of the beliefs, until Allah, glorified and exalted, opens for whomever He wills the purification of the heart from that through correct reflection.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. The author begins by establishing a comparison: if it is obligatory to teach common people about practical religious duties (like prayer and zakat), then it is even more obligatory to teach them about the foundations of their religion (usul al-din), because without correct belief, they cannot be true believers. This is an a fortiori argument (qiyas aulawi). The author then refutes the opponent's claim that common people do not need such teaching because they already possess knowledge of these matters innately. He denounces this as stubbornness and a lie, pointing out that observable reality shows confusion among them regarding many beliefs. Even if they had some belief by way of taqlid, it is not sufficient. He then clarifies that knowledge of beliefs is not intuitive (daruri) such that it can be obtained without reflection. On the contrary, what initially occurs to the mind is corruption in many beliefs, and only through correct reflection (nazar) can Allah purify the heart.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Common people do not need to learn kalam because they already have innate knowledge of correct beliefs.
Correction: Observable reality shows confusion among common people about many beliefs; true knowledge requires reflection (nazar), not innate intuition.

Checkpoint

B) Because it is as important as teaching them about furu', and even more foundational

Key Takeaway
The obligation to teach common people correct beliefs is firmly established, and the notion of innate knowledge is refuted by observable reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you see confusion or false beliefs among common Muslims, do you dismiss it as inevitable, or do you feel a personal responsibility to correct it? What step will you take today to ensure those around you have true faith?

Refuting the Misuse of the Saying Not to Stir Beliefs
Sanusi distinguishes between harmful stirring and beneficial teaching of beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct meaning of the prohibition against stirring beliefs and why teaching correct beliefs with proofs is not only permissible but praiseworthy.

Core Idea
Teaching correct beliefs is not stirring; it is confirming and strengthening.

Some argue that we should not disturb common people's beliefs, using a saying from the imams. Sanusi shows this is a misunderstanding. He explains that 'stirring' means casting doubts to uproot correct beliefs. Teaching correct beliefs with proofs does the opposite: it confirms and strengthens faith. He then argues that if beliefs are corrupt, we must stir them out. This passage clarifies a critical methodological principle for Islamic education.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note how Sanusi begins by dismissing the opponent's argument as 'madness and misunderstanding'.
The passage is quite long but forms a single argument.
2
Identify the two scenarios
Sanusi distinguishes two cases: (1) teaching correct beliefs to those who already have correct beliefs, and (2) removing corrupt beliefs. Notice the difference in his ruling for each.
The first case is not stirring; the second case is required.
3
Understand the key distinction
The key is the definition of 'tahrik' (stirring). It is not teaching, but casting doubts to uproot. Teaching strengthens; doubts weaken.
Sanusi uses the Quranic verse to support the removal of falsehood.
4
Reflect on the pedagogical principle
This lesson shows that teaching correct beliefs with proofs is an act of advice and worship. It elevates from taqlid to ma'rifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما احتجاجه على ذلك بقول بعض الأئمة: (لا تحرك على العوام عقائدهم) .. فهو هوس وسوء فهم منه؛ لأن تحريك عقائدهم إنما يصدق في إزالتها من قلوبهم، وزحزحتها عن تصميمهم بإيراد شبه عليهم تشككهم في الحق، وتوجب لهم التردد فيه، كما فعلت بهم في أزمنة استطالتهم على هذه الأمة، وأما تعليم العوام العقائد الصحيحة، ثم تأييدها مع ذلك بالبراهين القطعية المتضح فهمها لديهم؛ بطول التكرار الذي يوجب للنفس الطمأنينة، وعدم قبولها التشكك في الحق بوجه من الوجوه .. فلا يخفى أن هذا من أعظم النصيحة لهم، ومن أفضل ما يتقرب به إلى الله تعالى، وليس فيه تحريك لعقائدهم الصحيحة، بل هو تثبيت لها وتقوية لرسوخها ونقل للمقلد منهم فيها من درجة التقليد المختلف في إيمان صاحبه إلى درجة المعرفة المعتد بها إجماعاً. نعم؛ إذا كانت في قلوبهم عقائد فاسدة فلا شك أن بذكر الحق وإيضاح برهانه يتحرك ذلك الباطل وينزعج للخروج، بل نقذف بالحق على الباطل فيدمغه فإذا هو زاهق [الأنبياء:18]. ولا خفاء: أن التحريك لمثل هذه العقائد المهلكة صاحبها في الآخرة، والسعي في تطهير قلبه منها وإنقاذه من وثاق أسرها .. متعين على كل من له قدرة على ذلك، ويرجى له من ثواب الله تعالى على بمحض فضله جل وعز ما لا يفي بعدده ديوان، ولا يضبطه ميزان، ولأن يهدي الله تعالى بك رجلاً واحداً.. خير لك من حمر
As for his argument by the saying of some imams: 'Do not stir the beliefs of the common people' — it is madness and misunderstanding on his part, because 'stirring their beliefs' only applies to removing them from their hearts and uprooting them from their conviction by introducing doubts that make them doubt the truth and cause them to hesitate in it, as done to them in times of their predominance over this ummah. As for teaching the common people correct beliefs, then supporting them with demonstrative proofs whose understanding is clear to them through long repetition that brings tranquility to the soul and prevents acceptance of doubt about the truth in any way — it is no secret that this is among the greatest advice for them and among the best acts by which one draws near to Allah, and there is no stirring of their correct beliefs; rather it is a confirmation and strengthening of their firmness and a transfer of the imitator among them from the level of imitation (taqlid) regarding which the iman of its possessor is disputed to the level of knowledge (ma'rifa) which is considered valid by consensus. Yes, if there are corrupt beliefs in their hearts, there is no doubt that by mentioning the truth and clarifying its proof, that falsehood is stirred and disturbed to leave. Rather, 'We hurl truth against falsehood, and it destroys it, and behold it vanishes' [21:18]. And it is no secret that stirring such beliefs that destroy their possessor in the Hereafter, and striving to purify his heart from them and save him from the bonds of their captivity, is incumbent upon everyone who has the ability to do so, and he hopes from the reward of Allah Almighty by His pure bounty, glorified and exalted, that which no register can count nor scale measure. 'If Allah guides through you a single man, it is better for you than red...'
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the argument that one should not disturb the beliefs of common people. The author attacks the opponent's use of the quote from some imams as madness and misunderstanding. He explains that 'stirring beliefs' (tahrik al-'aqa'id) refers specifically to removing beliefs from hearts by casting doubts, thereby causing hesitation. The author contrasts this with teaching correct beliefs and supporting them with definitive proofs. Such teaching is not disturbance; it is confirmation (tathbit) and strengthening (taqwiyat). It elevates the common person from the level of taqlid (whose iman is disputed) to the level of certain knowledge (ma'rifa) that is valid by consensus. Then the author addresses the case of false beliefs: if the common person has corrupt beliefs, then by presenting the truth and clarifying its proof, the falsehood is stirred and expelled. This is praiseworthy and even obligatory. He cites the Quranic verse [21:18] to illustrate that truth destroys falsehood. He concludes by stating that removing such destructive beliefs is incumbent on those who have the ability, and the reward for guiding even one person is immense, alluding to the hadith about red camels.

شبه
تصميم
تقليد
معرفة
براهين قطعية

عقائد فاسدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That teaching a common person new beliefs after they already have beliefs is disturbing their faith.
Correction: Sanusi explains that teaching correct beliefs with proofs is not disturbing but confirming; disturbing only occurs when doubts are cast to uproot already correct beliefs.

Checkpoint
What does the author say is the true meaning of 'stirring the beliefs of common people'?
A) Teaching them correct beliefs
B) Casting doubts to uproot their correct beliefs
C) Making them reflect on their beliefs
D) Changing their beliefs to match the scholar's view

Key Takeaway
Teaching correct beliefs with proofs strengthens faith, while stirring applies only to casting doubts to remove correct beliefs; removing corrupt beliefs is obligatory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you avoid teaching someone about Islam because you fear you might 'stir' their beliefs, are you actually protecting them or depriving them of the confirmation that would strengthen their faith? Will you commit to teaching one person this week with clarity and patience?
?
Reflect on a time when someone corrected a wrong belief you held. Did it feel like an attack or a rescue? How does that memory shape your willingness now to gently 'stir' false beliefs in others, knowing it might be the means of their salvation?
?
The passage says that teaching with proofs through repetition brings tranquility and prevents doubt. Do you feel that tranquility in your own heart regarding your beliefs? If not, what step can you take today to move from imitation to certainty in at least one area of your faith?

Teaching Proofs to the Common People: A Defense
Sanusi defends teaching proofs to common people as strengthening faith, not harming it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi argues that teaching definitive proofs to common people strengthens their faith, moves them from imitation to certainty, and is a great act of counsel—not a cause of harm.

Core Idea
Teaching common people definitive proofs does not weaken faith—it moves them from imitation to certainty.

Sanusi addresses a common concern: that teaching theological proofs to ordinary believers might disturb their simple faith. In this passage, he argues the opposite—that such teaching, done with repetition and clarity, actually strengthens faith, removes doubts, and even helps those with false beliefs return to the truth. He considers this one of the greatest forms of sincere counsel to the community.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the full argument.
Notice the passionate tone and the use of Quranic verse and hadith.
2
Identify Sanusi's main claim
Find where Sanusi states that teaching proofs to common people benefits both those with correct beliefs and those with false beliefs.
He says it does not disturb correct beliefs but strengthens them.
3
Examine the treatment of false beliefs
See how he uses the Quranic verse (Al-Anbiya' 18) to argue that truth crushes falsehood when presented with proof.
He considers stirring false beliefs a necessary step for purification.
4
Reflect on the lament and conclusion
Consider Sanusi's criticism of scholars who neglect usul al-din and his call to gratitude for those who attain the truth.
This shows the urgency of the issue in his time.

العقائد الصحيحة ، ثم تأييدها مع ذلكَ بالبراهين القطعية المتَّضِحِ فهمها لديهم ؛ بطولِ التكرار الذي يُوجِبُ للنفسِ الطُّمأنينةَ ، وعدم قبولِها التشكُكَ في الحقِّ بوجهِ مِنَ الوجوه .. فلا يخفى أنَّ هذا مِنْ أعظم النصيحة لهم ، ومِنْ أفضل ما يُتقرَّبُ بِهِ إِلى اللهِ تعالى ، وليس فيه تحريك لعقائدهم الصحيحة ، بل هو تثبيت لها وتقوية لرسوخها ونقل للمُقدِّدِ منهم فيها مِنْ درجةِ التقليدِ المُختلفِ في إيمانِ صاحبِهِ إلى درجة المعرفة المعتد بها إجماعاً
نعم ؛ إذا كانَتْ في قلوبهم عقائد فاسدة فلا شكَ أَنَّ بذكرِ الحقِّ وإيضاح برهانِهِ يتحرَّكُ ذلكَ الباطل وينزعج للخروج ، بَلْ نَقْذِفُ بِالْحَقِّ عَلَى الْبَاطِلِ فَيَدْمَعُهُ فَإِذَا هُوَ زَاهِقٌ [الأنبياء : ۱۸]
ولا خفاءَ : أنَّ التحريكَ لمثل هذهِ العقائدِ المهلكة صاحبَها في الآخرة ، والسعي في تطهير قلبهِ منها وإنقاذِهِ مِنْ وَثَاقِ أَسرِها . . مُتعيِّن على كلِّ مَنْ له قدرة على ذلكَ ، ويُرجى لهُ مِنْ ثواب الله تعالى على بمحض فضلِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ ما لا يفي بعَدِّهِ ديوان ، ولا يضبطه ميزان ، وَلَأَنْ يَهْدِيَ اللهُ تَعَالَى بِكَ رَجُلاً وَاحِداً خَيْرٌ لَكَ مِنْ حُمْرِ النَّعَمِ أي : مِنَ التصدق بها
وبالجملة : فتقرير عقائدِ التوحيدِ ببراهينها الواضحة على العوام لا يزيدهم إلا خيراً ؛ لأنَّ الضالّ منهم يرجعُ عن ضلاله ، والمهتدي يزدادُ هُدى وقوَّةً في إيمانِهِ ، ورسوخاً في إيقانِهِ ؛ فالسعي في قطع ذلك شَيْطَةٌ لا شك فيها
وما أحوج كثيراً مِنْ مُتفقهة زماننا إلى تعلمهم أصول دينهم ، والاشتغال بما يعنيهم عن كثير مما لا يعنيهم ! فكيف بعوامهم ؟! لكن أينَ الحقُّ ؟! وأينَ أهلُهُ ؟! وأينَ مَنْ يقبلُه على تقدير وجودِهِ نادراً ؟! فمَنْ ظفر بمعرفةِ الحقِّ في هذا الزمانِ ، ثم وُفِّقَ للعمل به .. فليكثر مِنْ شكر الله تعالى غاية جهدِهِ ، وليَعُدَّ ذلكَ مِنْ خوارق العادةِ في هذا الزمانِ ، والله المستعانُ ، ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله .
The correct beliefs, then supporting them with definitive proofs whose understanding is clear to them; by the length of repetition that causes the soul tranquility, and the non-acceptance of doubting the truth in any way... So it is not hidden that this is among the greatest counsel for them, and among the best acts by which one draws near to Allah Almighty, and it does not involve disturbing their correct beliefs, but rather it is a confirmation for them and a strengthening of their rootedness, and a transfer for the one who is a muqallid among them from the degree of taqlid (blind imitation) regarding which there is disagreement about the faith of its possessor, to the degree of ma'rifa (certain knowledge) that is relied upon by consensus. Yes; if there are corrupt beliefs in their hearts, there is no doubt that by mentioning the truth and clarifying its proof, that falsehood is stirred and distressed to exit; rather, 'We hurl the truth against falsehood, and it crushes it, and lo, it vanishes' [Al-Anbiya' 18]. And it is not hidden: that stirring such beliefs that destroy their possessor in the Hereafter, and striving to purify his heart from them and rescue him from the bond of their captivity... is incumbent upon everyone who has the ability to do so, and is hoped for him from the reward of Allah Almighty—by His pure grace, may He be exalted and glorified—what a register cannot count, nor a scale measure; 'For Allah to guide through you a single man is better for you than red camels' i.e., than giving them in charity. In summary: presenting the beliefs of tawhid (monotheism) with their clear proofs to the common people does not increase them except in goodness; because the misguided among them returns from his misguidance, and the rightly guided increases in guidance and strength in his faith, and rootedness in his certainty. So striving to cut that off is a devilish prompting, no doubt about it. And how much in need are many of the mutafaqqiha (students of fiqh) of our time to learn the principles of their religion, and to occupy themselves with what concerns them, instead of much that does not concern them! So how about their common people?! But where is the truth?! And where are its people?! And where is one who accepts it, given its rarity?! So whoever obtains knowledge of the truth in this time, and then is granted success to act upon it... let him thank Allah Almighty as much as he can, and consider that among the extraordinary things in this time. And Allah is the one sought for help, and there is no power and no strength except through Allah.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a defense of teaching theological proofs to the common people ('awamm). The author argues that such teaching, when done with definitive proofs and repeated explanation, does not disturb correct beliefs but rather strengthens them and moves the believer from mere taqlid (imitation) to certain knowledge (ma'rifa). If the person already holds false beliefs, hearing the truth and its evidence will upset and expel that falsehood, as the Quranic verse states: 'We hurl the truth against falsehood, and it crushes it.' The author then emphasizes that removing corrupt beliefs is a religious duty for those able, with immense reward. He concludes that teaching tawhid to 'awamm always benefits: the misguided return and the guided grow stronger. He laments that even scholars of fiqh neglect usul al-din, and encourages gratitude for those few who attain the truth.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Teaching definitive proofs to common people disturbs their simple faith and causes confusion.
Correction: Sanusi argues that such teaching actually strengthens correct beliefs, provides tranquility, and moves the believer from imitation to certainty. For those with false beliefs, it exposes and removes falsehood, leading to guidance.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the effect of presenting the beliefs of tawhid with clear proofs to the common people?
A) It causes confusion and doubt in their faith.
B) It only benefits the misguided, not the rightly guided.
C) It increases goodness for all: the misguided return and the guided strengthen.
D) It is only beneficial if the people are already scholars.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi affirms that teaching tawhid with proofs always benefits the common people and is a profound act of counsel, countering the fear that it disturbs their faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you content to hold your faith based on imitation (taqlid) from your family or society, or have you sought the definitive proofs that give your soul tranquility and protect you from doubt? What specific belief do you hold without proof, and will you study it until certainty settles in your heart?
?
When you encounter someone with false or weak beliefs, do you avoid the conversation for fear of 'stirring' them, or do you carefully present the truth with its proof, trusting that Allah crushes falsehood? What is the one thing you have avoided saying that you must now say, and who is the person you need to speak to?
?
You have read that guiding even one person is better than the most prized possessions. Look at your life: how many people have you guided to the truth through clear proofs? If the answer is none, what has stopped you? And what will you change today to make guidance your mission?

Refuting Taqlid in the Principles of Religion
Sanusi refutes taqlid in usul al-din and praises the science of kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the science of kalam is superior to blind imitation in the principles of religion and why taqlid is condemned.

Core Idea
Blind imitation in creed is lowly and harmful; Allah guides those He loves to reasoned faith.

Sanusi opens his discussion of methodology by making a bold claim: the science of kalam is the most excellent and most obligatory of sciences. But he also warns against mere imitation in matters of belief. This passage sets the stage for the entire study of theology by distinguishing between the path of guidance and the path of ruin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text and its English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the strong language used for taqlid.
2
Identify the two groups described
The passage contrasts those whom Allah intends good for with those satisfied with taqlid. List their respective outcomes.
3
Reflect on the term 'taqlid'
Understand what taqlid means in this context: accepting beliefs without proof.
This is a key term.
4
Connect to your own learning
Ask yourself: why is it important to seek proof for beliefs, rather than just follow what others say?
This lesson establishes the rationale for studying kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إبطال القول بالتقليد في أصول الدين
وبالجملة: فمَنْ أَرادَ اللهُ بهِ خيراً عرَّفَهُ مراشده ، وفتح له في معرفةِ هذا العلم الذي هو أفضلُ العلوم وأوجبها ، وأولى ما يشتغل به كلُّ مُوفَّقِ ، والرضا بحرفةِ التقليدِ دناءة في الهمَّةِ والدين ، وتعرُّض لما يُخشى مِنْ عظم عذابِ القبرِ ، وهولِ الخلودِ في النار والعياذ بالله
Refuting the claim of taqlid (blind imitation) in the principles of religion. In summary: Whoever Allah intends good for, He makes known to him his proper paths, and opens for him understanding of this science ('ilm) which is the most excellent and most obligatory of sciences, and the most worthy pursuit for every divinely aided person. And being satisfied with the craft of taqlid is baseness in aspiration and religion, and exposure to what is feared of the great punishment of the grave, and the terror of eternity in the Fire—and we seek refuge with Allah.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a succinct refutation of taqlid in usul al-din (the principles of religion). The author states that the one Allah intends good for is guided to understand 'this science'—meaning the science of kalam ('ilm al-kalam)—which is described as the best and most obligatory of sciences, and the most deserving of attention for every successful person. In contrast, being content with taqlid is considered lowliness in both aspiration and religion, and it exposes one to severe punishment in the grave and the terror of eternal punishment in Hell. The passage thus establishes the superiority of reasoned faith (based on proof) over blind imitation in the most fundamental matters of belief.

المراشد

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think taqlid is acceptable in all religious matters.
Correction: The author restricts its condemnation to the principles of religion (usul al-din) and praises the science of kalam as the proper method.

Checkpoint

A) As being divinely aided and blessed.
B) As having low aspiration and religion, and exposed to punishment.
C) As being excused because of their inability.
D) As following the way of the righteous predecessors.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi teaches that the science of kalam is the most excellent science, and that blind imitation in creed is an act of spiritual baseness that incurs divine punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a belief about Allah or the afterlife simply because you were raised with it, without seeking to understand the proof? If so, are you not exposed to the punishment this passage warns of? What will you do today to start seeking that understanding?
?
Do you truly desire Allah to intend good for you? If yes, then where is your effort to learn the science of kalam or at least the proofs of your creed? Leave aside the comfort of imitation and ask yourself: are you satisfied with baseness in your religion?
?
The terror of eternity in the Fire is a real possibility for those who persist in taqlid in creed. What specific belief do you hold that you cannot prove from reason or revelation? What is stopping you from verifying it? Commit today to learning the evidence for one foundational belief.
