Teaching Aqeedah with Proofs
Sanusi argues for teaching proofs of tawhid to commoners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi’s argument for teaching theological proofs to common people and why he considers preventing it a devilish act.

Core Idea
Teaching aqeedah with proofs benefits everyone: the misguided return and the guided strengthen.

Sanusi makes a passionate case for teaching the clear proofs of tawhid to laypeople. He argues that such teaching only brings good: it guides the misguided and strengthens the faithful. He then laments those who neglect this duty, calling opposition to it satanic. This passage reveals the practical concern of a theologian for the spiritual welfare of the community.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp Sanusi's flow.
Notice the strong opening statement 'لا يزيدهم إلا خيراً'.
2
Identify the two benefits
Sanusi explains that teaching proofs helps the misguided return and the guided increase in faith and certainty. Highlight these in the text.
3
Reflect on his lament
Read his criticism of 'pseudo-jurists' and his remarks about the scarcity of truth. Consider why he calls opposition 'devilish'.
He concludes that attaining truth in that time is a miracle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالجملة : فتقرير عقائدِ التوحيدِ ببراهينها الواضحة على العوام لا يزيدهم إلا خيراً ؛ لأنَّ الضالّ منهم يرجعُ عن ضلاله ، والمهتدي يزدادُ هُدى وقوَّةً في إيمانِهِ ، ورسوخاً في إيقانِهِ ؛ فالسعي في قطع ذلك شَيطة لا شك فيها . وما أحوج كثيراً مِنْ مُتفقهة زماننا إلى تعلمهم أصول دينهم ، والاشتغال بما يعنيهم عن كثير مما لا يعنيهم ! فكيف بعوامهم ؟! لكن أينَ الحقُّ ؟! وأينَ أهلُهُ ؟! وأينَ مَنْ يقبلُه على تقدير وجودِهِ نادراً ؟! فمَنْ ظفر بمعرفةِ الحقِّ في هذا الزمانِ ، ثم وُفِّقَ للعمل به .. فليكثر مِنْ شكر الله تعالى غاية جهدِهِ ، وليَعُدَّ ذلكَ مِنْ خوارق العادةِ في هذا الزمانِ ، والله المستعانُ ، ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله .
In summary: presenting the doctrines of tawhid (monotheism) with their clear proofs to the common people does not increase them except in goodness; because the misguided among them returns from his misguidance, and the guided increases in guidance and strength in his faith, and firmness in his certainty. So striving to cut that off is an undeniable devilish act. How much more do many of the pseudo-jurists of our time need to learn the fundamentals of their religion and occupy themselves with what concerns them over much that does not concern them! How about their common people?! But where is the truth?! And where are its people?! And where is the one who accepts it, if it exists, rarely?! So whoever attains knowledge of the truth in this time, and then is granted success to act upon it, let him abundantly thank Allah Almighty with all his effort, and consider that as one of the miracles (khawariq al-‘ada) in this time. And Allah is the Grantor of success, and there is no power nor strength except with Allah.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is an argument in favor of teaching Aqeedah with proofs to the common people. The author begins by stating his thesis: presenting the clear proofs of tawhid to laypeople only increases them in good. He then explains why: the misguided person abandons his error, and the guided person gains more strength in faith and certainty. Therefore, any attempt to prevent such teaching is undoubtedly a satanic act. He then laments the state of many jurists of his time who neglect learning usul al-din while busying themselves with what is less important, so how much more so for the common people? He expresses regret over the scarcity of truth and those who accept it. He concludes by encouraging anyone who attains knowledge of the truth and acts upon it to thank Allah abundantly, considering it a miracle in that age, and ends with a prayer for divine assistance.

Nullifying Taqleed in the Fundamentals of Religion
Sanusi refutes taqleed as insufficient for knowledge in usul al-din.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why taqleed (blind imitation) cannot produce the certainty required for true faith, and how Sanusi uses hadith and logical reasoning to refute it.

Core Idea
Faith requires certainty, but taqleed can only give contradictory assents — not true knowledge.

Sanusi begins by declaring that taqleed has no place in the fundamentals of religion. He argues that faith demands certainty and knowledge, which can only be attained through sound reflection, not blind imitation. To prove this, he cites two hadiths that make certainty a condition for entry into Paradise, and then presents a logical demonstration that taqleed-based assent cannot be considered knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the English translation to understand the overall meaning before analysis.
Notice the strong language: 'dana'a' (baseness) and 'ta'arud' (exposure).
2
Identify the two main pieces of evidence
Sanusi uses two hadiths to show that certainty is required. Find them and note what they say about the condition for Paradise.
The hadiths are from Abu Hurairah and Muslim.
3
Understand the logical argument
Sanusi argues that if taqleed-based assent were knowledge, contradictory assents could both be true. Why is that impossible? Because knowledge is an attribute that does not admit opposites.
Think about how this shows taqleed cannot produce genuine certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إبطال القول بالتقليد في أصول الدين ] وبالجملة : فمَنْ أَرادَ اللهُ بهِ خيراً عرَّفَهُ مراشده ، وفتح له في معرفةِ هذا العلم الذي هو أفضلُ العلوم وأوجبها ، وأولى ما يشتغل به كلُّ مُوفَّقِ ، والرضا بحرفةِ التقليدِ دناءة في الهمَّةِ والدين ، وتعرُّض لما يُخشى مِنْ عظم عذابِ القبرِ ، وهولِ الخلودِ في النار والعياذ بالله تعالى (۱) ؛ لأنَّ المطلوب في الإيمانِ اليقين والمعرفة ، وذلك لا يكونُ إلا بالنظر الصحيح . وفي حديث أبي هريرةَ رضي الله تعالى عنه : ( مَنْ لَقِيتَ وَرَاءَ هَذَا الْحَائِطِ يَشْهَدُ أَنْ لا إِلَهَ إلا اللهُ مُسْتَيْقِناً قَلْبُهُ . . فَبَشِّرْهُ بِالْجَنَّةِ (٢) وفي ( مسلم ) : ( مَنْ مَاتَ وَهُوَ يَعْلَمُ أَنْ لا إِلَهَ إلا الله . . دَخَلَ الْجَنَّةَ ((٣) فانظر كيف شرط في هذين الحديثين اليقين والعلم ، وهما ضدَّانِ ولا يصح أنْ يُقالَ : ( الجزم لأجل التقليد علم ) لأنَّهُ لو كانَ ذلكَ الجزمُ علماً .. لزم اجتماع الضدين (٥) ؛ في الجزم بحدوثه تقليداً ، والجزم بقدمِهِ كذلكَ أيضاً ؛ لأنَّ العلم صفةٌ لا تحتمل النقيض بوجه ، فيلزمُ أنْ يكونَ العالم في نفس الأمر قديماً وحادثاً ! وذلكَ ممَّا لا يُعقَلُ . وهذان الحديثانِ يُفسّرانَ كلَّ ما أُجمِلَ مِنْ أحاديث الشهادتين
[Chapter: Nullifying the claim of taqleed (blind imitation) in the fundamentals of religion] In summary: whoever Allah intends good for, He makes him know his ways, and opens for him knowledge of this science, which is the best of sciences and the most obligatory, and the most deserving of occupation for every successful person. And being content with the profession of taqleed is baseness in aspiration and religion, and an exposure to what is feared of the great punishment of the grave and the terror of eternal fire – may Allah protect us – because what is required in faith is certainty and knowledge, and that is only attained through sound reflection (nazar saheeh). And in the hadith of Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Whoever you meet behind this wall, testifying that there is no deity but Allah, with his heart certain, then give him glad tidings of Paradise.' And in Sahih Muslim: 'Whoever dies while he knows that there is no deity but Allah enters Paradise.' So see how in these two hadiths, certainty ('ilm) and knowledge (yaqeen) are conditions, and they are opposites [to ignorance?]. And it is not valid to say: 'Assent (jazzm) for the sake of taqleed is knowledge' because if that assent were knowledge, then the coexistence of opposites would be necessary: in the assent of its occurrence through taqleed, and the assent of its pre-eternity likewise also, because knowledge is an attribute that does not admit of contradiction in any way. So it would necessitate that the person who knows is, in the same respect, both pre-eternal and temporal! And that is unintelligible. And these two hadiths explain all that is summarized from the hadiths of the two testimonies.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of taqleed (blind imitation) in the fundamentals of religion. It begins with a section heading declaring the nullification of the claim of taqleed in usul al-din. The author states that whoever Allah intends good for, He opens for him the knowledge of this science (the science of kalam), which is the best and most obligatory of sciences. Then he criticizes being content with taqleed as a low aspiration and a danger to one's religion. The reason is that faith requires certainty and knowledge, which can only be attained through sound reflection (nazar saheeh). To support this, he cites two hadiths: one from Abu Hurairah requiring certainty in the heart, and one from Muslim requiring knowledge. He then makes a logical argument: if one claims that assent (jazzm) due to taqleed is knowledge, then two contradictory assents could both be considered knowledge: for example, one person assents with certainty that the world is originated based on taqleed, and another assents with certainty that it is pre-eternal based on taqleed. Since knowledge cannot admit contradiction, this would require the person who knows to be both knowledgeable of its origination and its pre-eternity, which is impossible. Therefore, taqleed cannot be considered knowledge. Finally, he notes that these two hadiths explain all that has been summarized from the hadiths about the two testimonies (shahadatayn).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One may think that assenting to the truth based on the authority of scholars is sufficient for knowledge.
Correction: Sanusi shows that taqleed cannot produce the certainty required for true faith because it would allow contradictory certainties, which is impossible for knowledge.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi reject the claim that assent (jazzm) from taqleed is knowledge?
A) Because taqleed is forbidden in all matters.
B) Because it would allow contradictory certainties to coexist, which is impossible for knowledge.
C) Because the hadiths only require saying the shahada, not certainty.
D) Because taqleed is only for common people, not scholars.

Key Takeaway
Taqleed cannot generate the certainty required for true faith; only sound reflection (nazar) leads to genuine knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever examined the foundations of your own faith with the same seriousness Sanusi demands, or have you been content to simply follow what you were taught without question? What would it cost you to truly engage in nazar?
?
If your belief in Allah depends on the authority of a scholar or your parents rather than on your own certainty, would you be willing to stand before Him with that excuse?
?
The hadith requires certainty of heart for Paradise. Look at your own heart: is there any doubt, any area where you rely on 'taqleed' rather than personal conviction? How will you seek certainty starting today?

The Hadith of Jibril: The Objection and Its Refutation
Sanusi presents and refutes the objection from the Hadith of Jibril.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the flawed logic behind using the Hadith of Jibril to justify taqlid, and the correct interpretation that iman requires rational knowledge.

Core Idea
Iman requires knowledge, and knowledge requires nazar—taqlid falls short.

Sanusi begins by presenting a common but mistaken argument: some people claim that the famous hadith of Jibril shows that accepting beliefs by taqlid is sufficient for iman. They reason that since the Prophet simply listed the pillars without mentioning proofs, rational inquiry (nazar) cannot be a condition. However, Sanusi immediately declares this interpretation false and explains the proper understanding of the hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the first part where Sanusi presents the argument of those who rely on taqlid. Notice how they use the Prophet's silence on proofs as evidence.
The objection hinges on the assumption that if nazar were necessary, the Prophet would have mentioned proofs.
2
Understand the refutation
Sanusi states that this understanding is absolutely false. He then explains the meaning of the Prophet's words according to Ash'ari and others, showing that iman is knowledge or based on knowledge, which requires correct nazar.
3
Connect to the core idea
Reflect on why the necessity of nazar is derived from the same hadith. This shows that the objection fails because it misinterprets the Prophet's intent.
Iman and knowledge are intrinsically linked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وممَّا يَركنُ إليه في الاكتفاء بالتقليدِ بعضُ مَنْ لا بصيرة لهُ : الحديث الصحيحُ المشهورُ ؛ وهو حديث عبدِ اللهِ بنِ عمرَ عن رضي الله عنهما في سؤالِ جبريل عليه السلام النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلّمَ عنِ الإيمان والإسلام والإحسان (۱) ، في تفسيرِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ لها بما هو معروف مشهورٌ ، فيقولُ مَنْ لا بصيرة لهُ : دلَّ الحديث على أنَّ مَنْ حفظَ تلك الخصال المفسَّرَ بها الإيمان وفهمها واعتقدها ولو بالتقليد .. فهو مؤمن ؛ إذ لو كانَ حصولها بالنظر شرطاً في كونها إيماناً لَمَا اقتصر النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في تفسيرِ الإِيمَانِ على عدها دونَ ذكرِ أدلَّتِها . (( أن وهذا الأخذُ مِنَ الحديثِ باطل قطعاً ؛ لأنَّ قولَه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في شرح الإيمانِ : « أَنْ تُؤْمِنَ بِاللهِ . . . (۲) إلى آخرِهِ : معناه عند الشيخ الأشعري : أن تعرف ذلك ، وعند القاضي وغيرِهِ تُحدِّثَ نفْسَكَ بذلك حديثاً تابعاً للمعرفة(۳) ، وعلى كلا القولين فالمعرفة التي هي نفس الإيمان أو لازمةٌ له.. لا تحصل إلا بالنظر الصحيح ، وذلك يستلزم أنَّ الإيمان على القولين لا يحصل إلا بالنظر الصحيح وإنما لم يبين لهم النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أدلتها ؛ لأنَّها عقليَّةٌ ، لا تتوقَّفُ على بيان الشارع لها ، ولاكتفائه أيضاً بما في القرآنِ مِنَ الأدلَّةِ الكثيرة عليها ، وإنَّما بيَّنَ لهم صلّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ما لا يُعرَفُ إلا مِنَ الشرع ؛ وهو أنَّ معرفة هذه الخصالِ هي الإيمانُ الشرعي الذي يترتب عليه الدخول في الجنَّةِ وإن لم يوفِ بفروع الشريعةِ ، حتى يُؤخَذُ مِنْ تفسيره الإيمان بطلان مذهب المعتزلة في جعلهم الأعمال الواجبة جزءاً منه ، وأنَّ مَنْ لم يوفِ بها فليس بمؤمن ، ويُؤخَذُ منه أيضاً تكفيرهم ؛ لنقصهم خصلةٌ مِنْ خصال الإيمانِ ؛ وهي معرفةُ القَدَرِ ومن فوائدِ تفسيره صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّم للإيمان : أنَّ المكلف إذا عرف حقيقته بحث عن تحصيل هذه الحقيقة ومعرفتها بالنظر الصحيح ، أما إذا لم يعرف حقيقةَ الإيمانِ فقد يُحصِّلُ معرفة أشياءَ مِنَ الأجنبية عنه ؛ كعلم النجومِ والطب ونحوهما ، أو يحصل معرفة بعض خصالِ الإيمانِ فقط ، ويتوهَّمُ لجهلِهِ بحقيقةِ الإِيمَانِ أَنَّهُ قد حصل حقيقته ، وأنَّهُ مؤمن شرعاً ، وهو ليس كذلك ، وقس على هذه الفوائد ما يليقُ بكلام مَنْ أُوتِيَ جوامعَ الكَلِمِ وأمَّا فهُمُ صحَةِ التقليدِ مِنْ هذا الحديثِ فلا يخفى أَنَّهُ فهم ركيك في غاية ، ويدلُّكَ على غاية ركاكتِهِ زيادةً على ما سبق : أنَّ التقليد في هذه الخصال التي فُسِّرَ بها الإيمانُ باعتبار ثبوتِ مدلولها وصحته.
And among what some who have no insight rely upon for sufficiency with taqlid is the well-known authentic hadith; it is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, in the question of Jibril, peace be upon him, to the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, about iman, Islam, and ihsan (1), in his interpretation, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, of them by what is well known and famous. So one who has no insight says: The hadith indicates that whoever memorizes those characteristics by which iman is interpreted, understands them, and believes them, even if by taqlid, then he is a believer; for if their attainment through nazar were a condition for their being iman, the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, would not have confined himself in interpreting iman to enumerating them without mentioning their proofs. (This) and this taking from the hadith is absolutely false; because his statement, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in explaining iman: 'That you believe in Allah... (2) to its end,' its meaning according to al-Shaykh al-Ash'ari is that you know that, and according to al-Qadi and others is that you speak to yourself with that speech following knowledge (3), and on both sayings, knowledge which is itself iman or necessary for it is not obtained except by correct nazar. And that necessitates that iman on both sayings is not obtained except by correct nazar. And the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, only did not explain their proofs to them because they are rational, not dependent on the Lawgiver's explanation for them, and also because of his sufficiency with what is in the Quran of abundant proofs for them. Rather, he, peace be upon him, explained to them what is not known except from divine law: that knowledge of these characteristics is the legal iman by which entry into Paradise follows even if one does not fulfill the branches of the Law, so that from his interpretation of iman is taken the invalidity of the Mu'tazilite doctrine in making obligatory acts part of it, and that whoever does not fulfill them is not a believer, and also from it is taken their excommunication for their deficiency of one characteristic of the characteristics of iman, which is knowledge of predestination. And among the benefits of his interpretation, peace be upon him, of iman is that the morally responsible person, if he knows its reality, seeks to acquire this reality and know it by correct nazar. But if he does not know the reality of iman, he may acquire knowledge of things extraneous to it, such as the science of stars and medicine and the like, or he may acquire knowledge of some characteristics of iman only, and he deludes, due to his ignorance of the reality of iman, that he has attained its reality and that he is a believer legally, while he is not so. And analogize to these benefits what befits the speech of one who has been given the comprehensive expressions. As for their understanding the validity of taqlid from this hadith, it is not hidden that it is an extremely weak understanding, and what indicates to you the extreme weakness of it, in addition to what preceded, is that taqlid regarding these characteristics by which iman is interpreted is with respect to the establishment of their implications and their correctness.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (radd) of an objection. It begins by stating the objection: some people of little insight rely on the famous hadith of Jibril to argue that taqlid (uncritical acceptance) in matters of faith is sufficient. They argue that if nazar (rational inquiry) were necessary, the Prophet would have mentioned proofs when he explained iman. The author then refutes this objection (wa hadha al-akhdhu min al-hadithi batilun qat'an) by explaining the Prophet's silence on proofs: the proofs are rational (aqliyya), not dependent on revelation, and the Qur'an already contains abundant proofs. The Prophet only explained what is known exclusively from revelation—that these characteristics constitute saving faith. The author then draws several benefits: (1) refuting the Mu'tazila who make works part of iman, (2) excommunicating those who deny predestination, and (3) encouraging the seeker to pursue proper nazar. Finally, he stresses that the very idea of using the hadith to justify taqlid is extremely weak, since taqlid is about the truth of the propositions, not about their acceptance without understanding.

نظر
إيمان
معرفة
حديث جبريل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Hadith of Jibril shows that accepting beliefs by taqlid without rational inquiry is sufficient for iman.
Correction: The hadith actually defines iman as knowledge, which requires correct nazar; the Prophet's silence on proofs is because they are rational, not because nazar is unnecessary.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the meaning of the Prophet's statement 'That you believe in Allah...' according to al-Ash'ari?
A) That you do good deeds
B) That you know that
C) That you follow tradition
D) That you recite the shahada

Key Takeaway
The Hadith of Jibril does not support taqlid; it actually proves that iman requires knowledge obtained through rational inquiry.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When someone challenges your faith, do you feel confident that you can provide rational proofs, or do you rely on saying 'this is what I was taught'? How can you ensure your belief is grounded in knowledge, not just tradition?
?
If knowledge (ma'rifa) is necessary for iman, what concrete steps will you take today to move from taqlid to certainty? What is one belief you can start investigating rationally this week?

The Prophet's Wisdom and the Benefits of Understanding Iman Correctly
Sanusi explains the wisdom behind the Prophet's omission of proofs and lists the benefits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet did not mention the proofs of iman, and the important theological benefits derived from his explanation.

Core Idea
The Prophet revealed what only revelation can tell us: the content of saving faith.

Having refuted the objection, Sanusi now explains why the Prophet omitted the proofs: they are rational, not dependent on revelation, and are already abundantly present in the Quran. The Prophet's role was to define what constitutes legal iman, not to provide the arguments for it. This yields several crucial benefits, including the refutation of the Mu'tazila and the importance of seeking correct nazar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the reason for silence
Read the part where Sanusi explains that the proofs are rational and already in the Quran. This shows why the Prophet did not need to mention them.
Rational proofs do not depend on the Lawgiver's explanation.
2
Learn the benefits of interpretation
Note the three benefits: refutation of Mu'tazila, excommunication of those who deny predestination, and encouragement to seek nazar.
These benefits show the depth of the Prophetic teaching.
3
Understand the weakness of taqlid
Sanusi concludes that understanding taqlid from the hadith is extremely weak, especially since taqlid concerns the truth of propositions, not mere acceptance.

The Logical Impossibility of Taqlid in Belief
Sanusi presents a logical proof against taqlid in foundational beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why taqlid (blind imitation) is logically impossible for foundational beliefs, as Sanusi demonstrates through a circularity argument.

Core Idea
Taqlid in foundational beliefs leads to a logical circle.

Sanusi presents a crisp logical proof that taqlid cannot be the basis for the foundational truths of faith. Even if one were to imitate the highest authority—the Prophet—that imitation would depend on already knowing that he is truly a messenger, which in turn requires knowledge of God and His attributes. This sets up a circular dependency that makes taqlid impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get the argument's flow. Note the key terms: taqlid, prophethood, miracle, circularity.
2
Trace the dependency chain
Identify the sequence: taqlid depends on knowing prophethood; prophethood depends on a miracle; a miracle depends on knowing God and His attributes.
The dependency is a chain that loops back on itself.
3
Recognize the circularity
See that if knowledge of God depends on prophethood, and knowledge of prophethood depends on knowing God, we have a circle. This is what Sanusi calls 'al-dawr'.
Circular reasoning is logically invalid.
4
Understand the conclusion
Sanusi concludes that taqlid cannot be the basis for foundational beliefs. Instead, rational proof is necessary.
This is a fundamental principle in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أعلى مَنْ يُقلِّدُ في ثبوتها - لو صح التقليد - النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ وسائر الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، ولا شك أنَّ تقليدهم فيها فرعُ ثبوت رسالتهم ، وهي لا تثبتُ إلا بالمعجزة المتوقفِ معرفةُ دلالتِها على معرفة وجودِهِ تعالى ومعرفة صفاته التي يدخل فيها معرفةً القدر (وإنما دخل القدر في صفاته تعالى؛ لأنه يرجع للعلم والإرادة. « صفاقسي ») فإذاً ؛ لو توقَّفَتْ معرفةُ خصالِ الإيمانِ ـ مِنْ حيثُ ثبوتُها ، لا مِنْ حيثُ إنَّها تفسير للإيمانِ الشرعي - على قول الرسولِ .. لَلزِمَ الدورُ وتوقف الشيء على نفسه .
The highest one to imitate in establishing them — if imitation (taqlid) were valid — is the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, and all the messengers, peace be upon them. There is no doubt that imitating them in these matters is a branch of the establishment of their prophethood, and their prophethood is only established by a miracle (mu'jizah), the knowledge of whose indication depends on knowledge of His existence, may He be exalted, and knowledge of His attributes, which includes knowledge of al-qadar (divine decree). (And qadar is included among His attributes only because it returns to knowledge and will — al-Sfaqsi.) Therefore, if knowledge of the qualities of faith — in terms of their establishment, not in terms of their being an interpretation of legal faith — were dependent on the statement of the Messenger, then circularity (al-dawr) would result, and the thing would depend on itself.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage presents a logical proof (burhan) against the validity of taqlid (blind imitation) in matters of belief. Sanusi begins by identifying the highest authority one might imitate—the Prophet and all messengers. Even if taqlid were generally permissible, the problem is that imitating a messenger in these foundational beliefs presupposes that we already know that the messenger is truly a messenger. But establishing prophethood requires a miracle (mu'jizah), and to recognize a miracle as a sign of truthfulness, we must first know that God exists and know His attributes (since a miracle is a divine act). Among those attributes is qadar (divine decree), which relates to God's knowledge and will, as the commentator notes. So we have a circular dependency: to know God we need prophethood, but to know prophethood we need to know God. Therefore, if knowledge of the articles of faith (khisal al-iman) — specifically their being true, not their legal definition — relied solely on the Prophet's statement, it would lead to circular reasoning (al-dawr), meaning a thing depending on itself, which is impossible. Thus, taqlid cannot be the basis for foundational theological knowledge; rational proof is necessary.

Key Terms
تقليد
ثبوت الرسالة
المعجزة
الدور
صفات الله
القدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think taqlid is acceptable in all religious matters, including foundational beliefs.
Correction: Sanusi shows that taqlid in foundational beliefs leads to logical circularity, making it impossible. Rational proof is necessary.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's argument, why would making faith based on taqlid of the Prophet lead to circularity?
A) Because establishing prophethood depends on prior knowledge of God, and knowledge of God depends on prophethood.
B) Because the Prophet forbade taqlid.
C) Because miracles are not reliable.
D) Because faith is a personal matter.

Key Takeaway
Taqlid cannot be the basis for foundational beliefs because it leads to circular reasoning; rational proof must be used.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about God solely because you were taught it, without ever asking yourself if it could be rationally justified? What would it mean for your faith if that belief were based on imitation?
?
If even the Prophet's authority depends on rational proof of God's existence, then where does your own certainty come from? Are you willing to examine the foundations of your faith with the same rigor Sanusi demands?
?
Think of a core belief you hold about Allah. Can you articulate a rational proof for it without appealing to any authority? If not, what step will you take today to move from taqlid to certainty?

Knowledge of Allah is the Best Deed
Hadith on the virtue of knowledge of Allah over action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet (peace be upon him) considered knowledge of Allah superior to action, and how a little action with knowledge outweighs much action without it.

Core Idea
Knowledge of Allah is the foundation that gives all actions their value.

The first proof Sanusi presents is a hadith where the Prophet declares knowledge of Allah as the most virtuous deed. When questioned, he explains that even a small deed done with knowledge of Allah is more beneficial than many deeds done without it. This sets the priority of tawhid over all religious actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and translation
Read the full hadith where the Prophet is asked about the best deed. Notice the surprise of the questioner when the Prophet answers with knowledge instead of action.
The questioner expected a deed like prayer or charity.
2
Understand the Prophet's explanation
Reflect on the Prophet's statement: 'A little action benefits with knowledge of Allah, and much action does not benefit with ignorance of Allah.' Why does knowledge make such a difference?
Knowledge of Allah gives intention and sincerity its correct orientation.
3
Connect to tawhid
Recognize that 'knowledge of Allah' here means knowledge of His essence, attributes, and actions – the core of ilm al-tawhid. This hadith establishes its supreme rank among all sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1 بعضُ الآثارِ والأخبارِ الدالة على شرفِ علم التوحيدِ ] ومما يدلُّ على شرف هذا العلم وعظيم فضلِهِ : ما رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ قيلَ : يا رسولَ اللهِ ؛ أَيُّ الأعمالِ أَفَضلُ ؟ قالَ : « الْعِلْمُ بِاللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ » ، فقيل : يا رسولَ اللهِ ؛ نسألُكَ عنِ العمل ، فتجيب عنِ العلم ؟! فقالَ : « إِنَّ قَلِيلَ الْعَمَلِ يَنْفَعُ مَعَ الْعِلْمِ بِاللَّهِ ، وَإِنَّ كَثِيرَ الْعَمَلِ لا يَنْفَعُ مَعَ الْجَهْلِ بِاللهِ (۲) (رواه ابن عبد البر في جامع بيان العلم وفضله) ( ٢١٤ ) من حديث سيدنا أنس رضي الله عنه ، والقضاعي في « مسند الشهاب » ( ١٠١٥ ) من حديث سیدنا ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه) ورُوِيَ عنه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : أَنَّهُ أتاه رجلٌ فقال له : يا نبي الله ؛ علمْني مِنْ غرائب العلم ، فقال : « مَا فَعَلْتَ فِي رَأْس الْعِلْمِ حَتَّى تَطْلُبَ غَرَائِبَهُ ؟ » ، قال : وما رأسُ العلم يا نبي الله ؟ قالَ : ( أَعَرَفْتَ الرَّبِّ ؟ » ، قال : نعم ، قال : « فَمَا فَعَلْتَ فِي حَفِّهِ عَلَيْكَ ؟ » ، قال : ما شاءَ اللهُ ،  َقالَ : ( أَعَرَفْتَ الْمَوْتَ ؟ » ، قال : نعم ، قال : « فَمَا أَعْدَدْتَ لَهُ ؟ » ، قال : ما شاء الله ، فقال : انْطَلِقْ وَأَحْكِمْ مَا هَا هُنَا ، فَإِذَا أَحْكَمْتَ فَتَعَالَ أُعَلِّمْكَ مِنْ غَرَائِبٍ الْعِلْمِ (۱) (رواه الجوهري في « مسند الموطأ » ( ۱۰ ) ، وابن عبد البر في «جامع بيان العلم وفضله » ( ۱۲۲۲ ) من حديث عبد الله بن المسور رحمه الله تعالى مرسلاً .) ورُوِيَ في الخبرِ : أَنَّ الله تعالى أوحى إلى داود عليه السلام : يا داود ؛ تعلَّم العلم النافع ، قالَ : يَا رَبِّ ، وما العلم النافع ؟ قال : أن تعرف جلالي وعظمتي وكبريائي وكمال قدرتي على كلِّ شيءٍ ، فإِنَّ هذا هو العلم النافع الذي يُقرِّبُكَ إِليَّ (٢) (أورده حجة الإسلام الغزالي في « منهاج العابدين » ( ص ٥١ )، وقد نصح فقال : ( وليكن الطلب طلب دراية ، لا طلب رواية ، واعلم أن الخطر عظيم ، فمن طلب العلم ليصرف به وجوه الناس إليه ، ويجالس به الأمراء ويباهي به النظراء ، ويتصيد به الحكام .. فتجارته بائرة ، وصفقته خاسرة )) وفي القرآن العظيم : إِنَّمَا يَخْشَى اللَّهَ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ الْعُلَمُوا ) (فاطر : ٢٨]
1 Some of the traditions and reports indicating the honor of the science of tawhid: Among what indicates the honor of this science and its great merit is what has been narrated that it was said: O Messenger of God, which deed is most virtuous? He said: ‘Knowledge of God, Almighty and Majestic.’ It was said: O Messenger of God, we ask you about action, and you answer about knowledge?! He said: ‘Indeed, a little action benefits with knowledge of God, and indeed, much action does not benefit with ignorance of God.’ (Reported by Ibn Abd al-Barr in Jami' Bayan al-Ilm wa Fadlihi, 214, from the hadith of our master Anas, may God be pleased with him, and by al-Quda'i in Musnad al-Shihab, 1015, from the hadith of our master Ibn Mas'ud, may God be pleased with him.) And it has been narrated from him, may God bless him and grant him peace, that a man came to him and said: O Prophet of God, teach me from the rare types of knowledge. He said: ‘What have you done with the head of knowledge that you seek its rarities?’ He said: What is the head of knowledge, O Prophet of God? He said: ‘Do you know the Lord?’ He said: Yes. He said: ‘What have you done regarding His right upon you?’ He said: As God wills. He said: ‘Do you know death?’ He said: Yes. He said: ‘What have you prepared for it?’ He said: As God wills. He said: ‘Go and master what is here, and when you have mastered it, then come and I will teach you from the rare types of knowledge.’ (Reported by al-Jawhari in Musnad al-Muwatta, 10, and by Ibn Abd al-Barr in Jami' Bayan al-Ilm wa Fadlihi, 1222, from the hadith of Abdullah ibn al-Musawwar, may God have mercy on him, as a mursal report.) And it has been narrated in the report that God Almighty revealed to David, peace be upon him: O David, learn beneficial knowledge. He said: O Lord, what is beneficial knowledge? He said: That you know My majesty, My greatness, My pride, and the perfection of My power over everything. For this is the beneficial knowledge that brings you near to Me. (Mentioned by the Proof of Islam al-Ghazali in Minhaj al-Abidin, p. 51, and he advised, saying: Let the seeking be seeking of understanding, not seeking of transmission. And know that the danger is great. Whoever seeks knowledge to turn people's faces towards him, to sit with princes, to boast to peers, and to hunt for rulers... his trade is in ruin and his bargain is a loss.)) And in the Mighty Quran: ‘Only those among His servants who are knowledgeable fear God’ [Fatir: 28].
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage collects transmitted proofs (adillah naqliyyah) for the honor and virtue of ilm al-tawhid (knowledge of divine unity). It begins with a subheading indicating that these are some of the traditions (athar) and reports (akhbar) indicating the honor of this science. The first proof is a famous hadith: someone asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about the best deed, and he answered 'knowledge of Allah'. When asked why he answered about knowledge instead of action, he explained that a little action benefits with knowledge of God, but much action does not benefit with ignorance. This establishes the priority of knowledge of God over all actions. The second hadith involves a man asking the Prophet to teach him rare knowledge; the Prophet first asks about the 'head of knowledge' — which is knowing the Lord, and also knowing death and preparing for it. Only after mastering these fundamentals should one seek rare knowledge. This shows that ma'rifat al-Rabb (knowledge of the Lord) is the foundation. The third report is a divine revelation to Prophet David (peace be upon him) about beneficial knowledge: it is knowledge of God's majesty, greatness, pride, and perfect power. This knowledge draws one closer to God. A note from al-Ghazali warns against seeking such knowledge for worldly purposes. Finally, the Quranic verse (Fatir: 28) states that only the knowledgeable (al-'ulama) truly fear God, linking knowledge of Him with reverential fear (khashyah). Together, these texts argue for the supreme value and necessity of learning tawhid.

Key Terms
العلم بالله
معرفة الله
فضل العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that outward deeds like prayer and charity are more important than knowledge.
Correction: This hadith shows that knowledge of Allah is the root; deeds branch from it. Without knowledge, deeds lose their value.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in this lesson, why does a little action benefit with knowledge of Allah?
A) Because knowledge itself is a deed
B) Because knowledge ensures deeds are done with sincerity and correctness
C) Because deeds are not required if one has knowledge
D) Because the Prophet preferred knowledge over action

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of Allah is the most virtuous pursuit because it gives all other actions their worth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you first ensure it is built on knowledge of Allah? If not, what is one thing you will learn about Allah this week to transform your next action?
?
Think of a small deed you did today—did it arise from a conscious connection to Allah, or was it routine? How would the deed feel different if you had just studied a name of Allah before doing it?
?
The Prophet said that much action without knowledge of Allah is useless. Is there an area in your life where you are 'doing a lot' but have not sought knowledge of Allah about it? What step will you take today to replace ignorance with knowledge?

The Head of Knowledge: Knowing Your Lord
Hadith on the priority of fundamental knowledge over rare knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet described knowledge of the Lord (ma'rifat al-Rabb) as the 'head of knowledge' and the foundation before seeking other types of knowledge.

Core Idea
Mastering the knowledge of Allah comes before every other branch of learning.

The second hadith presents a man asking the Prophet for 'rare knowledge' (ghara'ib al-ilm). The Prophet redirects him to the 'head of knowledge' – knowing your Lord and preparing for death. This underscores that tawhid is the essential starting point, and only after mastering it can one delve into deeper or more specialized topics.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Notice the man's request for 'rare types of knowledge' and the Prophet's response. Identify what the Prophet calls the 'head of knowledge'.
The man thought rare knowledge was something advanced, but the Prophet went to the basics.
2
Understand the Prophet's questions
The Prophet asks: 'Do you know the Lord?' and 'Do you know death?' These are not optional; they are foundational. Reflect on how these two questions cover the essence of tawhid and accountability.
Knowing death and preparing for it is also part of beneficial knowledge.
3
Apply the lesson
Consider how this hadith prioritizes learning tawhid over all other Islamic sciences. Before studying fiqh, hadith, or spirituality, the first priority is to know Allah properly.
This is a reminder to many students today who jump into specialized topics without solidifying their aqidah.

D) Knowledge of the Prophet's biography

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of Allah and reflection on death are the foundations of all beneficial knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the Prophet asked, 'What have you done regarding His right upon you?' Stop and think: What specific right of Allah have you been neglecting today? What is one concrete action you will take to fulfill it before this day ends?
?
The Prophet asked about preparation for death. Are you truly prepared to meet your Lord? If not, what is one real step you will take today—not tomorrow—to begin that preparation?
?
You now know that knowing your Lord is the head of knowledge. Does your daily life reflect that priority? If your heart and time are filled with other pursuits, what will you remove to make room for this foundational knowledge?

Beneficial Knowledge: Knowing Allah's Attributes
Divine revelation and Quranic verse on beneficial knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that beneficial knowledge is knowledge of Allah's majesty, greatness, and power, and that such knowledge leads to true fear of Him.

Core Idea
Knowledge that draws you closer to Allah is knowledge of His attributes and reverential fear.

The next proof is a divine revelation to Prophet David (peace be upon him) defining 'beneficial knowledge' as knowledge of Allah's majesty, greatness, and perfect power. This is followed by a Quranic verse stating that only the knowledgeable truly fear Allah. Together, they ground the study of tawhid in both divine command and scriptural authority, showing that this knowledge is not merely theoretical but leads to spiritual transformation.

Guided Path
1
Read the revelation to Dawud
Read how Allah defines beneficial knowledge: knowing His jalal (majesty), azamah (greatness), kibrīya' (pride), and perfect power. Notice the emphasis on knowing Allah's attributes.
These attributes are central to tawhid.
2
Reflect on the purpose of this knowledge
The revelation says this knowledge 'brings you near to Me.' Consider how knowledge of Allah's greatness instills humility and draws the heart closer to Him.
Knowledge without implementation is not truly beneficial.
3
Connect to the Quranic verse
Read the verse from Surah Fatir: 'Only those among His servants who are knowledgeable fear Allah.' This shows that true knowledge produces khashyah (reverential fear), which is the fruit of ilm al-tawhid.
Fear here is not terror but awe and reverence.

1 بعضُ الآثارِ والأخبارِ الدالة على شرفِ علم التوحيدِ ] ومما يدلُّ على شرف هذا العلم وعظيم فضلِهِ : ما رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ قيلَ : يا رسولَ اللهِ ؛ أَيُّ الأعمالِ أَفَضلُ ؟ قالَ : « الْعِلْمُ بِاللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ » ، فقيل : يا رسولَ اللهِ ؛ نسألُكَ عنِ العمل ، فتجيب عنِ العلم ؟! فقالَ : « إِنَّ قَلِيلَ الْعَمَلِ يَنْفَعُ مَعَ الْعِلْمِ بِاللَّهِ ، وَإِنَّ كَثِيرَ الْعَمَلِ لا يَنْفَعُ مَعَ الْجَهْلِ بِاللهِ (۲) (رواه ابن عبد البر في جامع بيان العلم وفضله) ( ٢١٤ ) من حديث سيدنا أنس رضي الله عنه ، والقضاعي في « مسند الشهاب » ( ١٠١٥ ) من حديث سیدنا ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه) ورُوِيَ عنه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : أَنَّهُ أتاه رجلٌ فقال له : يا نبي الله ؛ علمْني مِنْ غرائب العلم ، فقال : « مَا فَعَلْتَ فِي رَأْس الْعِلْمِ حَتَّى تَطْلُبَ غَرَائِبَهُ ؟ » ، قال : وما رأسُ العلم يا نبي الله ؟ قالَ : ( أَعَرَفْتَ الرَّبِّ ؟ » ، قال : نعم ، قال : « فَمَا فَعَلْتَ فِي حَفِّهِ عَلَيْكَ ؟ » ، قال : ما شاءَ اللهُ ،  َقالَ : ( أَعَرَفْتَ الْمَوْتَ ؟ » ، قال : نعم ، قال : « فَمَا أَعْدَدْتَ لَهُ ؟ » ، قال : ما شاء الله ، فقال : انْطَلِقْ وَأَحْكِمْ مَا هَا هُنَا ، فَإِذَا أَحْكَمْتَ فَتَعَالَ أُعَلِّمْكَ مِنْ غَرَائِبٍ الْعِلْمِ (۱) (رواه الجوهري في « مسند الموطأ » ( ۱۰ ) ، وابن عبد البر في «جامع بيان العلم وفضله » ( ۱۲۲۲ ) من حديث عبد الله بن المسور رحمه الله تعالى مرسلاً .) ورُوِيَ في الخبرِ : أَنَّ الله تعالى أوحى إلى داود عليه السلام : يا داود ؛ تعلَّم العلم النافع ، قالَ : يَا رَبِّ ، وما العلم النافع ؟ قال : أن تعرف جلالي وعظمتي وكبريائي وكمال قدرتي على كلِّ شيءٍ ، فإِنَّ هذا هو العلم النافع الذي يُقرِّبُكَ إِليَّ (٢) (أورده حجة الإسلام الغزالي في « منهاج العابدين » ( ص ٥١ )، وقد نصح فقال : ( وليكن الطلب طلب دراية ، لا طلب رواية ، واعلم أن الخطر عظيم ، فمن طلب العلم ليصرف به وجوه الناس إليه ، ويجالس به الأمراء ويباهي به النظراء ، ويتصيد به الحكام .. فتجارته بائرة ، وصفقته خاسرة )) وفي القرآن العظيم : إِنَّمَا يَخْشَى اللَّهَ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ الْعُلَمُوا ) (فاطر : ٢٨]
1 Some of the traditions and reports indicating the honor of the science of tawhid: Among what indicates the honor of this science and its great merit is what has been narrated that it was said: O Messenger of God, which deed is most virtuous? He said: ‘Knowledge of God, Almighty and Majestic.’ It was said: O Messenger of God, we ask you about action, and you answer about knowledge?! He said: ‘Indeed, a little action benefits with knowledge of God, and indeed, much action does not benefit with ignorance of God.’ (Reported by Ibn Abd al-Barr in Jami' Bayan al-Ilm wa Fadlihi, 214, from the hadith of our master Anas, may God be pleased with him, and by al-Quda'i in Musnad al-Shihab, 1015, from the hadith of our master Ibn Mas'ud, may God be pleased with him.) And it has been narrated from him, may God bless him and grant him peace, that a man came to him and said: O Prophet of God, teach me from the rare types of knowledge. He said: ‘What have you done with the head of knowledge that you seek its rarities?’ He said: What is the head of knowledge, O Prophet of God? He said: ‘Do you know the Lord?’ He said: Yes. He said: ‘What have you done regarding His right upon you?’ He said: As God wills. He said: ‘Do you know death?’ He said: Yes. He said: ‘What have you prepared for it?’ He said: As God wills. He said: ‘Go and master what is here, and when you have mastered it, then come and I will teach you from the rare types of knowledge.’ (Reported by al-Jawhari in Musnad al-Muwatta, 10, and by Ibn Abd al-Barr in Jami' Bayan al-Ilm wa Fadlihi, 1222, from the hadith of Abdullah ibn al-Musawwar, may God have mercy on him, as a mursal report.) And it has been narrated in the report that God Almighty revealed to David, peace be upon him: O David, learn beneficial knowledge. He said: O Lord, what is beneficial knowledge? He said: That you know My majesty, My greatness, My pride, and the perfection of My power over everything. For this is the beneficial knowledge that brings you near to Me. (Mentioned by the Proof of Islam al-Ghazali in Minhaj al-Abidin, p. 51, and he advised, saying: Let the seeking be seeking of understanding, not seeking of transmission. And know that the danger is great. Whoever seeks knowledge to turn people's faces towards him, to sit with princes, to boast to peers, and to hunt for rulers... his trade is in ruin and his bargain is a loss.)) And in the Mighty Quran: ‘Only those among His servants who are knowledgeable fear God’ [Fatir: 28].
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage collects transmitted proofs (adillah naqliyyah) for the honor and virtue of ilm al-tawhid (knowledge of divine unity). It begins with a subheading indicating that these are some of the traditions (athar) and reports (akhbar) indicating the honor of this science. The first proof is a famous hadith: someone asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about the best deed, and he answered 'knowledge of Allah'. When asked why he answered about knowledge instead of action, he explained that a little action benefits with knowledge of God, but much action does not benefit with ignorance. This establishes the priority of knowledge of God over all actions. The second hadith involves a man asking the Prophet to teach him rare knowledge; the Prophet first asks about the 'head of knowledge' — which is knowing the Lord, and also knowing death and preparing for it. Only after mastering these fundamentals should one seek rare knowledge. This shows that ma'rifat al-Rabb (knowledge of the Lord) is the foundation. The third report is a divine revelation to Prophet David (peace be upon him) about beneficial knowledge: it is knowledge of God's majesty, greatness, pride, and perfect power. This knowledge draws one closer to God. A note from al-Ghazali warns against seeking such knowledge for worldly purposes. Finally, the Quranic verse (Fatir: 28) states that only the knowledgeable (al-'ulama) truly fear God, linking knowledge of Him with reverential fear (khashyah). Together, these texts argue for the supreme value and necessity of learning tawhid.

جلال الله
عظمة الله
كبرياء الله
القدرة
خشية الله

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think beneficial knowledge is only practical knowledge that helps in daily life, or merely memorising facts.
Correction: The revelation and verse show that beneficial knowledge is specifically knowledge of Allah's attributes, leading to awe and closeness to Him.

Checkpoint

B) Knowledge of Allah's majesty, greatness, pride, and perfect power
C) Knowledge of history and previous nations
D) Knowledge of the self

Key Takeaway
Beneficial knowledge that draws you closer to Allah is the knowledge of His attributes, leading to reverential fear.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn about Allah's names and attributes, does your heart tremble with awe, or is it merely intellectual information? What would it take for your knowledge to transform into genuine khashyah?
?
How much time each week do you intentionally devote to studying Allah's attributes compared to other subjects? Does your schedule reflect that this is the most beneficial knowledge?
?
If you were to stand before Allah today, could you honestly say that your knowledge of Him has made you a different person — more fearful, more loving, more obedient? If not, what is the barrier in your heart that you need to remove?

The Head of Knowledge is Knowledge of Allah
The Prophet and divine revelation define the head and benefit of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that knowledge of Allah is the foundation and most beneficial knowledge, as taught by the Prophet and revealed to Prophet Dawud.

Core Idea
Knowing Allah is the head of all knowledge.

This lesson presents two sacred narrations that establish the primacy of knowing Allah. A man asked the Prophet for esoteric knowledge, but the Prophet redirected him to the basics: first know your Lord and prepare for death. Then, a divine revelation to Dawud defines beneficial knowledge as knowledge of Allah's majesty and power. Together, they teach that the most important knowledge is ma'rifat Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the two narrations
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the structure: the first is a dialogue with the Prophet, the second is a divine revelation to Dawud.
The passage combines a prophetic hadith and a holy hadith (hadith qudsi).
2
Identify the 'head of knowledge'
Find where the Prophet defines the 'head of knowledge' (ra's al-'ilm). What does he point to?
He asks 'Have you known the Lord?' – this shows the head of knowledge is knowing Allah.
3
Define beneficial knowledge
In the second narration, what does Allah tell Dawud is 'beneficial knowledge' (al-'ilm al-nafi')? List the attributes mentioned.
Beneficial knowledge is knowing Allah's majesty, greatness, pride, and complete power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروي عنه صلى الله عليه وسلم: أنه أتاه رجل فقال له: يا نبي الله، علمني من غرائب العلم، فقال: «ما فعلت في رأس العلم حتى تطلب غرائبه؟»، قال: وما رأس العلم يا نبي الله؟ قال: «أعرفت الرب؟»، قال: نعم، قال: «فما فعلت في حقه عليك؟»، قال: ما شاء الله، قال: «أعرفت الموت؟»، قال: نعم، قال: «فما أعددت له؟»، قال: ما شاء الله، فقال: «انطلق وأحكم ما ها هنا، فإذا أحكمت فتعال أعلمك من غرائب العلم». وروي في الخبر: أن الله تعالى أوحى إلى داود عليه السلام: يا داود، تعلم العلم النافع، قال: يا رب، وما العلم النافع؟ قال: أن تعرف جلالي وعظمتي وكبريائي وكمال قدرتي على كل شيء، فإن هذا هو العلم النافع الذي يقربك إلي.
And it was narrated from him (peace be upon him) that a man came to him and said: O Prophet of Allah, teach me some of the strange knowledge. He said: 'What have you done with the head of knowledge that you seek its strange aspects?' He said: What is the head of knowledge, O Prophet of Allah? He said: 'Have you known the Lord?' He said: Yes. He said: 'Then what have you done regarding His right upon you?' He said: Whatever Allah wills. He said: 'Have you known death?' He said: Yes. He said: 'Then what have you prepared for it?' He said: Whatever Allah wills. He said: 'Go and master what is here, and when you have mastered it, then come and I will teach you from the strange knowledge.' And it was narrated in the report that Allah Almighty revealed to Dawud (peace be upon him): O Dawud, learn beneficial knowledge. He said: O my Lord, what is beneficial knowledge? He said: That you know My majesty, greatness, pride, and complete power over everything, for this is the beneficial knowledge that brings you near to Me.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a narration of two hadiths: the first from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the second from a divine revelation to Prophet Dawud (peace be upon him). The first hadith establishes that knowing Allah ('the Lord') is the 'head of knowledge' (ra's al-'ilm), meaning the foundation and most important part. A man asked for 'strange' or esoteric knowledge, but the Prophet redirected him to the fundamentals: first, ensure you know your Lord and fulfill His rights, and know death and prepare for it. Only after mastering these basics should one seek deeper knowledge. The second hadith identifies beneficial knowledge (al-'ilm al-nafi') as knowledge of Allah's majesty, greatness, pride, and complete power. This knowledge is what brings a person close to Allah. Together, these narrations emphasize that the primary and most beneficial knowledge is knowledge of Allah and His attributes.

Key Terms
رأس العلم (ra's al-'ilm): head of knowledge
غرائب العلم (ghara'ib al-'ilm): strange/esoteric knowledge
العلم النافع (al-'ilm al-nafi'): beneficial knowledge

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that esoteric or miraculous knowledge is the highest form of knowledge.
Correction: The Prophet teaches that foundational knowledge of Allah (ma'rifat Allah) is the 'head of knowledge' and the most important, while esoteric knowledge comes after mastering the basics.

Checkpoint
What does the Prophet identify as the 'head of knowledge' (ra's al-'ilm)?
A) The science of the Hereafter
B) Knowledge of the Lord (ma'rifat al-Rabb)
C) Knowledge of death
D) Knowledge of beneficial trades

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of Allah is the head and most beneficial knowledge; it is the foundation upon which all other knowledge should be built.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that knowledge of Allah is the head of all knowledge. But what have you actually done today to increase that knowledge? Have you studied His names and attributes, or have you been distracted by other types of knowledge? How will you change your priorities starting now?
?
The Prophet asked the man: 'What have you done regarding His right upon you?' Be honest: when you say you believe in Allah, what rights of His have you been neglecting? What specific act of worship or obedience will you commit to tomorrow to start fulfilling that right?
?
You know you will die, and you claim to have prepared. But the man in the hadith said 'Whatever Allah wills' — a vague answer. The Prophet sent him back to master the fundamentals. What does your preparation for death look like? Is it a vague hope, or is it concrete action? Write down one thing you will do this week to prepare for your meeting with Allah.

The Knowledge That Necessitates Khashyah and Ibrahim's Proof
Sanusi defines knowledge that necessitates khashyah and cites Ibrahim's proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the knowledge which necessarily produces fear of Allah is specifically knowledge of Allah Himself, and that rational theology (kalam) is the path of the prophets and the Imams of Sunnah.

Core Idea
True khashyah comes only from knowing Allah through rational proofs.

Sanusi begins by clarifying a key point: not all religious knowledge produces fear of Allah. The knowledge that does is knowledge of Allah's essence and attributes. He then anchors this in the Qur'anic story of Prophet Ibrahim, whose rational argument for creation's temporality was honored by Allah. This passage establishes that rational theology (kalam) is not only legitimate but the very means to the highest spiritual stations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses Qur'anic evidence to support his claim.
2
Identify the specific knowledge that necessitates khashyah
The passage begins by defining which knowledge entails khashyah. Find the exact phrase and note that it is exclusively knowledge of Allah.
3
Understand Ibrahim's proof
The passage summarizes Ibrahim's argument: the world undergoes changes, so it must have a creator who is unchanging. See how this rational proof is presented as a divine argument.
4
Observe the divine command and its followership
Allah commands following Ibrahim's way (millah). The Imams of Sunnah are praised for doing so. Reflect on the connection between rational theology and high spiritual rank.
This step ties the lesson together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَعْلُومٌ أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِالْعِلْمِ الَّذِي يَسْتَلْزِمُ الْخَشْيَةَ إِنَّمَا هُوَ الْعِلْمُ بِاللهِ تَعَالَى . وَقَالَ تَعَالَى بَعْدَ اسْتِدْلَالِ خَلِيلِهِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ عَلَى نَبِيِّنَا وَعَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ عَلَى حُدُوثِ الْعَالَمِ بِمُلَازَمَتِهِ التَّغَيُّرَاتِ ، وَأَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ لِجَمِيعِهِ مِنْ مُخْتَرِعٍ وَمُدَبِّرٍ لَهُ لَا يَتَغَيَّرُ وَلَا تَحُلُّ بِهِ الْحَوَادِثُ : ﴿ وَتِلْكَ حُجَّتُنَا آتَيْنَهَا إِبْرَاهِيمَ عَلَى قَوْمِهِ نَرْفَعُ دَرَجَاتٍ مَّن نَّشَاءُ ﴾ [الأنعام : ٨٣] ، فَأَضَافَ تَعَالَى تِلْكَ الْحُجَّةَ إِلَى نَفْسِهِ إِضَافَةَ تَشْرِيفٍ ، وَحَكَمَ بِرَفْعِ دَرَجَاتِ مَنْ فَتَحَ لَهُ فِي مَعْرِفَةِ الْحَقِّ بِبَرَاهِينِهِ الْعَقْلِيَّةِ ، وَقَدْ أَمَرَنَا جَلَّ وَعَلَا بِالِاقْتِدَاءِ بِخَلِيلِهِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ فِي قَوْلِهِ : ( مِلَّةَ أَبِيكُمْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ ) [الحج : ٧] ، وَقَالَ : ﴿ ثُمَّ أَوْحَيْنَا إِلَيْكَ أَنِ اتَّبِعْ مِلَّةَ إِبْرَاهِيمَ حَنِيفًا ﴾ [النحل : ١٢٣] . وَلَا شَكَّ أَنَّ أَئِمَّةَ السُّنَّةِ رَضِيَ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُمْ هُمُ الَّذِينَ اقْتَدَوْا بِهَذَا الْأَمْرِ ، وَفَازُوا بِرَفْعِ الدَّرَجَاتِ وَنَيْلِ أَعْلَى الْمَرَاتِبِ عِنْدَ اللهِ تَعَالَى جَعَلَنَا اللهُ مِنْهُمْ دُنْيَا وَأُخْرَى
And it is known that the intended meaning of the knowledge that entails khashyah (fear of Allah) is only knowledge of Allah, the Exalted. And Allah the Exalted said after the reasoning of His intimate friend Ibrahim, may salat and peace be upon our Prophet and upon him, for the temporality of the world by its being subject to changes, and that all of it must have an inventor and manager who does not change and in whom events do not occur: {And that was Our argument which We gave to Ibrahim against his people. We raise in degrees whom We will} [al-An'am 6:83]. So Allah the Exalted attributed that argument to Himself as an attribution of honor, and decreed the raising of degrees for whomever He opens the way to knowledge of the truth through His rational proofs. And He, Glorified and Exalted, commanded us to follow His intimate friend Ibrahim, peace and salat be upon him, in His saying: (The religion of your father Ibrahim) [al-Hajj 22:7], and He said: {Then We inspired you to follow the religion of Ibrahim, upright} [an-Nahl 16:123]. And there is no doubt that the Imams of the Sunnah, may Allah be pleased with them, are the ones who followed this command, and succeeded in attaining elevation of degrees and reaching the highest stations with Allah the Exalted. May Allah make us among them in this world and the next.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is an argument for the superiority of knowledge of Allah (ilm al-kalam) over other forms of knowledge. It begins by stating the well-known point that the knowledge which necessarily produces khashyah (fear of Allah) is specifically knowledge of Allah Himself—not knowledge of branches of law or other subjects. Then it cites Qur'anic proof: after Ibrahim presented his rational argument for the temporality of the world (based on the fact that the world constantly changes, so it must have a creator who is unchanging and free from events), Allah declared that this was His own argument given to Ibrahim, and that He raises in degrees those who are opened to recognizing the truth through rational proofs. Then Allah commanded the Prophet to follow Ibrahim's way (millah). The passage concludes by asserting that the Imams of the Sunni community are precisely those who followed this path, thus attaining the highest ranks from Allah. The prayer at the end expresses the hope that the reader be included among them. The overall argument is that rational theology (kalam) is not only permitted but the means to the highest spiritual station.

Key Terms
علم
خشية
حجة عقلية
ملة إبراهيم
براهين عقلية
أئمة السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any religious knowledge produces khashyah.
Correction: The passage specifies that only knowledge of Allah (His essence and attributes) necessarily entails khashyah, not knowledge of law or other subjects.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what kind of knowledge necessarily leads to khashyah?
A) Knowledge of Islamic law
B) Knowledge of Allah the Exalted
C) Knowledge of creation
D) Knowledge of the hereafter

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of Allah through rational proofs is the path of the prophets and the Imams of Sunnah, and it is the knowledge that truly produces fear of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do I truly fear Allah in a way that changes my daily choices, or is my 'fear' just a comfortable feeling that costs me nothing? Have I ever sat down to rationally know who Allah is, or do I rely on inherited beliefs without personal conviction?
?
When I recite the story of Ibrahim, do I see it as something that happened long ago, or do I feel the urgency to follow his method of thinking—questioning, reasoning, and arriving at certainty? What would it take for me to own my faith like he did?
?
The Imams of the Sunnah were raised in degrees because they followed Ibrahim's rational proofs. Am I content with my current level of knowledge, or do I long to be among those whom Allah opens the way to truth? What am I willing to sacrifice to attain that elevated station?

Why Knowing Allah Excels Knowing His Rulings
Sanusi argues for the superiority of those who know Allah's attributes over legal scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the knowers of Allah (al-ʿārifūn bi-llāh) are considered superior to legal scholars, based on the nobility of the known object and the fruits of that knowledge.

Core Idea
Knowledge is honored by the honor of its object; knowing Allah is the highest knowledge.

This passage from Sanusi's commentary presents a powerful argument for the supremacy of those who study the divine attributes over those who study legal rulings. Citing authorities like al-Ghazali and al-Qushayri, it culminates in 'Izz al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Salam's reasoning that the nobility of knowledge derives from its subject matter. As you read, notice how the argument moves from authority to logical principle to practical fruit.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and Translation
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing, then read the English translation. Let the flow of the argument sink in before analyzing details.
The passage begins with a citation and ends with a clear conclusion.
2
Identify the Authorities Cited
Notice that Sanusi first reports statements from al-Ghazali and al-Qushayri about the precedence of saints and knowers of Allah. This sets the stage for the main argument.
al-Ghazali is quoted as saying the secrets of divinity are only for prophets and saints.
3
Grasp the Core Principle
Focus on 'Izz al-Din's statement: 'knowledge is honored by the honor of the known.' This is the key logical premise. Ask yourself: why does the object of knowledge determine its value?
The object here is Allah, the most honorable being.
4
Apply the Principle to Two Kinds of Knowledge
Compare knowledge of Allah's attributes (necessary, impossible) with knowledge of His rulings (furūʿ and uṣūl). According to the principle, the former is more honorable because its object is more noble.
This is the direct application of the principle.
5
Consider the Practical Fruits
Notice how the passage describes the fruits: hope from knowing mercy, fear from knowing punishment, and that fear produces obedience. See how this shows the practical superiority of this knowledge.
The fruits are not just intellectual but transform behavior.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ تَفْضِيلُ الْعَارِفِينَ بِالْأُصُولِ عَلَى الْعَالِمِينَ بِالْفُرُوعِ ] وَقَدْ وَقَعَ فِي كَلَامِ الْغَزَالِيِّ : أَنَّ أَسْرَارَ الْإِلَهِيَّاتِ لَا يَسْتَقِلُّ بِهَا وَبِالْوُقُوفِ عَلَى طُرُقِ بَعْضِهَا إِلَّا الْأَنْبِيَاءُ وَالْأَوْلِيَاءُ . وَوَقَعَ فِي كَلَامِهِ تَقْدِيمُ الْأَوْلِيَاءِ عَلَى الْعُلَمَاءِ فِي مَعْرِفَةِ اللهِ تَعَالَى بَعْدَ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ . وَوَقَعَ نَحْوُهُ فِي رِسَالَةِ الْقُشَيْرِيِّ . وَسُئِلَ عَنْ ذَلِكَ عِزُّ الدِّينِ بْنُ عَبْدِ السَّلَامِ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى ، فَقَالَ : ( أَمَّا تَفْضِيلُ الْعَارِفِينَ بِاللهِ تَعَالَى عَلَى الْعَارِفِينَ بِأَحْكَامِ اللهِ تَعَالَى .. فَقَوْلُ الْأَسْتَاذِ وَالْغَزَالِيِّ فِيهِ مُتَّفَقٌ ; لِأَنَّ الْعَارِفِينَ بِمَا يَجِبُ للهِ تَعَالَى مِنْ أَوْصَافِ الْكَمَالِ ، وَبِمَا يَسْتَحِيلُ عَلَيْهِ مِنَ النُّقْصَانِ.. أَفْضَلُ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْفُرُوعِ وَالْأُصُولِ ; لِأَنَّ الْعِلْمَ يَشْرُفُ بِشَرَفِ الْمَعْلُومِ ، وَالْعِلْمُ بِاللهِ تَعَالَى وَصِفَاتِهِ أَشْرَفُ ; لِأَنَّ مَعْلُومَهُ أَشْرَفُ الْمَعْلُومَاتِ ، وَثَمَرَتَهُ أَفْضَلُ الثَّمَرَاتِ . فَمَنْ عَرَفَ سَعَةَ رَحْمَةِ اللهِ تَعَالَى أَثْمَرَتْ مَعْرِفَتُهُ سَعَةَ الرَّجَاءِ ، وَمَنْ عَرَفَ شِدَّةَ النِّقْمَةِ أَثْمَرَتْ مَعْرِفَتُهُ شِدَّةَ الْخَوْفِ ، وَأَثْمَرَ خَوْفُهُ الْكَفَّ عَنِ الْفُسُوقِ وَالْعِصْيَانِ ، مَعَ الْبُكَاءِ وَالْأَحْزَانِ ، وَالْوَرَعِ وَالْإِذْعَانِ .
[The preference of those who know the fundamentals over those who know the branches] And it occurred in the speech of al-Ghazali: that the secrets of the divine matters are not independently known, nor the access to some of their ways, except by prophets and saints. And it occurred in his speech: the precedence of saints over scholars in knowledge of Allah the Exalted after the prophets. And similar occurred in al-Qushayri's Treatise. And 'Izz al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Salam, may Allah have mercy on him, was asked about that, so he said: 'As for preferring those who know Allah the Exalted over those who know Allah's rulings... the opinion of the master and al-Ghazali agrees on it; because those who know what is necessary for Allah of attributes of perfection, and what is impossible for Him of deficiency... are better than those of the branches and the fundamentals; because knowledge is honored by the honor of the known, and knowledge of Allah the Exalted and His attributes is more honorable; because its known object is the most honorable of known things, and its fruit is the best of fruits. So whoever knows the extent of Allah's mercy, his knowledge produces breadth of hope; and whoever knows the severity of punishment, his knowledge produces intensity of fear; and his fear produces restraint from immorality and disobedience, along with weeping, sorrows, scrupulousness, and submission.'
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a classification and argument for the superiority of those who know Allah's essence and attributes (the 'arifeen bi'llah) over those who know only the branches (fur') or even the fundamentals (usul) of law. It begins by citing al-Ghazali's statement that only prophets and saints can independently access the secrets of divine matters, and that saints are ranked above scholars in knowledge of Allah after the prophets. It also cites al-Qushayri's similar view. Then it presents the response of 'Izz al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Salam, who affirms that the knowers of Allah are unanimously recognized as superior. His reason has two parts: (1) knowledge derives its honor from the nobility of its object; since the object here is Allah Himself—who possesses all perfection and is free from deficiency—that knowledge is the most noble. (2) The fruit of this knowledge is the best: knowledge of Allah's mercy produces hope, knowledge of His punishment produces fear, and that fear leads to practical obedience (restraint from sin, weeping, scrupulousness, and submission). Thus the passage justifies the primacy of kalam over other sciences.

Key Terms
تفضيل
عارف
غزالي
قديري
عز الدين بن عبد السلام
شرف المعلوم
ثمرة العلم
رجاء
خوف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many believe that scholars of Islamic law (fuqahāʾ) are the highest rank among Muslims, surpassing those who merely study theology.
Correction: This passage argues that those who know Allah's attributes (the ʿārifūn) are superior because their knowledge has a nobler object and produces the best fruits, including hope, fear, and righteous action.

Checkpoint
Why does 'Izz al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Salam consider those who know Allah superior to those who know His rulings?
A) Because they are more pious
B) Because knowledge is honored by the honor of its object
C) Because they perform more acts of worship
D) Because they have more miracles

Key Takeaway
The honor of knowledge comes from its object; therefore, knowledge of Allah's attributes is the most honorable, producing the best fruits in the believer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You spend hours learning fiqh and usul, but how much time do you dedicate to directly knowing Allah's attributes—His perfection, His mercy, His severity? If you were to die today, would your knowledge of Allah produce hope or fear in your heart?
?
When you sin, do you feel a genuine fear of Allah's punishment that restrains you, or do you rely on knowing the legal ruling without internalizing the majesty of the One you disobey? What would it take for your knowledge to transform into weeping and submission?
?
If knowledge is honored by its object, what does the content of your study say about your priorities? Are you seeking the most honorable knowledge, or are you content with lesser branches? How will you change your pursuit starting today?

The Sacred Foundation of Tawhid
States that only the spiritually blind disparage the science of Tawhid, as it is based on the Quran and Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that disparaging the science of Tawhid is equivalent to disparaging the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus of the Muslim community.

Core Idea
To attack the science of Tawhid is to attack revelation itself.

Sanusi begins by addressing a common objection: that the science of kalam is a human innovation and therefore open to criticism. He declares that only those whose hearts are blinded by Allah would denigrate this science, because it is derived directly from the Quran and Sunnah. The passage establishes the sacred foundation of Tawhid as a discipline and warns that rejecting it means rejecting the core sources of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the strong language used by Sanusi.
Notice the repetition of 'blinding'.
2
Understand the logical progression
Identify the three parts: (1) who disparages, (2) what that implies, (3) the consequence.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why the author equates criticism of tawhid with criticism of the primary sources. How does this defend the science?
This is a defense of kalam as a legitimate Islamic discipline.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يذم علم التوحيدِ إِلا مَنْ أعمى الله قلبَهُ . ولا خفاءَ : أنَّ القادحَ في هذا العلم قادح في الكتاب والسنَّةِ وما اجتمعَتْ عليه الأمَّةُ، لكنْ مَنْ أعمى الله تعالى بصيرتهُ فلن تملك لهُ مِنَ الله شيئاً.
Only one whose heart Allah has blinded disparages the science of Tawhid. And it is no secret: that the critic of this science is a critic of the Book, the Sunnah, and that upon which the community has agreed. But whomever Allah Almighty has blinded his insight, you will not possess for him anything from Allah.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This is a short but powerful statement. The author declares that any attack on the science of tawhid (ilm al-tawhid) is essentially an attack on the Quran and Sunnah and the consensus of the ummah, because this science is derived from them. He then consoles that whoever is blinded by Allah cannot be guided by you.

Key Terms

القادح
الكتاب
السنَّة
الأمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Criticism of kalam is permissible because it is a human science.
Correction: The author argues that kalam is inseparable from revelation; thus, criticizing it is criticizing the Quran and Sunnah.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does it mean to disparage the science of Tawhid?
A) It is a valid intellectual exercise.
B) It is a criticism of the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus.
C) It is permissible if done politely.
D) It only affects the scholars who teach it.

Key Takeaway
Disparaging the science of Tawhid is not a minor criticism; it is an attack on the very foundations of Islamic belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone dismiss the study of Tawhid as irrelevant or divisive, do you see it as a mere opinion, or as a spiritual condition? Will you now pray for their guidance rather than simply argue?
?

?
The passage says that those blinded by Allah cannot be helped by you. Are you willing to accept that there are people you cannot convince, and instead focus your energy on those who are seeking the truth?

The Defense of Tawhid Against Its Critics
Refutation of those who disparage the study of tawhid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author considers criticism of tawhid to be tantamount to criticism of the foundational Islamic sources.

Core Idea
Criticizing tawhid is criticizing the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus.

This passage is a defense of the science of tawhid against those who belittle it. The author does not simply rebuke such critics; he demonstrates the logical equivalency between rejecting tawhid and rejecting the primary sources of Islamic law and belief. Let's read the passage carefully.

Guided Path

3
Understand the logical chain

4
Reflect on the final warning

Key Takeaway
